    曾序
    近时钱塘瞿氏，著《剪灯新话》，率皆新奇希异之事，人多喜传而乐道之，由是其说盛行于世。余友广西布政李君昌祺，于旅寓之次，取近代之事得于见闻者，汇为一帙，名之曰《剪灯余话》。余得而观之，初未暇详也。一夕，燃巨烛翻阅，达旦不寐，尽得其事之始终，言之次第，甚习也。一日，退食，辄与同列语之。则皆喜且愕曰：“迩日必得奇书也，何所言之事神异若此耶？”既而昌祺以属余序。夫圣贤之大经大法，载之于书者，盖已家传人诵。有不可思议，有足以广材识、资谈论者，亦所不废。昌祺学博才高，其文思之敏赡，不啻泉之涌而山之积也。故其所著，秾丽丰蔚，文采烂然。读之者莫不为之喜见须眉，而欣然不厌也。又何其快哉！昌祺于余为姻家，且有同年之好。因观是编之作，遂为之序焉。

    Explanation

    The Tale of Flowers and Candles in the Fairyland

    Volume Five
    The Tale of Jia Yunhua's Return from the Dead

    Preface by Zeng
    Recently, the Qu family of Qiantang wrote The Tales of the Lanterns, which is filled with new and strange stories. People enjoy passing them on and discussing them, and thus the tales became widely popular. My friend Li Changqi, the governor of Guangxi, compiled recent events he had heard or witnessed into a collection and named it The Tales of the Lanterns Left Behind. I read it and initially did not have the time to examine it in detail. One night, I lit a large candle and read through the entire book, staying awake until dawn. I understood the entire narrative and its sequence, and it was quite familiar. One day, after finishing my meal, I discussed it with my colleagues. They were all delighted and surprised, saying, "You must have found a remarkable book! What stories are so extraordinary?" Li Changqi then asked me to write a preface for it. The great principles and teachings of the sages are already well-known and widely recited in books. Some are beyond comprehension, while others broaden one's knowledge and provide material for discussion, and these are not to be neglected. Li Changqi is highly learned and talented, with a mind that flows like a spring and accumulates like a mountain. Therefore, his writings are rich, beautiful, and adorned with brilliant language. Readers are all delighted to see the characters come to life and are never tired of reading them. How delightful it is! Li Changqi is related to me by marriage, and we share the bond of having passed the same imperial examination. Because I have read this collection, I have written this preface for it.

    3

    永乐庚子春闰正月下浣，翰林侍读学士奉训大夫兼修国史永丰曾棨书。

    王英序
    余读庐陵李君昌祺所著《剪灯余话》，所载皆幽冥人物灵异之事。窃喜昌祺之博闻广见，才高识伟，而文词制作之工且丽也。或有诘余者曰：“某事幽昧恍惚，君子所未信，子何为而喜耶？”余曰：“不然！经以载道，史以纪事。其他有诸子焉，托词比事，纷纷藉藉，著为之书。又有百家之说焉，以志载古昔遗事，与时之丛谈、诙语、神怪之说，并传于世。是非得失，固有不同，然亦岂无所可取者哉！在审择之而已。是故言之泛溢无据者置之。事核而其言不诬，有关于世教者录之。余于是编，盖亦有所取也。

    Explanation

    3

    In the spring of Yongle Gengzi, during the intercalary month of the lower half of the first month, the Hanlin Academy scholar-official, the Imperial Tutor, and the Doctor of Instruction, who was also tasked with compiling national history, from Yongfeng, wrote this.

    Wang Ying's Preface
    I have read The Remaining Tales of the Lantern by Li Changqi of Luzhou, which contains stories of supernatural beings and mystical events. I secretly admire Changqi's extensive knowledge and wide experience, his great talent and profound insight, as well as the skill and beauty of his literary works. Someone asked me, "Certain things are mysterious and vague, and gentlemen do not believe them. Why are you pleased with them?" I replied, "Not so! The classics carry the Way, and history records events. There are also the various schools of thought, who use words to compare events, creating a multitude of writings. There are also the diverse traditions of Chinese thought, which record ancient and forgotten events, along with contemporary miscellaneous discussions, witty remarks, and stories of the supernatural. These have varying merits and demerits, but are there not some valuable aspects to them? It lies in careful selection alone. Therefore, discard those who speak excessively without evidence. If the facts are verified and the words are not false, and they are relevant to the world and education, then record them. In this collection, there are indeed some valuable things."

    4

    其间所述，若唐诸王之骄淫，谭妇之死节，赵鸾、琼奴之守义，使人读之，有所惩劝。至于他篇之作，措词命意，开阖抑扬，亦多有可取者，此余之所以喜也。抑岂不闻之，昔者王充之著论，叹赏于蔡邕；张华之博洽，称美于阮籍；而干宝之撰记，见称于刘恢乎？操觚执翰，以著述为任者，人之所难能也。古之人盖重之，余何敢不企慕古人，而无所取于斯耶？”于是诘者乃退。因书以序其端，俾世之士皆知昌祺才识之广，而勿讶其所著之为异也。昌祺所作之诗词甚多，此特其游戏耳。初为礼部郎中，今仕为广西左布政使，盖与余为同年进士云。

    Explanation

    4

    What is described herein, such as the arrogance and licentiousness of the Tang princes, the loyal death of a woman named Tan, and the adherence to righteousness by Zhao Luan and Qiong Nu, serves to make readers learn from and be encouraged by it. As for the other works, their choice of words and themes, their opening and closing, their ups and downs, are also very commendable, which is why I am pleased. Have you not heard of this? In the past, Wang Chong wrote his treatise, which was praised by Cai Yong; Zhang Hua's extensive knowledge was praised by Ruan Ji; and Gan Bao's compilation was praised by Liu Hui. Those who wield the brush and take writing as their duty are something difficult for people to achieve. Ancient people highly valued it, so how dare I not aspire to the ancients and not find value in this? Thus, the questioner withdrew. Therefore, I write this preface to introduce the beginning, so that scholars of the world may know the breadth of Chang Qi's talents and knowledge, and not be surprised by the uniqueness of his writings. Chang Qi has written many poems and lyrics, but these are merely his play. Initially, he served as a Langzhong in the Ministry of Rites, and now he holds the position of Left Censor-in-Chief of Guangxi. He and I are fellow Jinshi graduates.

    5

    罗汝敬序
    《剪灯余话》凡四卷，计二十篇，广西布政使昌祺李公继钱塘瞿氏之作也。公尝以明经擢高第，又尝以名进士纂修中秘书。其雄辩博洽，盖有素矣。故其发为文章，昭诸翰墨，皆足以广心志，扩见闻，而资益学识，往往搜奇剔异，详书而备录之，亦岂无意乎！而或者乃谓所载多神异，吾儒所未信。余曰：“不然！夫圣经贤传之垂宪立范，以维持世道者，固不可尚矣。其稗官、小说、卜筮、农圃，与凡捭阖笼罩，纵横术数之书，亦莫不有裨于时。

    Explanation

    5

    Preface by Luo Rujing
    The Tales Told by the Lantern consists of four volumes, totaling twenty chapters, and is the work of Mr. Li Changqi, the Governor of Guangxi, who succeeded the compiler from Qiantang, Qiu. Mr. Li once passed the Mingjing examination and was promoted to a high rank, and he also served as a famous Jinshi who compiled and edited the central secret archives. He is eloquent and well-versed, qualities that he has possessed from the beginning. Therefore, his writings, which are recorded in writing, are sufficient to broaden one's heart and mind, expand one's knowledge, and enrich one's learning. Often, he searches for and highlights the strange and unusual, writing in detail and recording comprehensively. This is not done without purpose! However, some say that the content contains many supernatural elements, which Confucians do not believe. I say that this is not so! The sacred scriptures and the teachings of the wise, which set examples and establish norms, are essential for maintaining social order. Even minor works, short stories, divination, and agriculture, as well as books on strategy, diplomacy, and divination, all have value in the times.

    6

    矧兹所记，若饼师妇之贞，谭氏妇之节，何思明之廉介，吉复卿之交谊，贾、祖两女之雅操，真、文二生之俊杰识时，举有关于风化，而足为世劝者。彼其《齐谐》之记，《幽冥》之录，《搜神》《夷坚》之志述，务为荒唐虚幻者，岂得一经于言议哉？若布政公之所记，征诸事则有验，揆诸理则不诬，政人人所乐道，而吾党所喜闻者也，神异云乎哉！且余闻之：昌黎韩公传《毛颖》《革华》，先正谓其‘珍果中之查梨’，特以备品味尔。余于是编亦云。”或者唯唯。因次第之于简末，庶资薇垣高议之一噱焉。

    Explanation

    6

    Let alone what is recorded here, such as the chastity of the wife of the baker, the propriety of Tan's wife, the honesty and uprightness of He Siming, the friendship of Ji Fuxing, the elegant conduct of the two daughters of Jia and Zu, and the wisdom and insight of the two young men of Zhen and Wen—these all concern moral influence and are worthy of being examples for the world. Those records in the Qi Hua (Strange Tales), the Yi Ming (Records of the Underworld), the Soushen Ji (Records of the Supernatural), and the Yijian Zhi (Records of the Unusual) that are filled with absurd and fantastical tales, how could they be taken seriously in discussions? As for the records of the local official, they are verified by events and consistent with reason, and they are what everyone enjoys talking about and what our group enjoys hearing. Is it a matter of the supernatural? I have also heard that Han Yu of Changli wrote Mao Ying (The Biography of Mao Ying) and Ge Hua (The Biography of Ge Hua), and the respected scholars of the past described them as "among the precious fruits, the pear and the apple," merely to provide variety in taste. This compilation is also like that." Someone agreed. Therefore, I arranged it at the end of the scroll, perhaps to provide a laugh for the high-minded discussions of the officials.

    7

    永乐十八年正月朔吉，翰林修撰行在工部右侍郎同年友罗汝敬书。

    作者自序
    往年余董役长干寺，获见睦人桂衡所制《柔柔传》。爱其才思俊逸，意婉词工，因述《还魂记》拟之。后七年，又役房山，客有以钱塘瞿氏《剪灯新话》贻余者。复爱之，锐欲效颦。虽奔走埃氛，心志荒落，然犹技痒弗已。受事之暇，捃摭 闻，次为二十篇，名曰《剪灯余话》，仍取《还魂记》续于篇末。以其成于羁旅，出于记忆，无书籍质证，虑多抵牾，不敢示人。既释徽纆，寓顺城门客舍，学士曾公子棨过余，偶见焉。乃抚掌曰：“兹所谓以文为戏者非耶？”辄冠以叙，称其秾丽丰蔚，文采烂然。由是稍稍人知，竞求抄录，亟欲焚去以绝迹。而索者踵至，势不容拒矣。

    Explanation

    7

    In the first month of the year of Yongle's eighteenth year, on the first day of the month, auspicious, Huanlin Xiu Zhuan, Right Minister of the Ministry of Works at the Imperial Residence, friend of the same year, Luo Rujing, writes.

    Author's Preface
    In the past, when I was in charge of the construction of Changgan Temple, I had the opportunity to read the work "Rou Rou's Biography" by Guibin Gui. I admired his elegant and graceful thoughts, his gentle meaning, and his skillful words. Inspired by this, I wrote "The Return of the Soul" as a model for it. Seven years later, while working in Fangshan, a guest presented me with the collection "New Tales of the Lamp by Qu of Qiantang." I was again captivated by it and eagerly wanted to imitate it. Although I was busy with worldly affairs, my heart and mind were somewhat distracted, yet I still felt an urge to write. In my spare time, I gathered and collected hearsay, arranging it into twenty pieces, naming it "Tales of the Lamp: The Leftovers," and still included "The Return of the Soul" at the end. Because it was written while traveling away from home, based on memory, without books to verify, I feared many contradictions and did not dare to show it to others. After being released from my bonds, I stayed at a guesthouse near Shuncheng Gate. Scholar Zeng Gongzi Qi visited me, and he happened to see it. He clapped his hands and said, "Is this not what is called writing for amusement?" He then pre

    8

    因思在昔圣人谓：“饱食终日，无所用心。不有博弈者乎？为之犹贤乎已！”矧余两涉忧患，饱食之日少，且性不好博弈，非藉楮墨吟弄，则何以豁怀抱，宣郁闷乎？虽知其近于滑稽谐谑，而不遑恤者，亦犹疾痛之不免于呻吟耳，庸何讳哉？虽然，《高唐》《洛神》，意在言外，皆闲暇时作，宜其考事精详，修辞缛丽，千载之下，脍炙人口；若余者，则负谴无聊，姑假此以自遣，初非平居有意为之，以取讥大雅，较诸饱食、博弈，或者其庶乎？遂不复焚，而并识其造作之由于编末，俾时自省览，以毋忘前日之虞，而保其终吉。好事者观之，可以一笑而已，又何必泥其事之有无也哉？

    永乐庚子夏五初吉，庐陵李祯昌祺甫叙

    Explanation

    8

    Thinking back to what the ancient sage said: "To eat one's fill all day long without using one's mind. Isn't there something like playing games? Doing that is still better than nothing!" Especially since I have experienced two periods of hardship, and the days of eating my fill are few. Moreover, I have no inclination for games, and instead rely on paper and ink to write and compose poetry. How else can I open up my heart and express my inner frustrations? Although I know that this is close to being humorous and playful, but I cannot worry about that, just as one cannot help but groan when in pain. Why should I be ashamed? Although, in Gao Tang and Luo Shen, the meaning lies beyond the words. They were all written during leisure time, so they are naturally detailed and beautifully crafted, and even a thousand years later, they are still widely praised. As for me, I am burdened with guilt and have nothing better to do, so I use this as a way to distract myself. I did not do this intentionally in my daily life to invite criticism from the refined. Compared to eating one's fill and playing games, perhaps this is closer? So I did not burn it, but instead recorded the reason for its creation at the end of the book, so that I can reflect on it from time to time, to never forget the worries of the past, and to ensure a good ending. Those who enjoy such things can laugh at it, but why should they take it too seriously? In the first day of the fifth month of the Gengzi year of Yongle, by Li Zhen, courtesy name Changqi, from Luling.

    9

    长安夜行录

    洪武初，汤公铭之与文公原吉，俱以老成练达，学问渊源，政事文章，推重当代。未几而秦邸之国。汤公拜右辅，文公拜左辅，随从以行。时天下太平，人物繁庶，关中又汉、唐故都，遗迹俱在。二公导翊之暇，惟从容于诗酒中，临眺于山川，访古寻幽，未尝相舍。一日，文公谓汤公曰：“汉代诸陵，尽在于此。吾徒幸无案牍之劳，且有休退之日，登高能赋，此其时乎？”府僚洛阳巫马期仁对曰：“长陵、安陵、阳陵、平陵，皆在渭北咸阳原上，高十二丈，百二十七步。惟茂陵在兴平县东北十七里，高十四丈，百四十步，其形方正，状类覆斗。陵东为卫将军青墓。又稍东为霍去病墓，所谓象祁连山者。西北，为公孙弘墓。西一里为李夫人墓。山川雄秀，与他处异。公若欲游，宜先于是。且兴平去此十八里，一日可到。”二公然之。翌日遂往，期仁从焉，时九月二十日也。暨归，至半途，期仁马乏，追公不及。因缓辔徐行，不觉暝矣。

    Explanation

    9

    Night Journey to Chang'an

    At the beginning of the Hongwu era, Master Tang Mingzhi and Master Wen Yuanji were both highly esteemed for their experience, learning, and contributions to governance and literature. Soon after, the Prince of Qin was established in his fiefdom. Master Tang was appointed as the Right Chancellor, and Master Wen as the Left Chancellor, and they accompanied him on his journey. At that time, the world was at peace, and the population was thriving. Chang'an, being the former capital of the Han and Tang dynasties, was filled with historical sites. In their spare time, the two officials would only relax in poetry and wine, gaze upon the mountains and rivers, visit ancient sites, and explore secluded places, never parting from each other. One day, Master Wen said to Master Tang, "All the Han dynasty tombs are here. We are fortunate to have no burdensome paperwork, and we will soon retire. It is the perfect time to compose poetry while enjoying the scenery." The official from Luoyang, Master Wu Qiren, replied, "The Long Mausoleum, An Mausoleum, Yang Mausoleum, and Ping Mausoleum are all on the northern slope of Xianyang, twelve zhang high and one hundred twenty-seven bu wide. The Mao Mausoleum is located seventeen li northeast of Xingping County, fourteen zhang high and one hundred forty bu wide, with a square and upright shape resembling an overturned斗. To the east of the mausoleum is the tomb of General Wei Qing. Slightly to the east is the tomb of Huo Qubing, which is said to resemble Mount Qilian. To the northwest is the tomb of Gong Sun Hong, and one li to the west is the tomb of Lady Li. The mountains and rivers here are majestic and beautiful, different from other places. If you wish to visit, you should start here. Moreover, Xingping is eighteen li away, and it can be reached in one day." The two officials agreed. The next day, they set out, accompanied by Master Wu, on the 20th day of the ninth month. Upon returning, they reached the halfway point, and Master Wu's horse was exhausted, and he could not catch up. So, he slowed down and walked slowly, unaware that it had become dark.

    10

    路遥天黑，将近二更，禽鸟飞鸣，狐兔充斥。心甚恐，且畏且行。俄而望中隐隐有火光，意谓人家不远。策马以进，至则果民舍也。双户洞开，灯犹未灭。期仁下马，拴于庭树之上。入坐客次，良久寂然，不敢叩门。惟屡謦咳，使其家知之。少顷，苍头自便户出，问客何来。期仁以实告，苍头唯唯而去。未几，主人出，乃一少年，韦布翛然，状貌温粹。揖客与语，言辞简当，问劳而已。茶罢，延入中堂，规制幽雅可爱，花卉芬芳，几席雅洁。坐定，少年呼其妻出拜。视之，国色也，年二十余，靓妆常服，不屑朱铅，往来于香烟烛影中，绰约若仙姝神女。期仁私念彼寻常人，而妻美若此，必怪也。亦不敢问。

    Explanation

    10

    The road was long and dark, nearing the second watch of the night, as birds flew and called, and foxes and rabbits were abundant. Filled with great fear, he moved forward cautiously. Suddenly, he saw a faint light in the distance, thinking that a human settlement was not far away. Urging his horse forward, he arrived to find that it was indeed a civilian house. The double doors were wide open, and the lights were still burning. Period Ren dismounted and tied his horse to a tree in the courtyard. Entering and sitting in the guest area, he remained in silence for a long time, hesitant to knock on the door. He coughed repeatedly to make himself known. Shortly after, a servant appeared from the side door and asked where the guest had come from. Period Ren told the truth, and the servant nodded and left. Not long after, the host appeared, a young man dressed casually with a gentle and refined appearance. He greeted the guest and spoke in simple and appropriate terms, asking about the guest's well-being. After tea, he invited the guest into the main hall, which was elegantly and charmingly laid out. The flowers were fragrant, and the tables and seats were clean and elegant. Seated, the young man called his wife to greet the guest. She was exceptionally beautiful, in her twenties, dressed in everyday attire, and did not use makeup. Her graceful movements in the light of incense and candles resembled those of a fairy or goddess. Period Ren privately thought it strange that an ordinary person could have such a beautiful wife, but he was too shy to ask.

    11

    逡巡，设酒馔，杯豆罗列，虽不甚丰腆，而奇美精致，迨非人间饮食。少年相劝，意甚殷勤。酒半，夫妻俱起拜曰：“公贵人，前程远大。某有少恳，欲托公以白于世。”期仁曰：“子夫妇为谁？所恳者何事？”少年曰：“公无恐，当以诚告。某唐人，处此已七百余年，未尝有至此者。今公临降，殆天意欤？某白于世，必矣。”期仁曰：“愿卒闻之。”少年羞赧低回，欲说复止。其妻曰：“何害！我则言之。妾夫开元间长安鬻饼师也，让皇帝为宁王时，建第兴庆坊，吾家适近王邸。妾夫故儒者，知有安、史之祸，隐于饼以自晦。妾亦躬操井臼，涤器当垆，不敢以为耻也。王过，见而悦之，妾夫不能庇其伉俪，遂为所夺。从入邸中，妾即以死自誓，终日不食，竟日不言。王使人开谕百端，莫之顾也。一夕，召妾，托以程姬之疾，获免。如此者月余，王无奈何，叱遣归家。

    Explanation

    11

    After a moment of hesitation, they set out the food and drink, with bowls and beans arranged neatly. Though the table was not overly lavish, the food was strangely beautiful and exquisitely crafted, definitely not of earthly origin. The young men encouraged each other, showing sincere and earnest enthusiasm. When the wine was half gone, the couple both rose to bow and said, "You are a noble person, with a bright future ahead. I have a small request, and I wish to entrust you to convey it to the world." Period Ren replied, "Who are you, and what is your request?" The young man said, "Do not be afraid, I will speak honestly. I am from the Tang dynasty, and I have been here for over seven hundred years. I have never had anyone come here before. Now you have descended upon us, is it perhaps the will of heaven? I will certainly make my request known to the world." Period Ren said, "I wish to hear it all." The young man blushed and hesitated, wanting to speak but then stopping. His wife said, "What harm is there! I will speak for you. My husband was a baker in Chang'an during the reign of Emperor Xuanzong. When Prince Ning, the future Emperor Xuanzong, built his residence in Xingqing坊, our home happened to be near the prince's residence. My husband was a scholar who knew of the An Lushan Rebellion, so he hid by selling baked goods to avoid notice. I also personally handled the household chores, cleaned utensils, and served as a shopkeeper, not considering it a disgrace. One day, the prince passed by and saw me, and he liked me. My husband could not protect our marriage, so I was taken by him. I followed into the prince's residence, and I vowed to die, remaining silent all day. The prince tried to persuade me in many ways, but I paid no heed. One night, he summoned me, pretending I was ill like Cheng Ji, and I was spared. Like this for over a month, the prince had no choice but to order me to return home.

    12

    当时史官既失妾夫妇姓名，不复登载，惟《本事集》云：‘唐宁王宅畔，有卖饼者妻美，王取之经岁，问曰：颇忆饼师否？召之使见，泪下如雨，王悯而还之。’殊不知妾入王宫中，首尾只一月，而谓经岁；妾求死而得出，而谓召之使见；王实未尝问妾，亦未尝召妾夫至也；厚诬若此，何以堪之？而世之骚人墨客有赋《饼师妇吟》咏妾事者，亦皆逞其才思，过于形容，至有句云：‘当时夫婿轻一诺，金屋茆檐两迢递。

    Explanation

    12

    At the time, the historian failed to record the names of the woman and her husband, and thus their names were not documented. Only in The Collection of True Events is it said that: "At the side of Prince Ning's residence in the Tang Dynasty, there was a beautiful wife of a baker, whom the prince took for a year. He asked, 'Do you miss your baker husband?' He summoned him to see her, and she wept like rain; the prince felt pity and returned her." Unaware that I was in the prince's palace for only a month, yet it was said to be a year; I sought death to escape, but it was said that he summoned me to see her; the prince never asked me, nor did he ever summon my husband. To be so grossly slandered, how can I bear it? And in the world, poets and literati have composed The Baker's Wife's Lament about my story, all displaying their talents and exaggerating the description, with lines that say, "At that time, my husband lightly gave his word, the golden house and the thatched cottage are far apart."

    13

    ’呜呼！回思尔时，事出迫夺，薰天之势，妾夫尚敢喘息耶？今以轻一诺为妾夫罪，岂不冤哉？所谓有恳托公者，此也。”期仁曰：“若尔守义，实为可嘉。正须直笔，以励风俗，而使之昧昧无闻，安得不饮恨于九原，抱痛于百世哉？期仁不敏，滥以文辞称，当为子表而出之。但恐相传已久，胶于见闻，一旦厘正，不免人疑。愿得子姓字，以补史氏之缺，可乎？”少年愀然不乐，曰：“若显余姓名人间，则负愧愈无尽矣，非所愿也。”期仁曰：“然则如之何？”少年曰：“乞以前所云者，辩正足矣。”

    Explanation

    13

    Alas! Reflecting back on that time, the matter arose from coercion, under the overwhelming power of the tyrannical force, could my husband dare to breathe? Now, to be faulted for my husband's light promise, is it not unjust? The matter I entrust to you is this.” Period Ren said, “If you adhere to your principles, it is truly commendable. It is necessary to write honestly to encourage good customs, and to let it remain unknown, how could one not drink hatred in the underworld and bear pain for a hundred generations? Period Ren is not wise, to be praised for my writing, I will write it out for you. But I fear that if it has been passed down for a long time and people are stuck in their perceptions, if corrected at once, people will inevitably doubt. I wish to know your name, to fill the gap in historical records, is it acceptable?” The young man looked solemn and unhappy, saying, “If my name is revealed to the world, the guilt and shame will be endless, it is not what I desire.” Period Ren said, “Then what should be done?” The young man said, “I ask that the previous statement be corrected, that is enough.”

    14

    期仁复问曰：“史称宁王，明炳机先，固让储副，号称宗英，乃亦为是不道耶？”少年曰：“此是其常态，尚足怪乎？然在当时诸王中，最为读书好学。虽其负恃恩宠，昧于自见；然见余拙妇以礼自持，终不忍犯。其他宗室所为，犹不足道。若岐王进膳，不设几案，令诸妓各捧一器，品尝之。申王遇冷不向火，置两手于妓怀中，须臾间易数人。薛王则刻木为美人，衣之青衣。夜宴则设以执烛，女乐纷纭，歌舞杂遝。其烛又特异，客欲作狂，辄暗如漆，事毕复明，不知其何术也？如此之类，难以悉举，无非穷极奢淫，灭弃礼法。设若堕其手中，宁复得出？则王之贤又不可不知也。”

    酒罢，夫妇各赠一诗。其夫诗云：

    少年十五十六时，
    隐身下混屠贩儿。
    乍可无营坐晦迹，
    不说有学行求知。
    四时活计看垆鏊，
    八节欢情对酒卮。

    Explanation

    14

    Period Ren asked, "Historians say that Prince Ning was shrewd in anticipating events, firmly declined the position of heir apparent, and was called the pride of the royal family. Yet, he also engaged in such immoral behavior, is this surprising?" The young man replied, "This is his usual behavior, is there anything to be surprised about? However, among the princes of that time, he was the most studious and learned. Although he relied on his favored status and failed to recognize his own faults; yet, seeing my humble wife maintain herself with propriety, he ultimately could not bring himself to offend. The actions of the other members of the royal family are not worth mentioning. For example, Prince Qi did not set up tables when he had his meals, having the courtesans each hold a dish for him to taste. Prince Shen did not warm himself by the fire when it was cold, placing his hands in the bosoms of the courtesans and changing courtesans frequently. Prince Xue carved wooden statues of beautiful women, dressing them in green robes. At night feasts, he had them hold candles, with numerous women musicians and chaotic music and dancing. The candles were especially peculiar; when guests wanted to get drunk, they would suddenly go out like ink, and they would light up again after the event, and no one knew the trick behind it. Such examples are too numerous to list, all were examples of extreme luxury and debauchery, disregarding proper etiquette and law. If one fell into their hands, there would be no escape. Thus, it is important to know about the king's virtues."

    After the wine was finished, the couple exchanged poems. The husband's poem said:

    When I was fifteen or sixteen,
    I hid among the butchers and vendors.
    It was better to have no ambitions and remain obscure,
    Than to speak of learning and seeking knowledge.
    Throughout the year, I watched the stove and the pan,
    At every festival, I enjoyed the wine.
    Purple sugar was poured, dripping like milk,

    15

    白面新和软截脂。
    大堪纳吉团遮筥，

    妾家阀阈本寻常，

    15

    The newly made white, smooth, and delicate pastry.
    Greatly suitable for auspicious round baskets,
    Small enough to fill a dish in circular layers.
    Emerging from fire without any loss or damage,
    Held aloft by slender hands like the sun and moon.
    In times of hardship, a Han dynasty noble once sold his prized possessions,
    Now I blend in and hide myself.
    A woman in the household shares the same sentiments,
    A scholarly figure upholds high moral standards.
    Since our marriage, we have shared the same hardships,
    Always able to present a tray with humble vegetables.
    Harmonious couples are truly hard to maintain,
    Plain clothes and simple hairpins are still pleasing to someone.

    Like the man who died of grief, my heart was severed in the night.

    The sword was suddenly able to reunite,
    The overflowing river can indeed be reclaimed.

    Her wife's poem says:

    My family's gate is but ordinary,
    A thatched house with a simple gate and walls.
    Hard work leaves no time for adornment,
    Gentle and compliant, I only know to follow the rites.
    Last year, I married a learned neighbor,
    Well-versed in the classics and histories.
    I did not seek fame or fortune,
    Rather, I was content to sell baked goods and live among the common folk.
    Every day, as the sun rises, the shop door opens,
    Children and monks come and go in a crowd.
    Once money is earned, I close the door,
    We sit close together, drinking from the same cup.
    Who would have thought we would part like Han Peng,
    Determined to leap into the water or leap from the tower.

    A white jade returned remains unblemished.

    16

    当代豪华久已亡，
    贞魂万古抱悲伤。
    烦公一扫荒唐论，
    为传梁鸿与孟光。
    期仁玩之再四，
    收拾囊中。少年即命苍头导客东厅就榻。

    斯须，远寺钟敲，近村鸡唱，曙色熹微，晨光晻霭。开目视之，但见身沾露以犹湿，马龁草而未休。四顾阒然，咸无所睹。乃以诗呈二公，皆加赏异，以为真得唐体。命刻之郡东，以永其传。期仁果以文学升至翰苑，八十九而终，遂符远大之说。汤公后守吉安，屡为人道其详如此云。

    听经猿记
    庐陵之属邑吉水，有东山焉，根盘百里，作镇一方。秀丽清奇，望之如画。后唐天成间，有修禅师者，结草庵于山之绝处。树木蒙密，路径崎岖。旷岁弥年，人迹罕至。惟樵夫深入时，见师坐松下，辄有群鸟衔果集于前，师一一取食。食讫，飞去。樵夫间以语人，好事者相率造庵访之。师方鼾睡，朴握暖足，伊尼卫床。众异之，竞为除地集材，建大兰若。兴工之始，师召匠戒之曰：“汝手作人，必饮酒食肉。

    Explanation

    16

    The opulence of the contemporary era has long since perished,
    The pure soul has held sorrow for all eternity.
    Please sweep away the absurd theories,
    To transmit the story of Liang Hong and Meng Guang.
    Qi Ren played with it repeatedly,
    Packed it into his bag. The young man immediately ordered the servant to lead the guest to the east hall and to the bed.

    In a short while, the distant temple bell rang, and the nearby village rooster crowed. The dawn light was faint, and the morning light was dim. Opening his eyes to see, he saw his body was still wet with dew, and the horse was still eating grass. Looking around, everything was silent and empty. Nothing was seen. He then presented the poem to the two gentlemen, who both praised it highly, believing it truly captured the essence of Tang poetry. They ordered it to be carved on the east side of the county, to ensure its lasting transmission. Qi Ren indeed rose to the Hanlin Academy through his literary achievements, dying at the age of eighty-nine, thus fulfilling the prophecy of great things. Afterward, Tang Gong governed Ji'an, and he often recounted the details like this.

    The Monkey That Listens to the Dharma

    In the county of Jishui, under the jurisdiction of Luzhou, there is an East Mountain, whose roots span a hundred miles, serving as a stronghold for the region. Its beauty and uniqueness make it look like a painting. During the Tiancheng period of the Later Tang dynasty, there was a monk named Xiu who built a thatched hut at the extreme end of the mountain. The trees were dense, and the path was rugged. For years, human footprints were rare. Only when woodcutters ventured deep into the forest did they see the monk sitting under a pine tree, with a flock of birds carrying fruits gathering before him. The monk took each fruit and ate it. After finishing, the birds flew away. The woodcutters occasionally mentioned this to others, and those interested in the unusual followed suit, visiting the hut to see the monk. At that time, the monk was sound asleep, holding a simple pillow and warming his feet, with a young woman guarding his bed. The visitors found this strange and, in admiration, competed to clear the ground and gather materials to build a large monastery. At the start of the construction, the monk called the craftsmen and warned them: "You who work with your hands, must drink alcohol and eat meat."

    17

    此处山神利害，不可轻犯，如何？”匠齐应曰：“请断荤酒以从事。”师许之。经月余，一匠忽思肉不可忍。因下山，数日复来。政斫削间，两虎逾垣而入，立匠者前。左右视，作哮吼声。其人惊怖。师曰：“必汝犯戒，首实为宜，吾当遣去也。”匠者解腰间布囊付师，曰：“适过醪桥市中，买熟牛肉一块，带来作下饭，无他也。”师曰：“是矣。”因截作二段喂虎，抚其背曰：“山子且去。”言讫，虎隐。人愈敬之。由是金帛之施，川汇河输，栋宇庄严，不日而就。

    Explanation

    17

    The dangers posed by the mountain deity are grave, and one should not lightly provoke them, what do you think?” Craftsmen Qi responded, “I shall abstain from meat and alcohol to undertake this task.” The master agreed. After more than a month, one of the craftsmen suddenly could not resist the craving for meat. He descended the mountain, and after several days, returned. While he was engaged in cutting and carving, two tigers leaped over the wall and entered, standing before the craftsmen. They looked around, roaring loudly. The craftsmen were filled with fear. The master said, “It must be that you have broken your vow; it is best to confess, and I will send them away.” The craftsman untied a cloth bag from his waist and handed it to the master, saying, “I just passed through the market at Laobiao, bought a piece of cooked beef, brought it to eat, nothing else.” The master replied, “That is it.” He then cut the beef into two pieces and fed it to the tigers, patting their backs and saying, “Mountain spirits, go now.” After he finished speaking, the tigers disappeared. The people became even more respectful of him. Consequently, donations of gold and silk flowed in like rivers converging, and grand and solemn buildings were completed in no time.

    18

    既落成，师说法以报檀施。讲演妙义，诸天雨花。俄而堂下涌出五井，皆满贮米、面、油、盐、蔬菜，取以饭众，不欠不余。师曰：“此五方龙王献供，以济匮乏，可名此山曰龙济，寺曰清凉。”今四井已湮，惟一尚在。师庵前乔木千章，蔽翳云日，树下磐石坦平，师每据之诵经，日以为常。有老猿栖树间，潜听，且窥师熟。一日，师偶出，猿下著袈裟，取经石上，阅之。师还望见，猿踉跄走去。师不问，亦不以告诸僧，但心识之曰：“此已解悟矣。”

    Explanation

    18

    Upon the completion of the construction, the master expounded the Dharma to repay the donors. He explained profound teachings, and heavenly beings showered flowers. Soon, five wells emerged from the ground below the hall, all filled with rice, flour, oil, salt, and vegetables, taken to feed the congregation, neither lacking nor in excess. The master said, "These five Dragon Kings offered their tribute to relieve poverty; this mountain can be named Longji (Dragon Relief) and the temple Qingliang (Cooling)." Now, four of the wells have dried up, only one remains. In front of the master's hermitage, there were a thousand tall trees, shading the clouds and sun. Beneath the tree was a flat rock, and the master would sit there to recite scriptures every day, as a daily habit. An old monkey lived in the tree, hiding to listen and observing the master closely. One day, the master happened to leave, and the monkey descended, put on the master's robe, and took the scriptures from the stone, reading them. When the master returned and saw, the monkey hurriedly ran away. The master did not ask, nor did he tell the other monks, but in his heart, he recognized, "This has already attained enlightenment."

    19

    明日，果有峡州袁秀才来谒。师知之，请入相见，缁衣玄巾，风致朴野。叙礼竟，白师曰：“逊姓袁，字文顺，峡中人也。族大以蕃，不乐仕进。独逊有志功名，求官辇下。明宗胡人，暮年昏惑。贤士良才，莫得而进。留滞数年，竟无所就。有知己者，荐为端州巡官。念瘴乡恶土，实不愿行。彼又劝之曰：‘子蹇困如此，尚暇择地哉？’不得已挈家抵任。未逾年，妻妾子女丧尽。憔悴一身，遂不复仕。往来江湖间，惟寻山望水，谢扰扰于名场；问道参禅，谈空空于释部。侧闻尊宿建大法幢，不惮远来，求依净社。攒眉蹙頞，固非嗜酒之渊明；举手推敲，颇类苦吟之贾岛。如蒙不弃，夫复何求。”即取书一幅呈师，乃贽启也。

    Explanation

    19

    The next day, a scholar from Xiangzhou named Yuan Xiucai came to pay a visit. The teacher knew him and invited him in. Yuan Xiucai was dressed in a black robe and wore a dark headband, with a simple and rustic demeanor. After exchanging courtesies, he said to the teacher, "My surname is Yuan, my courtesy name is Wenshun, and I am from Xiangzhong. My family is large and numerous, and I do not enjoy pursuing official positions. Only I have aspirations for fame and success, and I sought an official position in the capital. Emperor Mingzong, a non-Han Chinese ruler, became confused and bewildered in his old age. Virtuous scholars and talented individuals could not be promoted. I stayed for several years in the capital but ultimately achieved nothing. Someone who knew me well recommended me to be an inspector in Duanzhou. Thinking about the malarial and unhealthy place, I really did not want to go. He then advised me saying, 'You are in such a difficult situation, how can you still choose a place?' Unwillingly, I took my family to the post. Before a year passed, my wife, concubines, and children all died. Alone and emaciated, I no longer served in office. Traveling between the rivers and lakes, I only sought mountains and gazed at water, disassociating myself from the hustle and bustle of fame; seeking the Way and practicing Zen, discussing emptiness in Buddhist texts. I have heard that venerable elders have established a great Dharma banner, undeterred by the distance, I seek to join a pure community. Frowning and furrowing the brows, I am certainly not like the wine-loving Tao Yuanming; gesturing and pondering, I quite resemble the hardworking poet Jia Dao. If you do not reject me, what more could I ask for?" He immediately took out a scroll to present to the teacher, which was a letter of introduction.

    20

    其词曰：

    窃以生一拳梦幻之身，盖由恶业；熟三峡烟霞之路，亦自善缘。凡居覆载之间，悉在轮回之内。恭维龙济山主，修公大禅师座下：性融朗月，目泯空花。衍术数则允过于图澄，逞神通则端逾于杯渡。菩提本无树，机锋肯让于同袍；松柏摧为薪，泡影等观于浮世。十方瞻仰，四众归依。若如逊者，天地毫毛，山林踪迹。悲来抱树，谁怜凄恻其伤弓；穷则投林，畴暇从容于择木。无家可返，有佛堪依。痛兹妻子之沦亡，坐此功名之汩没。逢人舞剑，素非通臂之才；过寺题诗，忽动归山之兴。干旋坤转，无端变化几湮沉；春去秋来，管得繁华有枯槁。伊欲出类而拔萃，除非舍妄以归真。指引迷途，使入涅槃之路；引登觉岸，遄登般若之舟。惟愿慈悲，和南摄受！

    Explanation

    20

    The words say:

    I humbly believe that to be born with a fistful of dreamlike body is due to bad karma; to be familiar with the misty and hazy path of the Three Gorges is also due to good connections. All beings live between heaven and earth, and are all within the cycle of rebirth. I show respect to the master of Longji Mountain, under the seat of the great Zen master Xiu Gong: his nature is as clear as the bright moon, his eyes see through the illusions of the world. In divination and numerology, he surpasses Tu Cheng; in supernatural abilities, he exceeds Bei Du. The bodhi tree is not a tree, his sharp wit and skill are shared with his fellow monks; the pine and cypress are reduced to firewood, bubbles and shadows are viewed equally in the floating world. Respected by all directions, the four assemblies of believers rely on him. If one is a humble person, they are as insignificant as a hair on the body of heaven and earth, a trace in the mountains and forests. To cry and embrace a tree when sorrow comes, who pities the pitiful one whose heart is wounded like a bird; to seek refuge in the forest when in poverty, how can one spare time to choose a tree with ease. With no home to return to, there is a Buddha to rely on. To mourn the loss of wife and children, to be submerged by fame and achievements. To dance with a sword in front of people, it is not due to having the ability of a monkey with long arms; to pass by a temple and inscribe poetry, suddenly it stirs the desire to return to the mountains. Heaven and earth revolve, random changes almost sink into oblivion; spring goes and autumn comes, managing the prosperity and decay of flowers. He wants to stand out and excel, unless one gives up illusions and returns to the truth. To guide those who are lost, leading them to the path to nirvana; to lead to the shore of awakening, quickly boarding the boat of wisdom. I only wish for compassion, accepting with reverence.

    21

    师览毕，谓之曰：“绝好俊才，兼通内典。辱公不鄙，壮观山门。第有一事未便，不敢不以相闻。”逊曰：“何事？伏请见喻。”师曰：“公若顶巾束发，在我教谓之沐猴而冠；遽使削发被缁，在公教谓之儒名墨行。若斯二者，何以处之？”逊踧踖若有惭色。久之，乃曰：“但使心向禅宗，何妨俗扮，愿勿以形迹见拘也。倘得食已残之芋，长源自是俗人；补未了之经，次律岂非道者？法门广大，何所不容？”师曰：“若公之言，真所谓朝三而暮四者也。”逊曰：“何见讥之深也！”师曰：“偶然耳。”遂留之西馆，俾教行童。

    Explanation

    21

    After reading through, the teacher said to him, “You are an exceptionally talented man, well-versed in the internal teachings. It is an honor that you have not looked down upon me, and your presence greatly enhances our monastery. However, there is one matter that is inconvenient, and I dare not remain silent about it.” Xun replied, “What is it? I humbly request you to explain.” The teacher said, “If you were to wear a cap and tie up your hair, in my tradition this would be like a monkey wearing a cap — an absurd pretense. But if you were suddenly to shave your head and put on monastic robes, in your tradition this would be like a man who calls himself a Confucian but behaves like a Mohist — inconsistent and hypocritical. How should one deal with such a situation?” Xun became embarrassed and looked somewhat ashamed. After a long pause, he said, “As long as the heart is devoted to Chan Buddhism, what harm is there in appearing in lay dress? I only hope you will not be bound by outward appearances. If one can be content with eating leftover yams, one’s origin is that of a layperson; if one can complete an unfinished scripture, is that not the act of a practitioner? The Dharma gate is vast and encompasses all things.” The teacher said, “If what you say is true, then you are indeed a ‘morning three, evening four’ person.” Xun replied, “Why do you criticize me so harshly?” The teacher said, “It was just a coincidence.” Thus, he was kept in the western pavilion and assigned to teach the novices.

    22

    逊虽性识聪明，文词敏捷，然戏舞跳梁，好为儿态。有时跏趺床上，以被蒙头，使僧徒礼拜，曰：“此白衣观音见身也。”有时箕踞龛中，以靛涂面，令厨人致敬。曰：“此洪山大圣监斋也。”或纳蛇钵中，谓之降龙；或缚猫座下，谓之伏虎；如此者不一。僧颇苦之，以白于师。师笑曰：“故态也，善视之。”众遂不敢言，逊亦自若也。然山中景物，经其题咏者甚众，多不悉录，纪其一二尤者焉。

    △题解空寺

    古塔凌空玉笋高，斜阳半压水嘈嘈。老禅掩却残经坐，静听松声沸海涛。△书方丈

    Explanation

    22

    Xun, though naturally intelligent and quick with words, was playful and mischievous, often acting like a child. Sometimes he would sit cross-legged on a bed, cover his head with a blanket, and make the monks pay homage, saying, "This is the manifestation of the White-robed Guanyin." At other times, he would sit with his legs spread in a niche, paint his face with indigo, and make the kitchen workers show respect, saying, "This is the Great Saint of Hongshan overseeing the kitchen." He would sometimes put a snake in a bowl, calling it taming a dragon; or tie a cat to the seat, calling it taming a tiger. There were many such instances. The monks found it troublesome and reported it to the master. The master smiled and said, "It's his usual behavior; treat him well." The monks then dared not speak, and Xun remained as usual. However, many of the mountain's scenery were inscribed by him, but not all were fully recorded; let's record a few of the best ones.

    △Title: Explanation of the Empty Temple

    The ancient pagoda soars high like a jade bamboo, its shadow half-pressing the noisy water under the slanting sun. The old monk sits with a closed sutra, quietly listening to the sound of pines roaring like the sea. △Inscription for the Abbot's Room

    23

    几曲风琴响暗泉，乱红飞坠佛龛前。白云深护高僧榻，不许人间俗客眠。△送僧出山

    松翠侵衣屐印苔，杖藜几度此徘徊？山僧忘却山中好，去入红尘不再来。△咏鹤

    远辞华表傍玄关，别却浮丘伴懒残。金磬数声秋日晚，双飞带得白云还。△赠僧

    一瓶一钵一袈裟，几卷《楞严》到处家。坐稳蒲团忘出定，满身香雪坠昙华。△布袋和尚

    童子牵衣也不管，放下布袋打鼾睡。萦缠只是贪嗔痴，解脱无过戒定慧。△毛女图

    衣纫槲叶不须裁，萝月秋悬宝镜开。鹤背几随王母去，蛾眉曾识祖龙来。

    蟠桃结子三回熟，若木为薪十度摧。回首同时金屋伴，重泉玉匣葬寒灰！△落叶

    万片霜红照日鲜，飞来阶下覆苔砖。等闲不遣僧童扫，借与山中麂鹿眠。△方丈巢燕花正开，雨霁春欲回，缉垒成双到，穿帘作对来。飞上下，上下去又还，白门辞王谢，出入傍禅关。

    Explanation

    23

    A Wind Instrument's Melody Echoes Through the Dark Spring, Red Petals Fall Before the Buddha Altar. White Clouds Deeply Guard the Monk's Bed, Refusing to Allow the Mundane Visitors to Sleep. △Farewell to the Monk Leaving the Mountain

    Green Pines Intrude on His Robe, Sandals Leave Marks on the Mossy Ground. With a Walking Stick, He Has Paced Here Many Times. The Mountain Monk Has Forgotten the Beauty of the Mountains, Departing into the Mundane World, Never to Return. △Elegy for the Crane

    Far from the Honorific Pillar, Near the Mysterious Threshold, He Leaves Behind the Transient and Superficial, Staying with the Lazy and Indifferent. The Sound of a Golden Bell Rings in the Evening of Autumn, Two Birds Fly, Bringing Back the Clouds. △Gift to the Monk

    One Bottle, One Bowl, One Robe, A Few Volumes of the Lengyan Sutra Follow Him Wherever He Goes. Sitting Steadily on the Meditation Cushion, Forgetting to Leave His Meditative State, His Body Covered in Fragrant Snow, the Lotus Flower Falls. △The Cloth-Bag Monk

    The Child Pulls on His Robe, He Doesn't Care. He Sets Down His Cloth Bag and Sleeps, Snoring. The Attachments Are Merely Illusions of Greed, Hatred, and Delusion, True Liberation Comes from Precepts, Concentration, and Wisdom. △The Maiden of the Pines

    Clothing Made from Oak Leaves, No Need to Cut, The Moon in Autumn Hangs Like a Precious Mirror. On the Crane's Back, He Follows the Queen Mother of the West, Having Once Known Qin Shi Huang. △The Falling Leaves

    The Peaches of Immortality Ripen Three Times, The Mythical Tree Is Used as Firewood Ten Times. Looking Back, He Remembers His Past Companions, His Remains Buried in a Jade Box in the Depths of the Earth. △The Falling Leaves

    Ten Thousand Pieces of Frost-Red Reflect the Sun's Freshness, Flying Down to Cover the Mossy Bricks. Indifferently, He Doesn't Send the Novice Monk to Sweep Them Away, Lending Them to Deer in the Mountains to Sleep. △The Swallows Nesting in the Abbot's Quarters

    The Flowers Are Blooming, After the Rain Clears, Spring Is Returning. The Swallows Build Their Nests in Pairs, Flying Through the Curtains in Pairs. Flying Up and Down, Up and Down Again, Leaving the White Gate of the Wang and Xie Families, Entering and Exiting Near the Zen Gate.

    24

    钟梵定，长廊清昼静，远近雏学飞，呢喃语堪听。

    栖寺好，画栋雕梁巢莫保，秋去春复来，永伴山僧老。△山中四景

    门径苔深客到稀，游丝低逐软红飞。松梢零落飘金粉，童子枝头晒衲衣。

    风敲窗竹惊僧定，鸟触残花坠涧香。《圆觉》半函看已了，纫针自补旧衣裳。

    几点归鸦几杵钟，纷纷凉月在孤峰。清霜独染千林树，明月漫山一片红。

    十笏房清百衲温，名香长是夜深焚。道人爱看梅梢月，分付山童莫掩门。

    师一日忽升堂，命侍者召袁秀才来，告之曰：“秀才，腊月三十日到矣。”逊曰：“某亦知之。”师即唱偈示之曰：

    万法千门总是空，莫思啸月更吟风。这遭打个翻筋斗，跳入毗卢觉海中。

    Explanation

    24

    The bell's sound stills the air,
    The long corridor, in clear daylight, is quiet,
    Young birds learn to fly near and far,
    Their soft murmurs are worth listening to.

    To dwell in the temple is good,
    Its painted beams and carved pillars hold no lasting nest,
    Autumn departs, spring returns,
    Forever I shall remain with the mountain monk.
    △ Four Scenic Views of the Mountains

    The path is overgrown with moss, few guests arrive,
    Silken threads drift low, following the soft red that flies.
    Pine branches shed, golden dust falls,
    A child hangs the monk's robe on a branch to dry.

    The wind strikes the bamboo by the window, startling the monk's meditation,
    A bird brushes against withered flowers, scattering fragrance into the ravine.
    Half of the Ruanjue has been read and understood,
    With needle in hand, I mend my old robe.

    A few crows return, a few chimes of the bell,
    Cool moonlight spreads over the lonely peak.
    Clear frost alone stains the thousand trees,
    The bright moon covers the mountain, turning it red.

    Ten hu of room are clear, a hundred na of robes are warm,
    Fragrant incense is burned deep into the night.
    The Daoist loves to watch the moon on the plum branch,
    I tell the mountain boy not to close the door.

    One day, the master suddenly ascended the hall,
    He ordered the attendant to summon Mr. Yuan, and said to him:
    "Mr. Yuan, the thirtieth day of the twelfth lunar month has arrived."
    Mr. Yuan replied: "I also know this."
    Then the master recited a verse:

    All laws and gates are ultimately empty,
    Do not long to howl at the moon or sing to the wind.
    This time, do a somersault,
    And leap into the sea of awakening of Vairocana.

    25

    逊言下大悟，亦作二偈以答师，曰：

    泉石烟霞水木中，皮毛虽异性灵同。劳师为说无生偈，悟到无生始是空。

    万种喽灊林大节，千般伎俩木巢南。从今踏破三生路，有甚禅机更要参？

    唱讫，端坐而化。

    师集大众曰：“此人有异，汝等不可草草，须要谛视。”僧乃群聚细观，则一猿也。师始为说前事，众皆嗟异！举火荼毗之际，师亲摩其顶曰：“二百年后，还汝受用。”至宋南渡末，有民家妇，怀妊将产，梦猿入室，而诞一男，貌与猿肖。及长，不乐婚娶，坚求出家，父母从之，送入龙济为僧，名宗鍪。其后道价高重，虎侍猿随，变幻神奇，不可胜述，世称为肉身菩萨。果能重修梵宇，大转法轮，如吉之螺山接待庵、永宁桥，皆其所建。号支云，丛林称为支云鍪禅公。有语录十卷，文集四卷。其《蛇秽说》，尤行四方。迨今龙济奉为重开山祖师。忌日，犹有群虎绕塔之异。后人以鍪生时计之，正协修公所记，亦神矣哉！

    Explanation

    25

    Upon hearing the words, Xun suddenly gained enlightenment and composed two verses in response to the master, saying:

    Amidst the springs, stones, mist, and clouds, amidst water and trees, though the skin and fur differ, the spirit is the same. I labor to hear the master explain the verse of non-being; only upon realizing non-being is one truly empty.

    A myriad of great principles in the forest, a thousand kinds of tricks in the wooden nest to the south. From now on, I shall tread the path of three lifetimes, but what deeper Zen is there to ponder?

    After finishing singing, he peacefully passed away.

    The master gathered the assembly and said, "This person is extraordinary; you must not rush through this matter, but examine it carefully." The monks then gathered to observe closely, and it turned out to be a monkey. The master then explained the previous events, and the assembly all marveled at the strangeness! At the time of cremation, the master personally touched the top of his head and said, "Two hundred years from now, you will still be able to enjoy your practice." By the end of the Southern Song Dynasty, there was a woman from a common household who was pregnant and about to give birth. She dreamed that a monkey entered her room, and she gave birth to a boy who resembled a monkey. When he grew up, he did not wish to marry or take a wife, and he firmly sought to become a monk. His parents agreed and sent him to Longji Temple, where he was named Zongmou. Later, he achieved high spiritual attainment, accompanied by tigers and followed by monkeys, performing miraculous transformations that cannot be fully described. The world came to call him a living Buddha. Indeed, he was able to rebuild Buddhist temples and widely spread the Dharma, such as the Reception Hermitage on Rosary Mountain and Yongning Bridge, both of which he constructed. He was nicknamed Zhuyun, and the monastic community called him Master Zhuyun Zongmou. He had ten volumes of recorded sayings and four volumes of collected writings. His discourse on "Snake Filth" was particularly well-known throughout the land. Until now, Longji Temple honors him as the founder of a new era. On his anniversary, there is still the miraculous sight of tigers circling the stupa. Later generations, calculating from the time of Zongmou's birth, found that it exactly matches the records of Master Xiu, and it is indeed a marvelous event!

    26

    月夜弹琴记
    四明乌斯道，博洽君子也。洪武初，除吉安永新知县。到任三日，祇谒先圣于邑庠。顾见殿楹础边，隐隐有人形，怪而问之。儒士贺仲善进曰：“此宋谭节妇赵氏影也。元下江南，此地既归附。文丞相天祥起兵勤王，复之。未几，镏盘引元兵陷城，城中死者大半。谭氏一家亦仓卒避难于学，节妇匿大成殿，乱兵追及，见其年少色美，欲犯之。

    Explanation

    26

    Moonlit Night Playing the Guqin

    Wu Sidao of Si Ming was a learned and virtuous man. In the early years of the Hongwu era, he was appointed as the magistrate of Yongxin County in Ji'an Prefecture. On his third day in office, he paid homage to Confucius at the local school. As he looked around, he noticed a faint human figure near the base of the pillars in the hall, which struck him as strange, and he asked about it. A scholar named He Zhongshan approached and said, "This is the shadow of Zhao, the chaste widow from the Song Dynasty. When the Mongols conquered the south, this area was annexed. Chancellor Wen Tianxiang raised an army to support the emperor and briefly reclaimed the region. Not long after, Liu Pan led Mongol forces to capture the city, and many people were killed. The family of Zhao, including the chaste widow, also sought refuge in the school in haste. The widow hid in the Dacheng Hall, but the disorderly soldiers caught up with her, saw her youth and beauty, and intended to assault her."

    27

    妇大骂曰：‘吾贵宗女，名家妇，岂汝犬彘耦哉？且吾舅死于汝，吾姑又死于汝，恨不磔汝肉万段喂乌鸢。吾有死而已，岂耦汝犬彘哉？’ 兵怒，并其怀抱一岁儿杀之，血沁入砖之上。自宋、元至今，磨以沙石，煆以烈火，愈见明莹。邑人义而祀之。”乌公问祠安在，仲善导至其所。但见鼠穿败壁，苔绣空阶。谷变陵迁，怅贞魂之已远；时殊事异，慨老屋之仅存。公乃叹曰：“此吾为令者之责也。”乃捐俸，新其堂于泮池之上，刻其影于碑石之阴，仍亲作文，刊诸庑下。读者为之毛发森竦，涕泗交颐，而节妇之名彰著矣。

    Explanation

    27

    The woman shouted fiercely, "I am a noble lady, the wife of a distinguished family. How can you be no better than a dog or pig? Furthermore, my father-in-law died at your hands, and my mother-in-law also perished by you. I wish to have your flesh torn into ten thousand pieces to feed the crows. I have only death to look forward to; how can I be coupled with you, you scum?" The soldier, enraged, also killed the one-year-old child she was holding. The blood seeped into the bricks. From the Song and Yuan dynasties to the present day, the bricks were ground with sand and stones, fired with intense heat, and became increasingly clear and bright. The townspeople honored her with a shrine. Mr. Wu asked where the shrine was, and Zhong Shan led him to the site. But all they saw were rats gnawing through the walls and moss adorning the empty steps. Mountains have become valleys and valleys have become mountains; lamenting that the pure spirit has long departed. Times have changed, and things are different; regretting that only the old house remains. The official then sighed and said, "This is my duty as an official." He then donated his salary to rebuild the hall above the pond, carved her image on the back of a stone tablet, and personally wrote an inscription, which he had engraved on the eaves. Readers were filled with awe, tears streamed down their faces, and the name of the chaste woman became renowned.

    28

    公之子熙，字缉之，尤尚风概，且精于琴。见节妇事，啧啧叹慕，作《贞松操》，写之丝桐。一夕，天空月明，夜凉人静，独坐轩中，拂琴拭徽，调弦转轸。忽有美姬自外入。缉之讶曰：“何物女子，辄此来耶？”姬敛衽拜曰：“妾姓钟，名碧桃，宋谭节妇侍儿也。主母贞节，上帝嘉之，已位高仙。见莅南岳左右魏夫人所，享天上之乐矣。太上以其影留下界，恐人亵慢，将命六丁取之。使之衣服冠而坐，藏诸洞天。文昌忠孝司言：影在孔子礼殿，托得其所。

    Explanation

    28

    The son of the public figure, named Xī and known by the courtesy name Jīzhī, particularly admired the spirit of integrity and righteousness and was excellently skilled in playing the qin. Upon seeing the story of the chaste wife, he admired and yearned for it, composing the "Song of the Chaste Pine" and writing it on the qin. One night, the sky was clear and the moon was bright, the air was cool and the people were quiet. Sitting alone in the pavilion, he stroked the strings, wiped the frets, tuned the strings, and adjusted the tuning pegs. Suddenly, a beautiful maiden entered from outside. Jīzhī was surprised and asked, "What kind of woman are you, coming here without permission?" The maiden bowed respectfully and said, "I am a maiden named Zhōng Bìtáo, a servant of the chaste wife of Song Tán. The lady of the house is chaste and virtuous, praised by the Heavenly Deity, and has already attained a high rank among the immortals. She presides over the place of Lady Wei in the vicinity of Mount Heng and enjoys the music of heaven. The highest deity, fearing that people would disrespect her shadow, ordered the Six Dings to retrieve it. They dressed her in clothes and a hat and had her sit, hiding her in the celestial realms. The office of Virtue and Filial Piety stated that her shadow is in Confucius' ritual hall, placed in its proper place."

    29

    今必取之，未免随以风雷，惊骇宣圣，非所以重道崇儒也。莫若留在人间，永为激劝，其于世教，甚非小补。太上可之，命玄枢省下酆都，令本学地灵，常加守护，雷部按临，以时稽审。今冥司建议，以为阴阳之道，贵远嫌疑。本学地灵，但可外护，若其亲近，宜用旧人。以妾幸无罪戾，夙侍教言，授以薄职，俾敬卫焉。但视事以来，依栖无所，寄寓学宫土地祠。猥厕男神，甚不便当，欲乞于节妇坐侧，别设一位，题曰‘故侍儿钟氏神主’。则身无所苦，获燕雀之帡幪；鬼有所归，免鱼龙之混杂。如蒙矜悯，即赐施行。”缉之许焉。

    Explanation

    29

    Now it must be taken, but this will inevitably be followed by wind and thunder, startling the revered sage, which is not the way to honor the Dao and exalt Confucianism. It would be better to remain in the human world, serving as eternal inspiration. For the world's teachings, this is not a small benefit. The highest authority approves it, ordering the Xuanhu Provincial Office to descend to Fengdu, commanding the spirits of the local school to always protect it, and the Thunder Department should periodically inspect and review. The underworld authorities suggest that the principles of yin and yang value distance and avoid suspicion. The spirits of the local school only need external protection; if close, it is appropriate to use old people. I am fortunate to have no sins or faults, having long served under the teachings, and am appointed to a minor position to serve and protect. Since taking office, I have no place to rest, temporarily residing in the school's land temple. Inappropriately mixed with male deities, this is very inconvenient. I wish to request setting up a separate seat beside the chaste woman, inscribed as 'The Spirit Tablet of Former Attendant Zhong.' Then there will be no suffering, gaining the shelter of a sparrow; spirits have a place to return to, avoiding being mixed with fish and dragons. If you show mercy, grant this request. Ji approved it.

    30

    因问曰：“节妇仙居南岳，亦颇至祠中否？”姬曰：“不来也，自尊公大君子修葺之后，暂一下降。是夜，万籁无声，月色如昼。主母临睨旧乡，人非物是，黄尘清水，块土樵苏，不胜令威华表之感！因援琴鼓悲风一曲，妾听之凄然，双泪雨落。主母顾谓曰：‘汝尚淹滞鬼箓，无以相慰，可取纸笔来。’妾如言以进，即濡毫集古句七言近体诗二十首以赐，掷笔凌空而去。”缉之曰：“诗何所在？”姬曰：“妾宝之若珙璧。元本不可得，纵以相付，仙书云篆，公亦不能识也，但可诵耳，宜即录焉。”诗曰：

    花压栏干春昼长（《唐音》温飞卿），清歌一曲断君肠（《唐音》沈云卿）。云飞雨散知何处（唐温飞卿），天上人间两渺茫（《鼓吹》宋邕）。已托焦桐传密意（《鼓吹》胡宿），不将清瑟理霓裳（《鼓吹》宋邕）。江南旧事休重省（《草堂诗余》李玉词）桃叶桃根尽可伤（《诗统》宋庠）。

    Explanation

    30

    The Virtuous Woman, residing in the southern mountains, was asked, "Did she also come to the shrine?" The lady replied, "She did not come. Since the great gentleman, a paragon of virtue, renovated the shrine, she descended briefly for a short while. That night, all sounds were silent, and the moonlight was as bright as daylight. The lady mother looked down upon the old hometown, seeing that people had changed while objects remained the same. The yellow dust and clear water, the earth and firewood, evoked a profound sense of the immortal's return! She then took up her zither and played a mournful tune. I listened to it, feeling deeply moved, and tears fell like rain. The lady mother turned to me and said, 'You are still lingering in the records of the dead, and I cannot comfort you. Go and fetch paper and ink.' I followed her instructions and brought them. She then dipped her brush and composed twenty seven-character regulated verse poems by collecting ancient lines, giving them to me, and then she tossed her brush into the air and disappeared into the sky." I asked, "Where are the poems?" She replied, "I treasure them as if they were precious jewels. The original manuscript is unattainable. Even if I were to give them to you, the immortal's writings in cloud script, you would not be able to read them. Only to be recited, it is appropriate to record them immediately." The poems are as follows:

    Flowers press against the railings, and the spring day is long (from "Tang Music" by Wen Feiying), a clear song breaks one's heart (from "Tang Music" by Shen Yunqing). Where do the clouds and rain disperse? (from Wen Feiying) Heaven and earth are both boundless (from "The Drum Blowing" by Song Yong). Already entrusted to the zither to convey secret meanings (from "The Drum Blowing" by Hu Su), not to play the qin for the celestial garments (from "The Drum Blowing" by Song Yong). The old stories of the south should not be revisited (from "The Grass Hall Poetic Remains" by Li Yu), both the peach leaf and the peach root are worthy of sorrow (from "The Poetic Canon" by Song Xiang).

    31

    魂归溟漠魄归泉（《三体》朱褒），却恨青娥误少年（《鼓吹》无名氏）。自是桃花贪结子（《唐音》王建），只应梅蕊故依然（《诗统》陈简斋）。风流肯落他人后（唐李白），哀乐犹惊逝水前（《鼓吹》许浑）。何事黄昏尚凝睇（《鼓吹》崔玨），孤灯挑尽未成眠（唐白乐天）。

    寒蛩唧唧树苍苍（《三体》李涉），城上高楼接大荒（《鼓吹》柳宗元）。午夜漏声催晓箭（唐杜甫），六街晴色动秋光（《鼓吹》张泌）。满庭诗景飘红叶（《三体》雍陶），此地悲风愁白杨（唐李白）。舞袖弓弯浑忘却（屏上画美人诗），人间惟有鼠拖肠（宋欧阳修）。

    云想衣裳花想容（唐李白），青春已过乱离中（《唐音》刘文房）。功名富贵若长在（唐李白），得丧悲欢尽是空（唐温飞卿）。窗里日光飞野马（《鼓吹》韩偓），岩前树色隐房栊（《唐音》王维）。身无彩凤双飞翼（《鼓吹》李商隐），油壁香车不再逢（《诗统》晏殊）。

    Explanation

    31

    The soul returns to the vast void, the spirit to the springs (from "Three-Body" by Zhu Bao), yet regrets that the beautiful maiden has misled the young man (from an anonymous work in "Gu Chu"). It is because the peach blossoms are greedy for fruit (from Tang dynasty poet Wang Jian), only the plum blossoms should remain unchanged (from Chen Jianzhai in "Shi Tong"). One would not fall behind others in charm or grace (Tang dynasty poet Li Bai), sorrow and joy still startle before the flowing water (from Xu Hun in "Gu Chu"). Why still gaze intently at dusk (from Cui Jue in "Gu Chu"), the lonely lamp has been picked clean, yet sleep has not come (Tang dynasty poet Bai Juyi).

    The cold insects chirp and the trees are dark green (from Li She in "Three-Body"), the tall buildings on the city wall connect to the vast wilderness (from Liu Zongyuan in "Gu Chu"). The sound of the water clock in the middle of the night urges the dawn arrow (Tang dynasty poet Du Fu), the six streets are bathed in bright autumn light (from Zhang Bi in "Gu Chu"). The entire courtyard is filled with poetic scenes of falling red leaves (from Yong Tao in "Three-Body"), the sad winds and weeping poplars here add to the sorrow (Tang dynasty poet Li Bai). The dance sleeves and bent bows are all forgotten (from a painting of a beautiful woman), in the world, only mice drag their intestines (Northern Song dynasty poet Ouyang Xiu).

    The clouds imagine clothes, the flowers imagine beauty (Tang dynasty poet Li Bai), youth has passed in the midst of chaos and turmoil (from Liu Wenfang in "Tang Yin"). If fame, wealth, and glory were to last forever (Tang dynasty poet Li Bai), gains and losses, sorrows and joys are all empty (Tang dynasty poet Wen Tingyun). Sunlight flies like wild horses through the window (from Han Wo in "Gu Chu"), the color of trees before the rocks hides the windows (from Wang Wei in "Tang Yin"). Without the colorful wings of a phoenix, one cannot fly together (from Li Shangyin in "Gu Chu"), the fragrant chariot with oil-burnished walls will not be met again (from Yan Shu in "Shi Tong").

    32

    应笑无成返薛萝（《鼓吹》谭用之），年年惆怅是春过（《鼓吹》罗邺）。时攀芳树愁花尽（《鼓吹》温飞卿），寒恋重衾觉梦多（唐温飞卿）。桂岭瘴来云似墨（《鼓吹》柳宗元），蜀江风澹水如罗（《唐音》温飞卿）。人生富贵须回首（唐薛能），世事无几奈尔何（《鼓吹》司空图）！

    家在寒塘独掩扉（《唐音》刘文房），高情雅澹世间稀（《鼓吹》刘梦得）。不将脂粉涴颜色（唐杜甫），惟恨缁尘染素衣（《诗统》陈简斋）。归目并随回雁尽（《鼓吹》柳宗元），离魂潜逐杜鹃飞（《鼓吹》韦庄）。东风吹泪对花落（《鼓吹》赵嘏），惆怅朱颜不复归（《鼓吹》宋邕）。

    Explanation

    32

    One should smile at returning to a simple life without much achievement, as each year brings sorrow during the passing of spring. Climbing fragrant trees while lamenting the fading of flowers, and feeling the warmth of heavy quilts leading to many dreams. The dark clouds from the mountainous region of Guilin are like ink, while the gentle wind and calm waters of the Sichuan River are like silk. One must reflect on their wealth and status, and there is little one can do about the many events of life.

    A home in a cold pond, with the door closed, is a place where a high and refined spirit is rare in the world. Not using makeup to spoil one's natural beauty, but regretting that black dust has stained one's white clothes. Looking back as the returning geese fly away, and the soul following the flying cuckoo bird. Tears blown by the east wind as flowers fall, and sadness that one's youthful appearance will not return.

    有时颠倒着衣裳（唐杜甫），万转千回懒下床（唐崔莺莺）。艳骨已成兰麝土（《鼓吹》皮日休），蓬门未识绮罗香（《鼓吹》秦韬玉）。汉朝冠盖皆陵墓（《三体》唐彦谦），魏国山河半夕阳（《鼓吹》李益）。满眼波涛终古事（《鼓吹》薛逢），离人到此倍堪伤（《鼓吹》罗邺）。

    33

    In every place, the setting sun casts shadows on grass that looks like moss (《鼓吹》韩偓); in a sunny, warm pond, one wanders alone (《鼓吹》韩偓).     Sparse stars fill the clear sky (《唐音》储光羲), and near the door, a cold river flows with a gentle sound (《唐音》戎昱). Often suspecting that good things are illusory (《鼓吹》薛能), it is said that even though it seems emotionless, there is still emotion (《唐音》刘禹锡). Drink and forget past grievances (《鼓吹》纪唐夫), and do not seek fame through writing (《鼓吹》柳宗元). In autumn, seeing the moon evokes thoughts of returning home (《唐音》雍陶), and leaning against a warm brazier, one sits until dawn (唐白乐天).

    缉之奇之，因曰：“节妇仙居，既已闻名，其舅姑夫子，抑又如何？”姬曰：“天医傅以玄洲不死之膏，赐以完形复体之符，一门百口，往梯仙国矣。” 曰：“何谓梯仙？”姬曰：“凡初得道者，皆送此修行，然后渐登品位，犹登梯然，故曰梯仙。”缉之又曰：“尔何不偕往？”姬曰：“缘妾前世为女医，误投人药，致损贵胎，以故再世罚为女身以偿，坐此少缓，尚隔两尘。”缉之曰：“然则汝亦良家子乎？”姬曰：“妾幼时，父母以贫故，鬻于赵氏。赵，故宋宗室也，售妾以媵其女。女即节妇，与妾年相若，蒙其怜爱，视犹骨肉。及归谭氏，妾从行焉。时谭方门庭鼎盛，圭组蝉联。褥隐绣芙蓉，极一时之富贵；砚寒金井水，洒万斛之珠玑。

    Ji was amazed and said, "The chaste woman who has attained immortality is already famous. How about her mother-in-law and father-in-law?" The maiden explained, "All those who initially attain the Dao are sent here to practice, then gradually ascend in rank, like climbing a ladder, hence the name ladder of immortals." Ji then asked, "Why don't you go together?" The maiden said, "Because in my previous life I was a female physician, I mistakenly administered medicine, causing harm to a noble fetus, and thus in this life I am punished to be reborn as a woman to atone. Because of this, I am slightly delayed, still separated by two layers of existence." Ji asked, "Then are you also from a good family?" The maiden said, "When I was young, my parents sold me to the Zhao family because of poverty. Zhao, a former member of the Song royal family, bought me to serve as a concubine for his daughter.     所见所闻，罔非礼义；若长若幼，皆擅才华。主母又聪明贤懿，不出闺房，雅善歌词，仍工笔札。每有吟咏，录似夫君，一览之余，辄焚其稿。盖以非妇人事，不欲使人知也。我主君亦英迈夙成，风流倜傥。文章水涌，倒三峡之词源；议论风生，惊四筵之雄辩。妾侍左右，饱闻训言；虽在贱微，颇习诗礼。不幸宋箓既讫，元运方兴。草昧英雄起，空怜文相之勤王；江山云雾昏，可恨镏盘之卖国。我主母洁身就死，而婢子忍耻偷生，颠沛流离，窜伏林莽。主恩难报，徒怀结草之心；女质易殂，竟作翳桑之鬼。物情恶衰歇，谁招碧玉之游魂；吾道属艰难，畴葬绿珠之弱骨。万言莫尽，大概若斯，不敢久留，幽明路异。” 遂去。明日，缉之白诸父。乌公以为诗虽奇妙，而怪诞不经，不许。

    41

    Everything seen and heard is without exception in accordance with propriety and righteousness; whether young or old, all possess great talent. The main lady is intelligent, virtuous, and skilled in poetry and calligraphy, despite staying within the confines of her home. Whenever she composed poetry, she would copy it for her husband, who would read it and then burn the manuscript, as it was not fitting for a woman to be known for her literary works. My master is naturally accomplished and has a free-spirited and elegant demeanor. His writings flow like a torrential flood, rivaling the source of the Three Gorges, and his oratory is so powerful that it astonishes everyone in the room. I, serving at his side, have heard much of his teachings and have learned much of poetry and propriety despite my lowly status. Alas, the Song dynasty has declined, and the Yuan dynasty is rising. Warlords have emerged during the chaotic period, and I lament the loyal officials who tried to support the fallen dynasty. The land is shrouded in mist, and I despise the traitors who betrayed the state for personal gain. My master's wife died nobly, while I, as a servant, survived through hardship and hiding in the wilderness. The master's kindness is hard to repay, and I can only harbor the intention to repay a favor as Ji Zha did. My frail body is easily weakened, and I have become a ghost of the Yisang. The world abhors decline, and who will remember the ghost of Bi Yu? My path is difficult, and who will bury the weak bones of Lu Zhu? A thousand words cannot fully express the situation, and I must part ways due to the different paths of the living and the dead. So, I departed. The next day, Jizi informed the elders. Wugong found the poem strange and unbelievable, and refused to accept it.

    越两月，一夕，缉之被酒，不能寝。起出轩前纵步，挹天香于丹桂，玩月影于素娥。已而，前姬又进拜，且言曰：“妾向所求，幸蒙允诺，意公仁者，见义勇为；而侧耳逾时，未闻施设，君子有成人之美，何惮而不果乎？”缉之谓曰：“吾父弗汝信，奈何？可取当时无人知者一两事语我，我白之家君，庶几有证，或可就也。”姬曰：“记文丞相起兵时，永新七大姓皆在勤王之死，而我主君与东门张御带家为之首。城复日，人皆相庆，独主母有忧色，告主君曰：‘城虽云复，戎马必再来，城中之人，定遭毒手。我夫妇生死未可知，万一不幸，惟死而已，誓不辱也’。主君姑为好言以解之，主母不以为然。主君又举司马温公语曰：‘天若祚宋，必无此事。’主母摇首长叹数声，取衣裙，题诗十首于其上；亦古语也。

    After two months, one evening, Jizhi was drunk and could not sleep. The concubine said, "Remember when Wen Shengxiang raised an army? Our fates are uncertain; in case of misfortune, we will only die, swearing never to be disgraced.' My master tried to reassure her with kind words, but the lady of the house did not agree. My master then quoted Sima Guang, saying, 'If heaven favors Song, this will not happen.' The lady of the house shook her head and sighed several times, took her clothes, and wrote ten poems on them; these are also ancient words."

    主君读之曰：‘若然，吾何恨！’已而主母又指抱儿曰：‘我则死矣，如此何？’主君曰：‘吾固知之，付之造物。’因以一金钱系之项上，弄之曰：‘若遇凶人，儿以此买命也。’遂相视泣下沾襟。后遇害日，金钱不知所在，为血渍成钱影一枚印儿傍，第观者不谛视，故不知也。诗亦惟妾记忆耳。若此二事，皆世所未知者。”缉之录以呈父，乌公尚未深信，即命骑往文庙，取水洗砖而验焉，则见儿影之傍，钱迹宛然在。众始惊愕。

    公乃如言，题一主，设于节妇神座侧畔，缉之又以酒肴祭之。其夕，妾来谢曰：“感君设位，兼辱祭仪，无以为报；公平生好琴，但《广陵散》一曲，世久失传。妾承教主君，尚忆之耳，愿以相授。”乃出其谱于袖中，付缉之曰：“公善自爱，妾不复来矣！”倏然而去。由是弹琴大进，独步浙中，靳秘此曲，弗以传人。缉之死，谱亦竟绝焉。
