    45

    The master read it and said, "If so, what have I to lament!" Afterward, the master's wife pointed to the child and said, "I will die, but what of this child?" The master replied, "I already knew it, leave it to fate." Then he tied a gold coin around its neck and said, "If you meet a wicked person, the child can use this to buy his life." They then looked at each other and cried, their tears wetting their sleeves. On the day of the disaster, the gold coin was nowhere to be found, but it was stained with blood and left a shadow of a coin beside the child. However, observers did not look closely, so they did not know. The poem is only remembered by me. These two things are unknown to the world." Ji Zhi recorded it and presented it to his father, but Wu Gong did not yet fully believe. He immediately ordered a rider to go to the temple, fetch water, and wash the brick to verify. The coin's trace was clearly visible. The crowd was then shocked.

    He then did as he was told, inscribed a tablet, and placed it beside the chaste woman's shrine. Ji Zhi offered wine and food to it. That evening, the woman came to thank him and said, "I am grateful for setting up the tablet and for the honor of the ritual, but I have nothing to repay you. Sir, you have always loved the lute, but the Guangling San tune has been lost for a long time. I was taught by the master and still remember it. I wish to teach it to you." She then took the score from her sleeve and gave it to Ji Zhi, saying, "Take care of yourself, I will not come again!" She suddenly left. From then on, his skill at the lute greatly improved, and he became the best in Zhejiang. He kept this tune secret and did not pass it on to others. When Ji Zhi died, the score also became extinct.

    46

    何思明游酆都录
    何思明，大宋人，号烂柯樵者。通五经，尤专于《易》，以性学自任，酷不喜老、佛。间遇其徒于道，辄斥之曰：“四民之中，纵不为士，为农、为工、商，岂不可也？何至为是哉？”著《警论》三篇，每篇反复数千言，推明天理，辨析异端，匡正人心，扶植世教。其上篇略曰：“先儒谓：天即理也。以其形体而言，谓之天；以其主宰而言，谓之帝。帝即天，天即帝。非苍苍之上，别有一天。宫室居处，端冕垂旒，若世之帝王者，此释、老之论也。不特此也，又有所谓三天、九天、三十三天；三帝、九帝、十方诸帝，何天之多而帝之众耶？由是言之，天未免如阶级之形，帝未免有割据之争矣。甚者尊汉张道陵为天师，天岂有师乎？以宋林氏女为天妃，天果有妃乎？盖天者，理之所从出，圣人法天。道陵纵圣，亦人鬼耳，使天而师之，是天乃道陵之不若也。林女既死，特游魂耳。

    Explanation

    46

    He Siming's Journey to Fengdu**

    He Siming, a man from the Song Dynasty, was known by the nickname "Lan Ke Woodcutter." He was proficient in the Five Classics, especially the Yijing (Book of Changes), and dedicated himself to the study of human nature. He strongly disliked Daoism and Buddhism. Whenever he encountered their followers on the road, he would rebuke them, saying: "Among the four classes of people, even if one is not a scholar, being a farmer, artisan, or merchant is surely acceptable. Why would they resort to such things?" He wrote three essays titled Jing Lun (Warning Discourse), each of which was thousands of words long, elaborating on the principles of heaven and reason, analyzing and refuting heterodox teachings, correcting and guiding people's hearts, and supporting and upholding the world's moral teachings. The first essay briefly states: "Ancient scholars said: 'Heaven is the principle.' When speaking of its physical form, it is called heaven; when speaking of its sovereign role, it is called the emperor. The emperor is heaven, and heaven is the emperor. It is not another heaven above the blue sky. The palaces and regalia, with their ceremonial robes and jade pendants, like the emperors and kings of the world, are the views of Buddhism and Daoism. Not only this, but there are also the three heavens, nine heavens, and thirty-three heavens; the three emperors, nine emperors, and emperors in all directions. Why so many heavens and so many emperors? Therefore, heaven is not free from the appearance of a hierarchy, and emperors are not free from territorial disputes. Some even regard Zhang Daoling of Han as the Heavenly Master. How can heaven have a teacher? Regard Lin, a woman from Song, as the Heavenly Consort. Does heaven really have a consort? Heaven is the source of principles. Sages follow the example of heaven. Even if Zhang Daoling is a sage, he is still a human ghost. If heaven were to regard him as a teacher, it would mean that heaven is inferior to Zhang Daoling. Lin, after death, is merely a wandering spirit."

    47

    使天而妃之，是天犹有情欲之未忘也，乌得为天哉？彼以道陵天师也，不敢遽指为帝，而加以师称，所以尊天。不知无是理，适所以慢天。彼以林氏天女也，不敢侪以为鬼，而蒙以妃号，所以敬天。不知为是说，乃所以诬天也。诬天慢天，罪不容诛矣。”又谓：“世之人，徒知在天之天，故见日月星辰之光，风雨霜露之显，吉与凶，天之为也；祸与福，天之降也，是则然矣。然不知有己之天焉，己之天，即天之天。是故丹扃煌煌，天之君也；灵台湛湛，天之帝也。

    Explanation

    47

    If Heaven were to make her a consort, it would mean that Heaven still has desires that it has not forgotten. How could it be called Heaven? They claim that the Daoist Master is superior to Heaven, and they dare not directly call him an emperor, but instead call him a Master, to show respect to Heaven. They do not know that this is not the case, and it is actually disrespectful to Heaven. They say that Lin is a heavenly maiden, and they dare not call her a ghost, but instead call her a consort, to show respect to Heaven. They do not know that this is not the case, and it is actually to defame Heaven. To defame and disrespect Heaven, the crime is unforgivable. They also say: "People in the world only know the Heaven in the sky, so they see the light of the sun, moon, stars, and the manifestations of wind, rain, frost, and dew. Good and bad fortune are the work of Heaven, and disaster and blessing are bestowed by Heaven. This is true. But they do not know that there is also a Heaven within themselves, and one's own Heaven is the same as Heaven. Therefore, the brilliant red gates are the ruler of Heaven, and the clear and serene mind is the emperor of Heaven.

    48

    三纲五常，炳焕昭晰，非日月星辰之光乎？礼乐法度，明白正大，非风雨霜露之教乎？己之君与天之君戾，则凶也祸也，必以类而从；天之帝与己之帝合，则吉也福也，亦以类而至。达者信之，愚者懵焉。冥顽之徒，谓天为不闻，造恶自若，然心之天则固闻矣；侥幸之徒，谓天为可谄，淫祀是务，然心之帝已斥之矣。庸昧之辈，谓帝为可罔，矫诬是为。寻常昧昧也，而指天曰此可恃；平昔蚩蚩也，而怨天曰此罔知。每夕焚香，不可告者多矣；终年素食，知而犯者屡焉。”其持论言近指远，类如此。

    Explanation

    48

    The Three Bonds and Five Constants shine brightly and clearly, are they not like the light of the sun, moon, and stars? Rituals, music, and legal systems are clear and upright, are they not like the teachings of wind, rain, frost, and dew? When one's earthly ruler conflicts with the heavenly mandate, calamity and misfortune are sure to follow; when the heavenly ruler harmonizes with one's earthly ruler, blessings and prosperity will also come. The wise believe this, while the foolish are confused. Stubborn and ignorant people claim that heaven does not hear, committing evil without restraint, yet the moral conscience of their hearts certainly does hear; those who take advantage of luck or chance claim that heaven can be flattered, engaging in excessive and improper worship, yet the moral ruler of their hearts has already rejected them. Ordinary and ignorant people claim that the moral ruler can be deceived, falsely claiming and deceiving. Those who are ordinarily ignorant point to heaven and say it can be relied upon; those who are usually foolish complain to heaven and say it is unaware. Every night they burn incense, yet there are many who cannot confess their wrongdoings; they eat vegetarian food all year long, yet those who know better but repeatedly violate it are numerous. His arguments are close in wording but far-reaching in meaning, like this.

    49

    至正丁酉正月初六日，偶得疾，数日加亟，诸生从俗，私为之祷。思明知之，训之曰：“贤辈虽曰读书，而烛理未彻，鬼神岂可以酒肉私？人命岂可以纸钱买？吾谁欺？欺天乎？”是夜卒。独心下稍暖，不敢殓。诸生环守之，凡七昼夜，觉绵动，候之。鼻中气勃勃出，急捣姜汁灌之，良久眼开，天明而呼吸续矣。十日始能言，乃召弟子告曰：“二教之大，鬼神之著，其至矣乎！曩吾僻见，过毁老、释，今致削官减禄，几不能生，小子识之。”

    Explanation

    49

    On the sixth day of the first lunar month in the year Ding You of the Zhizheng era (1357), I suddenly fell ill, and the condition worsened over several days. The students followed custom and privately prayed for me. Reflecting and knowing, I taught them, saying: "Though you call yourselves readers, you have not fully grasped the truth. Can ghosts and gods be privately appeased with food and drink? Can human life be bought with paper money? Whom am I deceiving? Am I deceiving Heaven?" That night, I passed away. Only my chest was slightly warm, so they dared not embalm me. The students guarded me around the clock for seven days and nights. They felt my pulse moving and waited. They saw my breath coming out in great gulps. They quickly mashed ginger juice and gave it to me. After a long time, my eyes opened, and by dawn, my breathing continued. Ten days later, I could speak again. Then I called my disciples and told them: "The greatness of the two teachings, the prominence of ghosts and gods, is indeed profound! In the past, my narrow view led me to criticize Buddhism and Daoism too harshly. Now I have lost my position and reduced my salary, nearly unable to survive. You must remember this, my disciples."

    50

    门人请其详，思明曰：“子不语怪，固然。亦不可不使汝曹知果报之不虚也。始吾病革时，见两苍蝇堕床前，视之，已变为人矣。青衣、黄巾、红抹额，揖余曰：‘奉命召君。’余问：‘谁召？’其人曰：‘内台。’余曰：‘乱离道梗，何由可去？且无知己在台。’其人曰：‘酆都内台也。’余曰：‘吾儒者，不知所谓酆都内台。’其人怒，囊余袋中，袋类网罟，结细绳为之。余坐袋内，两人持之行树巅如飞，时觉树梢拂袋，谡谡有声。既又入空濛中，渺渺茫茫，四无畔岸，波涛汹涌，腥风袭人。黄巾挈囊，如履平地，余亦不觉有所苦也。又半日，方有路，始出余袋中。押过一所，若把截处，守者高鼻深目，拳发胡须，类回回人。问黄巾曰：‘何篆？’对曰：‘朱篆。

    Explanation

    50

    The disciples asked for the details, and Sīmíng replied, "The sage does not speak of strange matters, which is true. Yet it is also necessary for you to know that the principle of retribution is not empty. When I was gravely ill, I saw two flies fall before my bed. Upon looking, they had already transformed into people. One wore a blue robe, a yellow cap, and a red headband. He bowed to me and said, 'We have come to summon you.' I asked, 'Who summoned me?' He replied, 'The Inner Court.' I said, 'In this time of chaos and broken roads, how can I go? Moreover, I have no friend in the court.' He said, 'It is the Inner Court of Fēngdū.' I said, 'As a Confucian scholar, I do not know what is meant by the Inner Court of Fēngdū.' The man became angry and put me into a bag, which was like a fishing net, made of fine ropes. I sat inside the bag as two men carried it through the treetops like they were flying. I could feel the tree branches brushing against the bag, making a rustling sound. Then we entered a vast, misty expanse, boundless and endless, with no shore in sight. The waves were surging, and a foul wind blew upon me. The man with the yellow cap carried the bag as if walking on solid ground, and I did not feel any discomfort. After half a day, a path appeared, and I was finally removed from the bag. We passed a place that seemed like a checkpoint. The guards had high noses, deep eyes, curly hair, and beards, resembling Huihui people. I asked the man with the yellow cap, 'What seal?' He replied, 'The red seal.'

    51

    ’又有二皂衣，引一男子三妇人来，守者又问：‘何篆？’皂衣曰：‘黑篆。’守者曰：‘不可不仔细，请观之。’各出一牌，长可寸半，阔可寸许，一朱字，一墨字，皆不可识。守者曰：‘是矣。’放入门。黄巾偕余遵左廊而行，彼则循右廊而去。余因问曰：‘此为何所？’曰‘酆都第一关也。’余方悟已死，复问其：‘所持牌，何有朱、墨之异？’曰：“冥司追人，暂至而复出者，则以朱。永不出者则以墨。’余不觉失声曰：‘然则我当复生也？’ 黄巾曰：‘虽当复生，亦甚费周折。’余见其颇有相眷之意，因浼之曰：‘某此行，全赖二公作成。’黄巾曰：‘自有主者，我何能焉？’行数里，入铁围城，城门守者问如前而加切。俄抵台府，黄巾曰：‘君虽无重罪，然阴道尚严，不比凡世。’解索缚余颈，牵以入。先过冠服司，主者令去余衣巾曰：‘送寄自房收。’余短衣囚首，带索而行。

    Explanation

    51

    There were two men in black robes who led a man and three women to come. The gatekeeper asked again, "What seal?" The black-robed men replied, "A black seal." The gatekeeper said, "One must be very careful. Please look at them." Each produced a tablet, about one and a half inches long and an inch wide, one with a red character and one with a black character, both of which were unrecognizable. The gatekeeper said, "This is correct." He then allowed them to pass through the gate.

    The yellow-hatted man walked with me along the left corridor, while the other went along the right corridor. I asked, "What place is this?" He replied, "It is the First Gate of Fengdu." At that moment, I realized I was dead. I asked again, "Why are there both red and black seals on the tablets?" He said, "In the underworld, those who are temporarily brought and then returned are marked with red, while those who never return are marked with black." Unconsciously, I exclaimed, "Does that mean I will be reborn?" The yellow-hatted man said, "Even if you are to be reborn, it will be very complicated." Seeing that he seemed to have some affection for me, I asked him to help me, saying, "This journey of mine depends entirely on your two gentlemen’s assistance." The yellow-hatted man replied, "There is a master in charge; how could I do anything?"

    After walking several miles, we entered the Iron Encircled City. The gatekeeper at the city gate asked questions as before, but with greater intensity. Soon, we arrived at the Hall of the Throne. The yellow-hatted man said, "Although you have no serious crime, the laws of the underworld are still strict, unlike in the world of the living." He unbound the rope around my neck and led me in. First, we passed through the Office of Hats and Clothing, where the official ordered me to remove my clothes and headgear, saying, "They will be sent to your own room for storage." I was left in short clothes and a prisoner’s head covering, still bound with a rope, and walked on.

    52

    “及仪门，一黄巾先去，顷间，引五六人出，执余以入，跪阶下。台尊服章如王者，侍卫甚多。问余曰：‘尔非衢州儒士何思明乎？’余曰：‘是也。’台尊曰：‘所贵乎儒者，上窥鸿濛，中法圣智，下穷物理？辟干阖坤，造妙诣微；陶冶精醇，橐龠元和。究无中有象之蕴，妙阴阳动静之根。渊默澄凝以为体，翕忽变化以为用。出入无方，会三于一，夫是之谓儒，而鬼神莫能窥之矣。今尔偏执己见，造作文词，谤毁仙真，讥讪道佛。天至大，以阶级比之；帝至尊，以割据戏之；妄论天师之号，妄辨天妃之称。其罪大矣。

    Explanation

    52

    Upon reaching the ceremonial gate, a man clad in a yellow turban went ahead. Shortly thereafter, he led out five or six others, who seized me and brought me inside, where I knelt at the steps below. The venerable figure before me was dressed in regal attire, and was accompanied by a large entourage of attendants. He asked me, "Are you not the Confucian scholar He Siming from Quzhou?" I replied, "Yes, I am." The venerable one said, "What is valued in a scholar is to look upward to the boundless void, to follow the wisdom of the sages, and to explore the principles of nature. He opens heaven and earth, attains the subtle and profound; refines the pure and refined, and channels the primal harmony. He explores the hidden forms within the void, and grasps the root of the movement and stillness of yin and yang. He takes deep silence and clarity as his essence, and sudden transformation as his function. He moves without fixed form, unifying the three into one — this is what is called a scholar, and even ghosts and spirits cannot fathom him. Yet now you stubbornly cling to your own views, composing words and phrases that slander immortals and mock Daoism and Buddhism. Heaven is the greatest, yet you compare it to social hierarchy; the emperor is the most exalted, yet you treat him as a fragmented power. You recklessly discuss the title of Celestial Master, and recklessly debate the name of the Heavenly Consort. Your guilt is great indeed."

    53

    且儒书中言天者不一，若《春秋》书‘天王’，《诗》称‘伣天之妹’、‘昊天其子’，使皆若尔论，天既无师与妃，又安得有王、有妹、有子者乎？尔之学诚拘而不通，滞而有碍。拘则局于一器，滞则胶于一隅。不通则固陋，有碍则鄙僻，真俗腐迂谬之士，胡可冒儒者之名乎？’命取何姓簿来，于余姓名下，以朱笔抹之，复傍注之，毕。省谕曰：‘尔本合为六品官，出入华要。由尔弗信仙佛，诬罔鬼神，特降为七品。’余顿首谢，且请改过。台尊曰：‘此人面承腹诽，退有后言，可令阅狱，折服其心。’数卒捽余下，付黄巾领去省业司。中有宝塔一座，僧立塔傍，香烛幡幢，荧煌罗列。黄巾再拜，余亦拜。僧开塔取一大珠，以金盘承之，黄巾以双手擎捧前行，余随之，皆幽暗境也。余问：‘僧谁乎？’曰：‘导冥和尚也。’又问：‘珠何为？’曰：‘地藏王菩萨愿珠也。狱中业气深重，赖珠光照破。不尔，则鬼王于暗中食人心肝，不得出矣。”

    Explanation

    53

    In Confucian texts, the concept of "heaven" is discussed in various ways. For instance, the Spring and Autumn Annals refer to it as "heaven's king," while the Book of Poetry calls it "the sister of heaven" and "the child of heaven." If all these references were to align with your interpretation, heaven would have neither a teacher nor a consort, and how could there be a king, a sister, or a son? Your learning is indeed confined and not thorough, obstructed and hindered. Being confined means being limited to one tool, being obstructed means being stuck in one corner. Not being thorough leads to narrow-mindedness, and being obstructed leads to narrow and biased thinking. Truly, vulgar, corrupt, and absurd people, how can they claim to be Confucian scholars?

    The provincial governor ordered the retrieval of the register of the surname He, marked my name with a red pen, and then annotated it, finishing the task. The provincial governor said, "You should originally be a sixth-rank official, entering and leaving important places. Because you do not believe in gods and Buddhas, and deceive ghosts and spirits, you are specially demoted to a seventh-rank official." I bowed and thanked, and requested to correct my mistakes. The provincial governor said, "This person pretends to agree but disapproves inwardly, and speaks ill of others behind their backs. He should be made to see the prison, to convince his heart." Several soldiers pulled me down and handed me over to a man in yellow robes to take to the provincial office. There was a treasure pagoda, a monk standing beside it, incense, candles, banners, and streamers arranged brightly. The man in yellow robes bowed twice, and I also bowed. The monk opened the pagoda and took out a large pearl, placed it in a golden tray, and the man in yellow robes held it with both hands as we proceeded, all in a dim and dark place. I asked, "Who is the monk?" He said, "He is the Guiding to the Underworld monk." I asked, "What is the purpose of the pearl?" He said, "It is the wish-fulfilling pearl of the Bodhisattva Ksitigarbha. In the prison, the karma is heavy, and it relies on the light of the pearl to dispel it. Otherwise, the ghost king would eat the hearts and livers of people in the dark, and they would not be able to leave."

    54

    “于是首造一狱，曰‘勘治不义之狱’，以砖砌一长槽，满堆炭火，火上焰烨烨然红，呼罪人跪槽边，出火中铁条，大如指，刺入人眼，连十余贯而吊之，如悬槁鱼。黄巾曰：‘此男子在世，不能恭友兄弟，视如秦越，轻灭大伦，惟重财利，受此报也。’次一狱曰：‘勘治不睦之狱’，皆妇人，老少相杂，每人舌上挂一钩，钩上悬一圆石如西瓜，旋转不已，舌出长尺余，痛不可当。黄巾指曰：‘此妇人在世，不能和顺闺门，执守妇道，使夫家分门割户，患若贼仇，受此报也。’东南一狱稍大，谓之‘阎浮总狱’，九流百姓，诸等混杂之人，皆在其中，不令余入也。总狱之北，曰‘剔镂’，绑人于柱，以刀镂之如蓑衣，持小扇煽之，茸茸然动，浇以热醋，绝而复苏，仍沃以水，肉如故，镂十余度。盖世之凶恶，虐害良善者，治于此。

    Explanation

    54

    Then he first created a prison, called the "Prison for Investigating and Punishing Injustice." He built a long trough with bricks and filled it with piles of charcoal. The flames above were brightly red. He called the criminals to kneel by the trough, took out an iron bar from the fire, as big as a finger, and pierced it into their eyes, piercing through more than ten times and hanging them up, like hanging dried fish. The Yellow Turban said, "This man in his lifetime did not respect his brothers, treating them like distant relatives, and disrespected the great bond of kinship, valuing only wealth and profit, and thus received this punishment."

    The next prison was called the "Prison for Investigating and Punishing Discord." All were women, mixed with old and young. Each had a hook hanging from their tongue, with a round stone as big as a watermelon hanging from the hook, continuously spinning. The tongue protruded more than a foot, and the pain was unbearable.

    The southeastern prison was slightly larger, called the Yama's Total Prison. All sorts of people, including scholars, commoners, and various mixed types, were all inside, and no one else was allowed to enter.

    North of the total prison was a place called "Tik Lou," where people were tied to pillars and carved with a knife like a straw cloak. A small fan was held to fan them, moving slightly. Hot vinegar was poured over them, and they died and then revived. Still, water was poured over them, and the flesh remained as before. This was done more than ten times. Those who are extremely wicked and cruel to the good are punished here.

    55

    邻剔镂狱曰‘秽溷’狱，狱尽大粪池，滚沸如汤，臭不可近，鬼以长叉叉人下煮之，出没其间，顷刻溃烂，化为蛆虫，又以竹箩捞蛆于锅中，细炒之，炒辄成灰，仍汲粪汁洒之，复成人，亦十余度。余问‘此治何事？’黄巾曰：‘此世之小人，谤毁君子者，治于此。’已，乃相谓曰：‘不须遍历，直引去那里看了罢！’遂出，逾百步许，入一门，榜曰‘惩戒赃滥’之门，亦大狱也。裸十余人于地，夜叉数辈，状貌狞恶，以铁索牵八九饿鬼来，夜叉抽刀于裸者胸股间割肉，置锅中煎之，以啖饿鬼，啖尽又割，至余筋骨而后已。少焉，业风一吹，肢体如故。又有铁蛇铜犬，咋人血髓，叫苦之声动地，皆人间清要之官，而招权纳赂，欺世盗名，或于任所阳为廉洁，而阴受包苴，或于乡里恃其官势，而吩咐公事，凡瞒人利己之徒，皆在其中。亦有一二与余相识者。

    Explanation

    55

    The hellish realm of Lin Tikou, known as the "filthy latrine" (秽溷), is a place of extreme filth and degradation. The entire realm is a vast pit of human excrement, boiling like soup, with an unbearable stench. Demons use long spears to skewer and boil the condemned, who are plunged into the boiling excrement. They emerge, only to be immediately disintegrated and transformed into maggots. The demons then scoop the maggots from the pot with bamboo baskets, finely fry them, and the maggots turn to ash. The demons sprinkle the excrement on the ash, and the condemned are restored to their original form, a cycle that repeats itself many times.

    I asked, "What is the purpose of this punishment?" Huangjin replied, "This is the place where the wicked of the world, those who slander and defame the virtuous, are punished." He then said, "There is no need to visit all the realms. Let me take you to see another one!"

    We left the "filthy latrine" and walked about a hundred steps before entering another gate, which bore the inscription "Punishment for Corruption and Embezzlement." This was another hellish realm. Several naked individuals were chained to the ground, and several ferocious-looking night demons dragged eight or nine famished ghosts towards them. The demons drew their swords and cut flesh from the naked ones' chests and thighs, placing the meat in a pot to cook and feed the famished ghosts. After devouring the meat, the ghosts were cut again until only bones remained.

    After a short while, the karmic wind blew, and the bodies of the tortured were restored to their original form. There were also iron snakes and copper dogs that bit into the flesh and marrow of the tortured, causing them to cry out in pain, their voices shaking the earth. All of these were high-ranking officials of the world, who had accepted bribes, deceived the world, and stolen fame. Some pretended to be廉洁 while secretly accepting bribes, while others used their official power to interfere in public affairs. All those who deceived others for personal gain were punished in this realm. There were also one or two who were familiar to me.

    56

    “观毕，回省业司，纳珠还僧，赴台复命。台尊又赐训曰：‘今当改过，毋作昔非，若更不悛，罪在不赦。’乃敕黄巾送归，方得去索散行，往冠服司取衣服。黄巾曰：‘公在此相候，吾二人去领符来相送。’食顷，至曰：‘今取捷径，不由旧路矣。’遂同行，出数关，中一关新创，匾曰‘蜉蝣’。把关者知余儒者，俾作《蜉蝣关铭》，余请命名之义，彼曰：‘凡鬼受生人间者，悉从此出，然不久复至，犹蜉蝣朝生夕死然。’余承命撰数语酬之，铭曰：

    有崇者关，镇厚地也。有赫其威，把关吏也。名之蜉蝣，精取义也。凡厥有生，自兹逝也。去未逾时，旋复至也。何殊此虫，一日毙也。南阎浮提，光阴易也。幢幢往来，曷少憩也。请视斯名，悟厥譬也。六道四生，早出离也。逍遥无方，证忉利也。举为天人，关可废也。敬听余铭，发弘誓也。咨尔幽灵，守勿替也。

    Explanation

    56

    After viewing, I returned to the Office of Industry and Commerce, handed over the pearls to the monk, and went to the platform to report. The respected official on the platform gave further instruction: "Now you should correct your mistakes and not repeat past errors. If you do not reform, you will be beyond forgiveness." Then he ordered the Yellow Cap to escort me back, and only then could I leave to seek a wandering life. I went to the Office of Robes and Hats to get my clothes. The Yellow Cap said, "The official will wait for you here. We will go to fetch the document and escort you." After a meal's time, they returned and said, "We are taking a shortcut; we will not be following the old road." We traveled together, passing through several gates. One of the gates was newly built, and its sign read "Mayfly." The gatekeeper, knowing I was a scholar, asked me to compose an inscription for the Mayfly Gate. I asked for the meaning of the name, and he said, "All spirits who are reborn in this world pass through here, but they do not stay long, just like the mayfly that lives for only a day." I composed a few lines in response, and the inscription read:

    "There is a grand gate, stabilizing the thick earth. There is a majestic presence, the gatekeeper. Named 'Mayfly,' it takes its name from its meaning. All beings who are born, depart from here. They do not stay long, soon returning. What is different about this insect, which dies in a day? In the Southern Jambudvipa, time passes quickly. Coming and going, why not rest a little? Please look at this name and understand the analogy. The six realms and four births, escape them early. Wander freely without bounds, attain Tavatimsa. If everyone becomes a celestial being, the gate can be abolished. Hear my inscription, and make a great vow. O spirits, guard and uphold this truth."

    57

    把关者喜，便放余行。至二更，行至家。正见身卧地上，灯照头边，妻子门人，悲啼痛哭。黄巾猛一推余，不觉跌入尸内，恍然而寤矣。”

    其后思明果终知县。所至以清慎自将，并无瑕玷，号称廉洁，盖有所儆云。

    两川都辖院志
    京口吉复卿，唐吉温之后。宋建炎间，有讳深者，补润之金坛尉，遂尔家焉。子孙世为金坛人，以资雄乡邑。人呼吉半州家。复卿生有异质，一目重瞳。与毗陵富室赵得夫、姜彦益为友，交莫逆。复卿气豪，勇于为义。三人尝挟重资，商闽、浙间。时武林妓蒋秋娘、陶玉箫，擅声乐籍。得夫、彦益与昵甚厚，复卿屡劝止之，往来自若。仅二载，囊橐一空。于是言还，再治装而出，买笑缠头，挥金不吝。又期年，罄矣。

    The gatekeeper was pleased and let me go. By the second watch of the night, I arrived home. I saw myself lying on the ground, the lamp lighting my head, while my wife, children, and disciples were weeping and crying.     Later, Si Ming indeed became the magistrate. Wherever he went, he governed with integrity and caution, having no flaws, and was called clean and upright. It seems he was warned in some way.

    Records of the Two Rivers Prefecture

    Ji Fucheng of Jingkou was a descendant of Tang Jiwen. During the Jianyan period of the Song dynasty, there was a man named Shen who was appointed as the military governor of Jintan and thus settled there. His descendants have lived in Jintan for generations, being wealthy and influential in their hometown. People called him the Ji Half-State family. Fucheng was born with an unusual appearance, having a double pupil in one eye. He befriended Zhao Defu and Jiang Yanyi, wealthy men of Piling, and they were inseparable friends. Fucheng was bold and generous, brave in doing what was right. The three of them once carried a large sum of money and traded between Fujian and Zhejiang. At that time, Jiang Qiuniang and Tao Yuxiao, courtesans of Wulin, were renowned for their singing and dancing. Zhao Defu and Jiang Yanyi were very close to them, and Fucheng repeatedly tried to stop them, but they continued as before. Only two years later, their bags were empty. They decided to return, prepared again, and set out, buying laughter and entertainment, spending money freely. Another year passed, and they were all spent.

    58

    二人私议，悉货产业，载以适武林。门户老小，皆不顾。复卿患之，百喻莫听。怒而入闽，置酒与别，席间苦口规谏曰：“吾与子既为深交，安可缄默，药石之箴，朋友之责，纵人微言轻，弗能感悟，二公独不为妻子计乎？” 则佯应之曰：“兄言是，吾辈知所警矣。”复卿寓福州，生理如意，荏苒三秋，才方返棹。比过钱塘，首访二子，遇之于途。憔悴其形，褴褛其服，几不相识，握手道左，不任唏嘘！复卿即拉诣舟中，易以美衣，饮以醇醪，慰劳再三，情礼交至。
    二人泣数行下曰：“余惟不用兄言，故至于此，然悔无及矣。所恨烟花泼贱，乃大无情，吾二人万金之资，因渠破荡。昨过其门，如不相识，麾叱使去。惧为己羞，必杀之而后已。”复卿解之曰：“二公平生遨游花街柳陌中，岂不知彼门庭如此，尚奚怒为？人命至重，切不可辄兴恶念，但早收拾回归。

    Explanation

    58

    The two privately discussed, sold all their property, and loaded up to go to Wulin. Ignoring their doors, the old and the young, Fu Qing was concerned about it, but he could not persuade them with a hundred analogies. Angered, he went to Fujian, set up a banquet to say goodbye, and at the banquet, earnestly advised, saying: "Since we are close friends, how can I remain silent? Admonitions like medicine and stones, the duty of a friend. Even if my words are light and my person insignificant, I cannot move them. Do the two of you not consider your wives and children?" Then they feigned agreement, saying: "Brother, your words are right; we now know what to be cautious of." Fu Qing settled in Fuzhou, his livelihood going well. After three autumns, he finally returned. When passing by Qiantang, he first visited the two, meeting them on the road. Their appearance was haggard, their clothes ragged, almost unrecognizable. Holding hands on the side of the road, unable to hold back tears, Fu Qing immediately pulled them to the boat, changed them into fine clothes, and had them drink strong wine. Comforted and praised repeatedly, showing both emotion and courtesy.

    The two wept, saying: "We only did not follow your advice, so we ended up like this, but it's too late to regret. We regret that the courtesans are so heartless, squandering our wealth of ten thousand gold coins. Yesterday, when we passed their door, they acted as if they didn't recognize us and ordered us to leave. Afraid it would bring shame to themselves, they must kill us to end it." Fu Qing explained, saying: "You two have always roamed the flower streets and willow alleys, how could you not know their ways? Why should you be angry? Human life is precious, do not rashly harbor evil thoughts. Just pack up and return home."

    59

    若要本钱，此间一一应付，古人谓朋友有通财之义，若只衔杯酒，逐嬉游，贫穷不相恤，患难不相顾，犬彘将不食其肉，尚可谓之人哉？”于是各以二万假之。二人挈所得，又复过妓者之家，妓见其衣巾整饬，颜色光华，颇以为讶，款待如旧。复卿促之回，二人绐曰： “容略收拾，少候数时，万一有干，宜在先发。”复卿曰：“嘻，是何言欤！我若一去，子必不能动身；便一两月，亦须等候，岂敢相抛耶？”无何，彦益遇疾，卧于妓家。得夫日往扶持，亦染其症，未浃旬，相继殒殁。复卿往哭尽哀，缯衣漆棺，殓皆如礼，仍刲羊酾酒设祭，暂殡于灵隐寺僧舍。比开舟，又携酒肴往奠，赋诗悼之，诗曰：

    生死交情不敢亏，一杯重奠泪双垂。游魂好共故人去，莫向东风怨子规。

    Explanation

    59

    If one needs capital, it can be provided here comprehensively. The ancients said that friends should share resources. If one only indulges in drinking and leisurely pursuits, neglecting each other in times of poverty and hardship, even dogs and pigs would not eat their flesh—how can they still be called human?" Thus, each lent them twenty thousand. The two, carrying what they had gained, passed by the courtesan's home again. The courtesan, seeing their clothes and hats neat and their appearance radiant, was quite surprised but treated them as before. Fu Qing urged them to return, but the two lied, saying, "Let me tidy up a bit and wait a few moments. In case there is any trouble, it's better to leave early." Fu Qing said, "Ah, what are you saying! If I leave, you surely cannot move. Even a month or two, you must wait, how could I abandon you?" Soon after, Yan Yi fell ill and lay in the courtesan's home. De Fu visited daily to support him, but also contracted the same illness. Within a few days, they died one after another. Fu Qing went to mourn them with deep sorrow, dressing them in fine silk and placing them in a lacquered coffin, all according to proper rites. He still slaughtered a sheep, poured wine, and set up an offering, temporarily burying them in the Lingyin Temple's monk's quarters. When it was time to set sail, he again brought wine and food to pay respects, composing a poem to mourn them, which reads:

    "Bound by lifelong friendship, I dare not betray. A cup of wine, double tears flow. May the wandering soul go with the old friend. Do not blame the east wind for the cuckoo's cry."

    人间急景似飞梭，枉费黄金买笑歌。断雨残云休更念，相携莲座礼弥陀。

    The fleeting moments of life pass like a shuttle, wasting gold to buy laughter and songs. Do not think of the broken rain and scattered clouds anymore, and together on the lotus seat, worship Amitabha.

    Tired from dancing and songs, yet unwilling to stop, splendor does not stay for the young. If only I had known there would be no place to bury the white bones, cherish gold to buy a mound of earth.

    After offering wine, untie the rope. After returning home for a month, immediately went to Pizhou to see the wife and children, explaining the cause of death, detailing the funeral arrangements. He consoled them, saying, "My honorable husband's remains will be taken back to your noble hometown after I pass through Hangzhou, seeking a blessed place for burial. Do not worry." Later, Fu Qing successfully traded in Zhejiang, making tenfold profits. He personally visited Lingyin Temple, opening the coffin, placing the remains in a small wooden box, and bringing them back to buy land in Wuxi for burial. All expenses were covered by Fu Qing. He also invited monks to hold a three-day and three-night water and land feast to offer blessings to the dead, and his noble character and high friendship spread throughout the rivers and lakes.

    61

    俄值元末丧乱，人咸汹汹，复卿无以为计，默坐于家。忽得夫、彦益联袂而来，复卿忘其死也，欣然相接。彦益曰：“公何燕居深念，似有重忧？”复卿告以故。两人同应曰：“无妨，吾已请命上天，令率阴灵卫公宅眷。”言讫隐形，方悟其死。自尔，复卿之家，虽出入兵戈中，鲜遇惊恐，安然如平时。至洪武己酉，寿八十一，无疾而终。

    又二年壬子，同县徐建寅为四川苍溪丞，于山中见旌旗甲马，从者百余，气象甚都。谓是上司官员，立道傍，候其过。至则复卿也，顾徐曰：“闻尔哦松此邑，久欲一见。”便下马叙话，问乡曲及其家事甚详。徐于复卿为通家子，因再拜问曰：“姻丈谢世以来，服已阕矣，何得若是？”复卿云：“上帝以余薄有阴骘，命为两川都辖院主者。职事尊重，全蜀土地社公，及不入祀典神祇，悉听节制。前村古宇，吾所治也，部下判官四，今尚缺二员，已奏保得夫、彦益矣，早晚将至。子当为吾修葺庙貌，吾当为国福祐生灵。

    Explanation

    61

    Suddenly, at the end of the Yuan dynasty, chaos erupted, and people were all agitated. Fu Qing had no plan, so he sat silently at home. Suddenly, Dufu and Yan Yi came together, and Fu Qing forgot his death, meeting them with joy. Yan Yi said, "Why are you deeply contemplating while living in peace, as if you have a great worry?" Fu Qing told him the reason. The two replied together, "It's not a problem. We have already requested a command from heaven, ordering the spirits to protect your family." After speaking, they disappeared, and Fu Qing realized they were dead. From then on, although Fu Qing's household was often in the midst of military conflicts, they rarely encountered fear, and they lived peacefully as usual. In the year Jiyou of the Hongwu era, he lived to be eighty-one and died without illness.

    Two years later, in the year Renzi, Xu Jianyin, who was from the same county and served as the magistrate of Cangxi in Sichuan, saw flags and armored horses in the mountains, with over a hundred followers, and the scene was very impressive. He thought they were officials from a higher rank, so he stood by the road, waiting for them to pass. When they arrived, it was Fu Qing. Fu Qing looked at Xu and said, "I heard you in Oh Song in this town, and I have wanted to see you for a long time." Then he dismounted and talked with Xu, asking him in great detail about the affairs of the village and his family. Xu was related by marriage to Fu Qing, so he bowed twice and asked, "Uncle-in-law, since you passed away, the mourning period is over. How can it be like this?" Fu Qing said, "Heaven has appointed me as the head of the court of jurisdiction in the two Sichuans because I have some merit. My duties are respected, and all the local deities of Sichuan, as well as the deities not included in the ritual calendar, are subject to my control. The ancient buildings in the village ahead are under my jurisdiction. I have four judges under my command, but two are still missing. I have already recommended Dufu and Yan Yi, and they will arrive soon. You should repair the temple for me, and I will bless the country and its people."

    62

    况尔少年，乍到官守，非吾阴相，曷致声名？”徐拱手请教。复卿曰：“廉、恕两字符也。惟廉可以律身，惟恕可以近民，廉则心有养，恕则民易亲，民亲化行，能事毕矣。”语讫，策马去，其疾如飞。徐惘然，前至村落，果有故祠一所，峙于山椒。询之乡老，曰：“此都辖相公庙也，多年颓圮，近间，稍稍有人见骑马导从，出入其中，颇著灵响。老夫辈拟新其栋宇，尚未兴工。”徐丞闻之喜，告以见复卿事，即劝成之，兼助其费，专委县吏邹忠董其役。未几而完，仍揭旧额，塑复卿象于堂中，肖得夫、彦益于东西庑。遣人走夔州，求太守盛南金文，刻碑序公事迹。由是威惠大振，利泽昭彰，远方之民，水旱疾疫，祷辄立应。

    62

    As for you, young man, just arrived in office, if not for my unseen assistance, how could you achieve fame?” Xu bowed his hands in respect and asked for guidance. Fu Qing replied, “Integrity and forgiveness are the two essential virtues. Only integrity can govern oneself, and only forgiveness can approach the people. Integrity nurtures the heart, and forgiveness makes the people easier to befriend. When the people are befriended, transformation follows, and all tasks are completed.” After speaking, he rode away on horseback, as swift as flying. Xu was bewildered, and as he proceeded to a village, he indeed found an old shrine standing on a mountain peak. He inquired of the village elders, who said, “This is the shrine of the Right Minister Gongfu, which has been in ruins for many years. Recently, there have been occasional sightings of someone riding with attendants, entering and exiting within it. It is quite famous for its spiritual influence. We old men plan to renovate its structure, but work has not yet begun.” Xu, the magistrate, was pleased upon hearing this and informed them about his encounter with Fu Qing. He immediately urged them to complete the renovation and also helped with the expenses, entrusting the county official Zou Zhong to supervise the work. Shortly after, the renovation was completed, and the old name was retained. A statue of Fu Qing was placed in the main hall, and statues of De Fu and Yan Yi were placed in the eastern and western wings. Someone was sent to Kuizhou to seek an inscription from Governor Sheng Nangjin, which was carved on a stele to chronicle his deeds. Therefore, his authority and benevolence greatly increased, and his benefits became widely known. People from distant places, facing floods, droughts, diseases, and epidemics, found that their prayers were answered immediately.

    63

    后徐任满，便道过家，访复卿二子元礼、元信，首及兹事，元礼曰：“余兄弟向梦二人言，蒙尊公谬举为两川都辖院判官，来日起程，敬诣拜别。近有至自毗陵者，能言其家，亦得梦如此，皆莫晓所谓。今闻公所说，则悟先子之为神，而于二君，亦可谓生死而骨肉者也。”明年，徐再任，往竭于庙，则丹碧辉煌，于时有耀，牲牢酒楮，祭日无虚，处处村村，家家户户，莫不虔诚礼拜，冀沾福惠。迨今神迹显著，香火不绝云。

    连理树记
    上官守愚者，扬州江都人。为奎章阁授经郎时，居顺天。馆东与国史检讨贾虚中为邻。贾，柯敬仲友也，工诗善画。家藏古琴三张，曰“琼瑶音”、“环佩音”、蓬莱音”，皆敬仲所鉴定。守愚亦雅好吟咏，兼嗜绿绮，与贾交游特厚。每休暇过从，诗酒琴棋，从容竟日。贾无嗣，止三女，尝曰：“吾三女可比三琴。” 遂取琴名名女焉。守愚子粹，甚清俊聪敏，生时人送《唐文粹》一部，故小字粹奴。年十岁，因遣就贾学，贾夫妇爱之如子，三女亦视之犹兄弟，呼为粹舍。尝与其幼女蓬莱同读书学画，深相爱重。贾妻戏之曰：“使蓬莱他日得婿如粹舍足矣。”归以告，守愚曰：“吾意正然。”遣媒言议，各已许诺。粹二人亦私喜不胜。不期贾忽罢归，姻事竟弗谐。

    Explanation

    64

    The Story of the Twin-Rooted Tree

    Shangguan Shouyu, a native of Jiangdu, Yangzhou, served as a teaching official at the Kuizhang Pavilion in Shuntian. He lived near Guo Shitan, a historian and scholar named Jia Xuzhong, who was a close friend of Ke Jingzhong. Jia was skilled in poetry and painting. He owned three ancient zithers named "Qiongyaoyin," "Huanpeiyin," and "Penglaiyin," all of which had been authenticated by Ke Jingzhong. Shouyu also had a refined appreciation for poetry and music, particularly the green qin, and he had a particularly close friendship with Jia. Whenever they had leisure time, they would gather to drink, play music, and enjoy poetry and chess, spending the entire day in pleasant conversation.

    Jia had no male heir, only three daughters. He once said, "My three daughters can be compared to these three zithers." He then named his daughters after the zithers. Shouyu's son, Cui, was exceptionally intelligent and talented. When he was born, people gave him a copy of Tang Wencui, a collection of Tang Dynasty writings, hence his nickname "Cui Nu." At the age of ten, he was sent to study under Jia. Jia and his wife loved him as if he were their own son, and Jia's three daughters treated him as a brother, calling him "Cui She." He often studied and painted with Jia's youngest daughter, Penglai, and they deeply cared for each other. Jia's wife once teased him, saying, "If Penglai were to marry someone like Cui She in the future, she would be satisfied." She told her husband about this, and Shouyu agreed, saying, "That is exactly my intention." They arranged for a matchmaker to discuss the matter, and both families agreed to the marriage. Cui and Penglai were privately overjoyed. However, unexpectedly, Jia suddenly resigned and returned home, and the marriage plans ultimately failed to materialize.

    后三年，守愚出为福州治中。始至，僦居民舍，得楼三楹，而对街一楼，尤清雅。问之，乃贾氏宅也。守愚即日往坊，则琼瑶、环佩已适人，惟蓬莱在室，亦许婚林氏矣。粹闻之，悒怏殊甚！蓬莱虽为父母许他姓，然亦非其意也。知粹至，欲一会而未由，彼此时时凝立楼栏，相视不能发语。蓬莱一日以白练帕裹象棋子掷粹。粹接视之，上画绯桃，题一诗曰：

    65

    Three years later, 守愚 was appointed as the Governor of Fuzhou. Upon his arrival, he rented a house occupied by residents and obtained a building with three rooms. Opposite the street was another building, which was particularly elegant. He asked about it, and it turned out to be the house of the family 贾. 守愚 immediately went to the neighborhood, where he learned that 琼瑶 and 环佩 had already been married, while 蓬莱 was still unmarried but had been betrothed to the family 林. 粹 heard about this and was very depressed! Although 蓬莱 had been betrothed to another family by her parents, it was not her wish. Knowing that 粹 had arrived, she wanted to meet him but had no opportunity to do so. She often stood fixedly by the railing of the building, looking at him but unable to speak. One day, 蓬莱 wrapped the chess pieces in a white silk scarf and threw them to 粹. 粹 received and looked at them, and on the top was painted a red peach with a poem written on it:

    1. Idiomatic Expressions

    • 守愚出为福州治中 - "守愚" is a name, and "治中" is an official title, meaning "Governor of Fuzhou." The phrase indicates that the person named 守愚 was appointed as the Governor of Fuzhou.
    • 僦居民舍 - "僦" means to rent, and "居民舍" means a house occupied by residents. The phrase means "to rent a house occupied by residents."
    • 对街一楼，尤清雅 - "对街" means opposite the street, and "尤清雅" means especially elegant or refined. The phrase describes a house opposite the street that is particularly elegant.
    • 问之，乃贾氏宅也 - "问之" means to ask about it, and "乃贾氏宅也" means it is the house of the family 贾. The phrase indicates that the house is owned by the family 贾.
    • 即日往坊 - "即日" means immediately, and "往坊" means to go to the neighborhood. The phrase means "to go to the neighborhood immediately."
    • 琼瑶、环佩已适人 - "琼瑶" and "环佩" are names, and "适人" means to be married. The phrase means that 琼瑶 and 环佩 have already been married.
    • 惟蓬莱在室，亦许婚林氏矣 - "惟蓬莱" means only 蓬莱, "在室" means unmarried, and "许婚林氏矣" means has been betrothed to the family 林. The phrase means that only 蓬莱 is still unmarried but has been betrothed to the family 林.
    • 悒怏殊甚 - "悒怏" means depressed or gloomy, and "殊甚" means very much. The phrase means "very depressed."
    • 彼此时时凝立楼栏 - "彼" means she, "时时" means often, and "凝立楼栏" means to stand fixedly by the railing of the building. The phrase means "she often stands fixedly by the railing of the building."
    • 相视不能发语 - "相视" means to look at each other, and "不能发语" means unable to speak. The phrase means "unable to speak to each other."
    • 蓬莱一日以白练帕裹象棋子掷粹 - "蓬莱" is a name, "一日" means one day, "以白练帕裹象棋子" means to wrap the chess pieces in a white silk scarf, and "掷粹" means to throw them to 粹. The phrase means "one day, 蓬莱 wrapped the chess pieces in a white silk scarf and threw them to 粹."
    • 上画绯桃 - "上画" means on the top is painted, and "绯桃" means red peach. The phrase means "on the top is painted a red peach."
    • 题一诗曰 - "题一诗" means to write a poem, and "曰" means saying. The phrase means "to write a poem saying."

    2. Cultural and Historical Allusions

    • 守愚 - A name, likely a personal name of a historical figure or a fictional character.
    • 福州治中 - An official title, meaning "Governor of Fuzhou," indicating a high-ranking administrative position.
    • 贾氏宅 - Refers to the house of the family 贾, a common surname in Chinese history.

    66

    朱砂颜色瓣重台，曾是刘晨旧看来。只好天台云里种，莫教移近俗人栽。

    粹识其意，然静而思之，彼业已定矣，莫如之何。亦画梅花一枝，写诗以复，诗曰：

    玉蕊含春捏素罗，岁寒心事谅无他。纵令肯作仙郎伴，其奈孤山处士何？

    用彩绳系琴轸三枚，坠之，投还蓬莱。蓬莱展看有“孤山处士”之说，知其谓己订盟林氏，衷情不白，惟闷闷而已。

    未逾时，值上元节，闽俗放灯甚盛，男女纵观。粹察贾氏宅眷必往，乃潜伺于其门。更深人静，果有舆夫舁轿数乘而前，蓬莱与母三四辈上轿，婢妾追随，相续不绝。粹尾其后，过十余街，度不得见，乃行吟轿傍曰：

    天遣香街静处逢，银灯影里见惊鸿。彩舆亦似蓬山隔，鸾自西飞鹤自东。

    蓬莱知其粹也，欲呼与语，诉其所怀，而从者纷纭，不敢启口，亦于轿中微吟曰：

    Explanation

    66

    The petals of the flower are red like cinnabar and layered like a peony, having been admired by Liu Chen in the past. It is best to plant it in the clouds of Tian Tai Mountain; do not allow common people to cultivate it.

    The woman understood the meaning of the flower, but upon reflecting quietly, she realized that its fate was already determined, and there was nothing she could do about it. She also painted a branch of plum blossoms and wrote a poem in response, which said:

    The white petals of the flower hold the essence of spring, as if made of fine silk, and its integrity remains unchanged through the harshness of winter. Even if it were to become a companion to a fairy, what can be done about the solitary scholar who appreciates it but remains isolated?

    She tied three tuning pegs of a qin with colored cords, dropped them, and sent them back to Penglai. Upon seeing the phrase "solitary scholar of Solitary Mountain," Penglai understood that it referred to her own alliance with the Lin family, where her true feelings remained unspoken, and she could only feel disheartened.

    Not long after, it was the Lantern Festival, and the custom in Fujian of setting up many lanterns was particularly grand, attracting large crowds. The woman observed that the household of the Jia family would surely attend, so she secretly waited outside their gate. When the night deepened and the area grew quiet, indeed, several sedan chairs were carried forward by bearers, and Penglai, along with her mother and a few others, entered the sedan chairs, followed by maids and servants, continuing without interruption. The woman followed behind, passing through more than ten streets, and realizing she could not see them, she began to recite poetry by the side of the sedan chair:

    Fate brought us together in a quiet, fragrant street, and I saw a beautiful and unexpected sight in the shadow of silver lamps. Even the colorful sedan chair seemed distant, like the mythical Penglai Mountain, and the paths of the phoenix and the crane diverged, symbolizing separation or different destinies.

    Penglai recognized the woman as well and wanted to call out to her and speak of her feelings, but the crowd around her was too chaotic, and she dared not open her mouth. Instead, she softly recited a poem from inside the sedan chair:

    67

    莫向梅花怨薄情，梅花肯负岁寒盟！调羹欲问真消息，已许风流宋广平。

    粹听之，知其答己梅花之作，不觉感叹！归坐楼中，念蓬莱之意虽坚，而林氏之聘，终不可改。乃赋《凤分飞》曲以寄之曰：

    梧桐凝露鲜飙起，五色琅玕夜新洗。矫翮蹁跹拟并栖，九苞文彩如霞绮。惊飞忽作丹山别，弄玉箫声怨呜咽。咫尺秦台隔弱流，琐窗绣户空明月。皞皞扫尾仪朝阳，可怜相望不相将！下谪尘寰伴凡鸟，不如交颈两鸳鸯。

    诗成，无便寄去，忽贾遣婢送荔子一盘来，粹诡曰：“往在都下，与蓬莱同学，有书数册未取，以此帖呈之，俾早送见还也。”婢不悟是诗，持去，递与蓬莱，读之，垂泣曰：“嗟乎！郎尚不余谅也。”乃作《龙剑合》曲答之，示终身相从之意，写以鱼笺，密置《古文真宝》中，付婢绿荷曰：“粹舍取旧所读诗，此是也，汝持去还之。”婢送粹所，揭之，中有笺烂然，知必诗也，题曰《龙剑合》曲。词曰：

    68

    龙剑埋没狱间久，巨灵昼卫鬼夜守。蛟螭藏，魍魉走，精光横天气射斗。冲玄云，发金钥，至宝稀世有。奇姿烁人声撼牖，鹈膏润锷凤刻首。龙剑煌，新离房，静垂流电舞飞霜，影含秋水刃拂铓，？ 团金宝珠装。司空观之识其良，悬诸玉带间金章，紫焰煌煌明瑀珰，星折中台事岂常！逡巡莫敢住，一去堕渺茫。龙灵是龙精，莹如鹇尾摇清冰。雄作万里别，雌伤千古情，暂留尘埃匣，何日可合并？会当逐风雷，相寻入延平。纯钩在奉必，纵然贵重非我匹。我匹久卧潭水云，一双遥怜两地分。度山仍越壑，苦辛不可言。天遣雷焕儿，佩之大泽濆。铿然一跃同骏奔，骇浪惊涛白昼昏。始知神物自有耦，千秋万岁肯离群。

    68

    The Dragon Sword, hidden in the depths of the abyss for a long time, is guarded by the giant spirit during the day and the ghosts at night. Dragons and serpents hide, and spirits flee, as the sword's brilliance pierces the sky and reaches the stars. It breaks through the clouds, unlocks treasures, and is a rare treasure in the world. Its unique appearance and the sound it makes when drawn are awe-inspiring, with its blade polished like oil and its hilt adorned with phoenix motifs. The Dragon Sword shines brightly, recently emerging from its sheath, gracefully moving like a flowing lightning and flying frost, with its reflection in the autumn water and the sharpness of its edge. The hilt is decorated with golden beads and precious jewels. The high official recognizes its excellence, hanging it on a jade belt with a gold seal, and its purple flame illuminates the jade pendants, suggesting a significant event. No one dares to stop it as it departs, disappearing into the unknown. The spirit of the sword is as clear and pure as a white bird's tail swaying in clear ice. The male spirit separates from the female spirit, with the female spirit feeling a deep sorrow, and the male spirit temporarily stays in a dust-filled box, wondering when they will reunite. It will follow the wind and rain to find the female spirit in the Yandang region. Even if it is highly valued, it is not a match for the male spirit. The male spirit's counterpart has been lying in a deep pool of water and clouds, separated by great distance, and the male spirit longs for her. The journey across mountains and valleys is filled with hardship and suffering. The heavens send a descendant of Lei Huan to wear the sword in the vast marshes. The sword is drawn with a resounding sound, causing the waves and tides to rise and the day to become dark. It is realized that divine objects have their counterparts and will not be separated for eternity.

    粹读之曰：“清才丽句，无妇人女子萎苶之气，宛然李青莲之韵度也。是岂寻常庸碌者之配哉？”

    俄而闽中大疫，蓬莱所议林生竟死。贾夫妇知粹未婚，乃遗人报守愚求终好，守愚欣跃从之。六礼既备，亲迎有期。花烛之夕，粹与蓬莱相见，不啻若仙降也。因各赋诗一首以志喜，时至正十九年己亥二月八日也。粹诗曰：

    Cui read it and said: "The elegant and refined poetic expressions, without the weak and frail spirit of women and girls, exactly match the elegance and style of Li Bai. How could this be matched with an ordinary and mediocre person?"

    Soon, a great epidemic broke out in Fujian, and the man discussed by Penglai, Lin, died. Jia's couple knew that Cui was unmarried, so they sent someone to inform Shouyu and seek a match. Shouyu was delighted and agreed. After the six marriage rituals were completed, the wedding was scheduled. On the night of the wedding, when the candles were lit, Cui met Shouyu, and it was as if a deity had descended.     70

    海棠开处燕来时，折得东风第一枝。鸳枕且酬交颈愿，鱼笺莫赋断肠词。桃花染帕春先逗，柳叶舒黄画未迟。不用同心双结带，新人原是旧相知。

    蓬莱诗曰：

    与君相见即相怜，有分终须到底圆。旧女婿为新女婿，恶因缘化好因缘。秋波浅浅银灯下，春笋纤纤玉镜前。天遣赤绳先系足，从今唤作并头莲。

    蓬莱自入上官之门，孝事舅姑，恭顺夫子，一家内外，罔不称贤。暇则与粹唱和诗词，娱情琴画，平生所作，编成一集，粹题之曰《絮雪稿》，且为序于首简。诗与序多不录，姑载一二以传好事者：

    △闺怨

    露颗珠团团，冰肌玉钏寒。杏梁栖只燕，菱镜掩孤鸾。残树枯黄遍，圆荷湿翠干。绣奁生画色，窗下带愁看。△白苎词二首

    茜裙紫袖映猩红，飞絮轻飏桃花风。缓歌白苎捧玉钟，娇音芳韵绕帘栊，梁尘飞堕云凝空。秋波回目蛾扫黛，余声悠扬歇还在。歌当细听杯当再，绿鬓朱颜能久待！

    Explanation

    70

    When the crabapple blossoms bloom and the swallows arrive, I pluck the first branch of the east wind. Let us share the pillow of mandarin ducks and fulfill our wish for a close and affectionate relationship; do not write sad or sorrowful letters. Peach blossoms dye the handkerchief, hinting at the arrival of spring; it's not too late to paint the yellow willow leaves. There is no need for a double-knot belt symbolizing unity, for the new person is actually an old acquaintance.

    The poem of Penglai says:

    When I meet you, I immediately cherish you; if there is a destined connection, it will eventually come to fruition. The old son-in-law becomes a new son-in-law, and bad karma is transformed into good karma. Under the light of a silver lamp, the gentle gaze is soft, and in front of a jade mirror, the young, tender bamboo shoots are graceful. Heaven has already tied us together with a red thread, and from now on, we will be like lotus flowers growing together.

    Since entering the household of the official, she has been filial to her in-laws and respectful to her husband. Within and without the family, she is universally praised as virtuous. In her spare time, she engages in poetry and verse with her husband, finds joy in music and painting, and has compiled all her works into a collection titled Xuexue Gao (Drafts of Snowflakes), with a preface written by her husband. Many of the poems and prefaces are not recorded here, but a few are included to amuse those who appreciate such things:

    △ Gū Yuàn (Grief of a Woman)

    Pearl-like dewdrops form round clusters, the ice-like skin and jade bracelet are cold. A solitary swallow roosts on the apricot beam, the square mirror conceals a lonely phoenix. The remaining trees are covered in withered yellow, the round lotus leaves are damp and green. The embroidered chest opens to reveal the colors of a painting, and I look out the window with a heart full of sorrow.

    △ Bái Zhù Cí (Two Poems on White Cotton)

    The crimson red of the foxglove and the purple sleeves are reflected in the pink wind of the peach blossoms. Slowly singing Bái Zhù, holding the jade bell, the sweet voice and fragrant melody linger around the curtains, the dust on the beams falls like clouds, and the air is filled with a sense of emptiness. The gentle gaze returns, and the eyebrows are swept with black ink, the lingering sound remains. The song should be listened to carefully, and the cup should be filled again, for the green hair and red face can last for a long time.

    71

    响如苍玉触鸣玑，蹁跹锦袖红地衣。回风激雪当世稀，翻身按节疾如飞。香尘蒙蒙发委坠，玳筵夜静纱灯晦，鲛绡湿透胭脂泪。△春晓曲

    Explanation

    71

    春晓曲

    The sound is as clear as jade striking a jade disc, and the movements are graceful like a brocade sleeve on a red carpet. A swirling wind and flying snow are rare in this world, and the quick, agile turns are as swift as a dancer. Fine dust scatters, and the banquet is quiet, with a dimly lit gauzy lamp. The delicate fabric is wet with tears, as if stained by rouge. △Spring Morning Song

    秋夜曲

    The thin ice reflection in the fragrant pond, and the sweet, delicate bird songs in the curved veranda. The cold, red silk cushion in front of the mirror, and the fading of her eyebrows and green makeup.     咏蝶

    The dew on the fragrant orchid is heavy, and a cool breeze moves through the gauzy curtain. A wooden box containing fragrant silk, and a quilted bedcover, asking who will share it? The extinguishing of a silver lamp, and she removes a green flower-shaped ornament. △Song of Butterflies

    谢大姊惠鞋

    Lotus petals are sent far away, and the brocade robe still carries the scent of her fingers. The bow-shaped object is so well-fitted that it leaves no marks, and she stands alone in the shade of flowers, watching the formation of geese. △Song of Twin-Lipped Litchi

    园中咏菜

    Plants grow with connected stems, and the divine order is evident. A woman in a secluded room, weary and pale, sees something that evokes strong emotions. △Song of Vegetables in the Garden

    满圃绿纤纤，芳苗雨后添。惟应穷措大，咬得寸根甜。

    72

    粹时才名藉甚，当道有欲荐之者，蓬莱苦口止之曰：“今风尘道梗，望都下如在天上，君岂可舍父母之养，而远赴功名之途乎？独不见王儒仲妻之言曰： ‘令狐子伯之贵，孰与君之高哉？’”粹然之，亦无意于出，乃以亲老辞。次年，治中物故。又明年，为至正壬寅，闽城为盗所据，城中大姓多避匿山谷，粹亦挈家遁。盗踪迹得之，尽戕其一门。留蓬莱一人不杀，将以为妻。蓬莱知不免，绐盗曰：“我一家尽死，无所于归，将军纵舍我，我亦何以为生乎？愿事将军终身，乞埋其故夫，然后相从未晚也。”盗喜从之，同至尸所，拔佩刀为掘一坑，掘讫，植刀于地，坐于旁曰：“吾倦矣！吾倦矣！”目蓬莱，使取刀抄土掩之。蓬莱即举刀自刎曰：“死作一处，无恨也。”盗遽起夺刀，已绝咽矣。盗怒曰：“汝死则死，我定不教汝死作一处。”遂埋蓬莱二十步外，使两冢相望。

    Explanation

    72

    Cui was renowned for his talent, and officials in power had plans to recommend him. Penglai, however, strongly advised against it, saying, "Now the roads are blocked by dust and thorns, and looking toward the capital is like looking at the sky. How can you abandon the care of your parents to pursue the path of fame and achievement? Haven't you heard the words of Wang Ruzhong's wife, who said, 'The high status of Lihufu, how does it compare to the virtue of staying with your family?'"

    Cui heeded her advice and had no intention of leaving. He declined the opportunity, citing the need to care for his elderly parents. The following year, the magistrate died. Another year later, in the year 1352 of the Yuan dynasty, the city of Fujian was seized by bandits. The city's prominent families fled to remote mountains and valleys, and Cui also took his family to hide. The bandits tracked them down and massacred the entire family. They spared one person, named Penglai, intending to make her their wife. Penglai knew she could not escape and deceived the bandit, saying, "My entire family is dead, and I have nowhere to go. Even if you spare me, how can I live? I wish to serve you for life. Please allow me to bury my deceased husband, and then I will follow you."

    The bandit leader was pleased and agreed. They went to the place where Cui's body lay. The bandit leader pulled out his dagger and began digging a pit. When the pit was finished, he placed the dagger on the ground and sat beside it, saying, "I am tired! I am tired!" He looked at Penglai and instructed her to take the knife and cover the grave. Penglai immediately raised the knife and cut her throat, saying, "Die together, and there will be no regret." The bandit leader quickly stood up to seize the knife, but she had already choked to death. Angered, he said, "You may die, but I will not let you die together with your family." He then buried Penglai twenty steps away, making sure the two graves faced each other.

    73

    其年，燕只普化为福建行省平章，乃集诸县民兵克城，民方复业。又数年，有同避寇者，始备说蓬莱事。平章遣人视之，将以礼改葬；至则两墓之上，各生一树相向，枝连柯抱，纠结不可解。使者归报，平章亲往视之，果不谬。乃不敢发，但加修葺，仍设奠祭焉。人呼为连理冢树，闽人至今称之不绝。

    Explanation

    73

    In that year, Yan Zhihua became the Governor of Fujian Province. He gathered the militia from various counties to pacify the city, and the people were just beginning to resume their livelihoods. After several more years, those who had fled from the bandits began to fully recount the events of the Penglai incident. The Governor sent someone to inspect the site, intending to rebury the remains according to ritual. Upon arrival, they found that on top of the two graves, each had grown a tree facing one another, with branches and trunks intertwined and inseparable. The messenger returned to report this, and the Governor personally went to inspect the site, confirming that it was indeed true. He then decided not to disturb the graves but instead repaired them and offered sacrifices. The people called these trees the "Twin Trunk Tomb Trees," and the people of Fujian continue to speak of them to this day.

    74

    田洙遇薛涛联句记
    五羊田洙，字孟沂。洪武十七年甲子四月，随父百禄赴蜀成都教官。洙清雅有标致，书画琴棋，靡所不晓。诸生日与嬉游，爱之逾于同气。凡远近名山胜境，吟赏殆遍。尝曰：“吾平生懒事声利，但长得好处登临足矣！”明年秋，百禄将遣回，洙母不忍舍。乃曰：“儿来未久，奈何使去？且官清毡冷，路费艰难，公宜再思。”百禄乃谋于诸生之亲厚者，使开馆于人家，一则自可读书进学，一则藉俸金为归计。诸生深幸洙留，遂荐于附郭大姓张氏。次岁丙寅正月十八日设帐，庠序朋好，群送以往。张大喜，开宴，待为上宾，且谓百禄曰：“令嗣晚间免回，可令就宿舍下。”百禄许之。

    Explanation

    74

    Meeting Record of Tian Shu and Xue Tao**

    Tian Shu of Wuyang, courtesy name Mengyi, accompanied his father Baolu to serve as a teaching official in Chengdu, Sichuan, in the fourth month of the year 1384 (the 17th year of the Hongwu era). Tian Shu was clear and elegant in appearance, knowledgeable in calligraphy, painting, music, and chess. His classmates often played with him and loved him more than their own blood. He had visited and appreciated famous mountains and scenic spots far and near. He once said, "All my life I have been lazy about seeking fame and profit; as long as I can find good places to climb and look around, that is enough!" The following autumn, Baolu was planning to send him back, but Tian Shu's mother did not want to let him go. She said, "He has only been here for a short time; why should we make him leave? Moreover, the official position is low-paying and the travel expenses are difficult. You should think about it again." Baolu then consulted with his close friends among the students and decided to set up a private school in someone's home. One reason was that Tian Shu could continue his studies and advance his learning, and another was to use the salary to plan his return. The students were very happy that Tian Shu would stay and recommended him to a prominent family near the city, the Zhang family. In the following year, on the 18th day of the first month of the third year of the Ming dynasty, he set up his teaching post. Friends from the school and academy all sent him off. The Zhang family was very pleased and held a banquet, treating him as the highest guest. They also told Baolu, "Your son may stay overnight and can stay in the dormitory." Baolu agreed.

    75

    至二月花晨，洙解斋归省。偶经一所，境甚幽僻，山下皆桃树，花方盛开。洙爱之，小立徘徊。忽见桃林中一美人，延伫花下，洙不敢顾而去。尔后经从，美人必在门首。一日，洙过，偶遗所得俸金，美人命婢拾以还洙，洙感激。明日，诣谢。至门，丫鬟入报曰：“前遗金郎来矣！”请入内厅，美人出相见，笑问曰： “君非张运使宅西宾乎？”洙曰：“然！”且谢还金事。

    Explanation

    75

    On the morning of the second month when flowers were blooming, Zou returned home after leaving his study. He happened to pass by a secluded and quiet place, where below the mountain were all peach trees, and the flowers were just in full bloom. Zou loved the place and stood there for a while, wandering around. Suddenly, he saw a beautiful woman standing by the flowers in the peach grove. Zou dared not look back and left. Afterward, whenever he passed by, the woman was always at the gate. One day, Zou passed by and accidentally left behind the salary he had received. The woman ordered a maid to pick it up and return it to Zou, who was grateful. The next day, he went to thank her. When he arrived at the gate, a maid went in to report, saying, "The gentleman who lost his gold has come!" She invited him to enter the inner hall, and the woman came out to meet him, smiling and asking, "Are you not the guest teacher at Zhang's mansion?" Zou replied, "Yes," and thanked her for returning the gold.

    76

    美人曰：“张氏一家亲戚，彼西宾即吾西宾也，奚谢为？”洙起揖曰：“敢问夫人名阀为谁？与敝东何亲？”美人曰：“此为平姓，成都故族也。妾文孝坊薛氏女，嫁平幼子康，不幸早卒，妾独孀居。”坐久，茶至再，洙辞出，美人留之曰：“今夕且宿寒舍，若贤东知君至此，而妾不能为一款曲，惶愧殊甚！”即陈酒馔，设二席，与洙耦坐。坐中劝酬极至，语杂谐谑。洙以其张氏姻娅，不敢少纵。美人曰：“闻君倜傥俊才，雅能赋咏，何至作儒生酸乎？妾虽不敏，亦颇解吟事。今既遇赏音，而高山流水，何惜一奏！”因尽出其家所藏唐贤遗墨示洙，其中元稹、杜牧、高骈诗词手翰尤多，皆真迹，炳然如新。洙玩之不忍释手。

    Explanation

    76

    The beautiful woman said, "The Zhang family is my relatives, and that tutor is the same as mine, so why should we thank each other?" Zhu rose and bowed, saying, "May I ask, what is your family name and social status, and what relation do you have with my master?" The woman replied, "This is the Ping family, an old clan from Chengdu. I am the daughter of the Xue family from the Wenxiao坊, and I married the youngest son of the Ping family, named Kang. Unfortunately, he passed away early, and I remain a widow." They sat for a long time, and tea was served twice. Zhu excused himself to leave, but the woman invited him to stay, saying, "Tonight, please stay at my humble abode. If my master knows you have come here, and I cannot offer a single piece of entertainment, I feel extremely ashamed and uneasy!" She immediately set out wine and food, arranged two seats, and sat with Zhu in pairs. During their conversation, they encouraged and responded to each other's toasts to the fullest extent, and their talk was mixed with jokes and humor. Zhu, considering his connection to the Zhang family, did not dare to let himself go. The woman said, "I have heard that you are a talented and free-spirited person, skilled in writing poetry. Why be so pedantic like a scholar? I may not be very clever, but I also understand poetry. Now that I have met someone who appreciates my art, and we share the rare and perfect understanding of a 'high mountain and flowing water,' why not perform one piece?" She then showed Zhu all the authentic works of poetry and verse from her collection, particularly those of Yuan Zhen, Du Mu, and Gao Pian, which were all bright and fresh as if new. Zhu could not put them down.

    77

    美人麾婢撤去旧俎，别出佳肴，中多异味，不能识。取玻璃杯酌洙。洙口占一诗曰：

    路入桃源小洞天，乱红飞处遇婵娟。襄王误作高唐梦，不是阳台云雨仙。

    韶艳应难挽，芳华信易凋（薛）。缀阶红尚媚（洙），委地白仍娇（薛）。坠速如辞树（洙），飞迟似恋条（薛）。藓铺新蹙绣（洙），草叠巧裁绡（薛）。丽质愁先殒（洙），香魂痛莫招（薛）。燕衔归故垒（洙），蝶逐过危桥（薛）。粘帙将晞露（洙），冲帘乍起飙（薛）。遇晴犹有态（洙），经雨倍无聊（薛）。蜂趁低兼絮（洙），鱼吞细杂薸（薛）。轻盈珠履践（洙），零乱翠钿飘（薛）。鸟过生愁触（洙），儿嬉最怕摇（薛）。褪英浮雨涧（洙），残蕊漾风潮（薛）。

    Explanation

    77

    The beautiful lady waved her servant to remove the old dishes and bring out new delicacies. Among them were many exotic flavors, which could not be recognized. She took a glass cup and poured wine for Zhu. Zhu spontaneously composed a poem saying:

    The path leads into a small paradise, where amidst the scattered red petals, I meet a graceful maiden. King Xiang of Chu mistook it for a dream of Gaotang, but it is not the fairy of the cloud and rain on the Yangtai.

    The beautiful lady said, "It is good, but it is too short and lacks depth to fully express joy; how about using 'fallen flowers' as a theme and composing a joint poem?" Zhu replied, "I will follow your instruction." The beautiful lady sang saying:

    The beauty of youth is hard to hold back, and the bloom of spring is easily withered. The red flowers on the steps still charm, and the white petals on the ground remain delicate. They fall quickly like bidding farewell to the tree, and they fly slowly as if reluctant to leave the branch. Moss spreads like newly embroidered brocade, and grass layers like skillfully cut silk. The beautiful nature grieves before it perishes, and the fragrant spirit cannot be summoned back. Swallows carry home the old nest, and butterflies chase each other over the precarious bridge. They stick to the pages about to dry the dew, and rush through the curtains with sudden gusts of wind. Even in sunny weather, they still have a demeanor, but after rain, they become even more listless. Bees chase low and mixed with fluff, and fish swallow fine and mixed with water lettuce. Graceful, like pearl shoes stepping, and scattered, like green jade hairpins floating. Birds passing cause sorrowful touches, and children playing fear shaking. Fading flowers float on the rain-filled stream, and withered petals ripple in the wind-blown tide.

    78

    积径教童扫（洙），沿流倩水漂（薛）。媚人沾锦瑟（洙），瀹茗入诗瓢（薛）。玉貌楼前堕（洙），冰容梦里消（薛）。芳园曾藉坐（洙），长路或追镳（薛）。罗扇姬藏瓣（洙），筠篱仆护苗（薛）。折来随手尽（洙），带处近环焦（薛）。泥涴犹凄惨（洙），瓶空更寂寥（薛）。叶浓阴自厚（洙），蒂密子偏饶（薛）。岂必分茵溷（洙），宁思上砑硝（薛）。香余何吝窃（洙），佩解不烦邀（薛）。冶态宜宫额（洙），痴情妒舞腰（薛）。妆台休浪拂（洙），留伴可怜宵（薛）。

    78

    Teaching children to sweep along the path (Zhu), entrusting the water to float downstream (Xue). Charming people touch the golden zither (Zhu), brewing tea into the poet's gourd (Xue). Beautiful appearance falling before the tower (Zhu), cold demeanor disappearing in a dream (Xue). Fragrant garden once used as a seat (Zhu), long road sometimes chasing the reins (Xue). Silk fan lady hiding the petals (Zhu), bamboo fence servant guarding the young plants (Xue). Picking and finishing with a casual gesture (Zhu), belt near the ring of fire (Xue). Muddy and still sad (Zhu), empty bottle even more lonely (Xue). Dense leaves creating a thick shade (Zhu), dense stems with plentiful seeds (Xue). Why necessarily divide the mat and the toilet (Zhu), would rather think of grinding nitre (Xue). Fragrant remainder, why be stingy and steal (Zhu), unfasten the pendant, do not bother to invite (Xue).     79

    联成，美人出小笺写之，写讫。夜已二鼓，延入寝室，自荐枕席，鱼水欢情，极其缱绻。枕边切切叮咛洙曰：“慎勿轻言，若贤东知之，彼此名节丧尽矣。”次日，以卧狮玉镇纸一枚赠洙，送至门外，曰：“无事再来，勿效薄幸也。”洙遂绐馆东曰：“老母相念至深，必令归家宿歇，不敢留此。”馆东信之，洙由是常宿美人所。逾半年，人无知者。惟赏花玩月，举白弄琴，曲尽人间之乐。

    Explanation

    79

    Linking, the beauty took out a small note and wrote on it, then finished writing. By the second watch of the night, she invited him into her chamber, offering him her pillow and mat, and they shared a deep and intimate pleasure. Beside the pillow, she earnestly warned Zhu, saying: "Be careful not to speak of this lightly. If the patron were to learn of it, both of us would lose our reputations." The next day, she gave Zhu a jade paperweight shaped like a sleeping lion, and as she saw him to the door, she said: "Come again only when there is no business; do not imitate the unfaithful." Zhu then deceived the patron by saying: "My mother misses me deeply, and she will surely have me return home to stay the night; I dare not remain here." The patron believed him, and from then on, Zhu often stayed at the beauty’s residence. For over half a year, no one knew of this. They only enjoyed flowers and the moon, raised their cups of wine, played the zither, and fully experienced all the pleasures of the world.

    一夕，与洙论诗曰：“唐人喜作回文，近时罕见。”洙曰：“惟夫人柔情幽思，谈笑为之，若予荒钝，无复措辞。”美人笑曰：“请试命题，以求教益！”洙遽曰：“四时词也。”美人即赋诗曰：

    花朵几枝柔傍砌，柳丝千缕细摇风。霞明半岭西斜日，月上孤村一树松。

    凉回翠簟冰人冷，齿沁清泉夏井寒。香篆袅风清缕缕，纸窗明月白团团。

    Explanation

    80

    One night, the man named Zhu and the woman discussed poetry. The woman said, "Tang people enjoyed writing rebus poetry, but it is rarely seen in recent times." Zhu replied, "Only you, with your gentle emotions and deep thoughts, can do it in a casual and playful manner. As for me, I am rustic and dull, unable to find words." The woman smiled and said, "Please try to set a topic, so I can learn from you!" Zhu quickly suggested, "How about a poem about the four seasons?" The woman immediately began to write the poem:

    Tender flowers lean against the steps, willow branches sway gently in the wind. The sunset shines brightly over half the hill, the moon rises over a lone village with a solitary pine tree.

    The coolness of the green mat brings a chill, the refreshing coolness of spring water from a summer well. The scent of incense rises in thin, clear threads, the bright, round moonlight through the paper window.

    Snow covers the reeds in autumn, the wind through the willows and the twilight landscape. A lonely lamp and a traveler's dream in an empty building, a solitary goose carrying a letter to a distant homeland.

    The cold weather and the closing of doors in the morning, the snow and cold wind in the night, with the city gates closed. The warmth of a red charcoal fire around a stove, the clear, light green tea in a porcelain cup.

    Zhu read the poem and was impressed by the woman's quick-witted and ingenious nature, preparing to write his own response. The woman modestly acknowledged the value of the man's response, using a metaphor to express her gratitude. Zhu praised the woman's poem and expressed the difficulty in matching its quality, then wrote his own four lines of poetry in response.

    芳树吐花红过雨，入帘飞絮白惊风。黄添晓色春舒柳，粉落晴香雪覆松。

    81

    A fragrant tree blooms with red flowers after rain, and white catkins fly into the curtains, startled by the wind. Yellow adds to the morning color as spring willows stretch out, and powdered petals fall, leaving a fragrant snow covering the pines.

    Melons float in a jar of cool water to relieve summer heat, and lotus roots are layered on a plate with ice, suggesting a cold, refreshing dish. Slanted stones near the steps, with dense bamboo shoots growing through them, and in a small pond, leaves stretch out, and lotus flowers emerge in clusters.

    The setting sun with its red glow, contrasting with the red leaves covered in frost, and thin smoke envelops the trees, giving the evening forest an ashen hue. A phoenix letter carries sorrow, too ashamed to seal the tears, and in a dream of a butterfly, one is startled by sorrow, afraid to think of home.

    The cold wind blows through the snow-covered fishing boat, signaling the end of fishing, and the moonlight shines on the frosty watchtower, where cold sounds echo through the city. The rich fragrance of wine fills the cup, like a rosy hue, and the faint shadow of a plum tree crosses the paper screen, creating a clear, serene image.

    The beautiful woman reads and smiles, saying, "These are truly wonderful words, but if both rhymes are harmonious, they would be even better." Zhu says, "A gentleman does not wish to surpass others, so I lose one point." Zhu then says, "The mountains and waters of Shu are uniquely beautiful, and since ancient times, they have produced many beautiful women. If we compare them to Lady Zhaojun, Wenjun, and Xue Tao, who is superior?" The beautiful woman says, "Lady Zhaojun was far away and married into the desert, and Zhuo Wenjun selling wine is shameful. They are both beautiful but have short lives, suffering hardships. If you met Xue Tao, it would not be different from today. From this perspective, she is indeed superior." Zhu says, "Xue Tao was a courtesan, how dare I compare her to you. But her talent and beauty are also rare. I once read Qin Zaisi's Records of the Strange which states that Gao Qianli governed Shu and once held a banquet, changing a one-character command to 'mouth, like an endless measure.'"

    ’涛曰：‘川，有似三条椽。’高曰：‘奈何一条曲。’涛曰：‘相公尚使没量斗，穷酒佐三条椽有一条曲，又何足怪！’妇人敏赡，诚未易比。”美人曰：“子知其然，而不知其所以然，如此之类，特戏笑之语耳。若其‘水国蒹葭夜有霜，月寒山色共苍苍，谁云万里自今夕，离梦杳如关塞长’之作，可以伯仲杜牧。而尤善制小笺，至今蜀人号薛涛笺。而子以妓女薄之，非知涛者也。”酒罢就枕，洙馈以八珠耳榼一付。美人谢曰：“谨当佩服，犹君子之常在耳边也。”

    82

    Tao said, "The river is like three rafters." Gao replied, "Why is one curved?" Tao said, "Even a high-ranking official still uses a measuring cup, and a minor official has a curved rafter, so what is there to be surprised about!" The woman was intelligent and generous, truly hard to compare with others." The beauty said, "You know the result but not the reason behind it, such as these kinds of things, they are just playful words. If it is her work 'In the water country, the reeds are covered with frost at night, the moon and the cold mountain colors are all the same, who says that from tonight, a distance of ten thousand miles, the dream of separation is as long as the frontier,' it can rival Du Mu. And she is especially good at making small notes, even today, people in Shu call them Xue Tao notes. And you belittle her because she is a courtesan, you do not know Tao." After drinking, they went to bed, and Shu gave her a set of eight pearl wine containers. The beauty thanked him, saying, "I will cherish it, like a constant presence in the ear of a gentleman."

    After some time, Shu's mother fell ill, and he stopped teaching to take care of her. It took more than three months for her to recover. The beauty was surprised that he had been away for so long, fearing he had met someone else, and so she composed the 'Annoyed Song' to express her resentment. When Shu's mother recovered from her illness, he returned to the study, and that evening, he went to see Ping. The beauty greeted him and said, "Why have you been away for so long?" Shu told her the truth. The beauty said, "I have not seen you for three months, and now I have not seen you for three months." Shu joked with her, saying, "I have not tasted meat for three months, but I know the taste of meat tonight." While chatting, she took out the previous song to show Shu, and the song said:

    83

    黑铅铸剑难为锋，碧芰制衣宁御风？歙漆阿胶忽纷解，清尘浊水何由逢？请看绿草南园蝶，并宿花房花亦悦。鸳鸯头白不相离，那学秋胡便长别！东邻美女红玉梭，雪缕凤机成素罗。雨意云情肯轻许，纵然折齿将如何？深深永巷闲风月，锦帐兰缸泪如血。血点年深久尚红，至今洒在同心结。

    83

    A black lead sword cannot be sharpened, nor can a green lotus leaf be made into a garment that can withstand the wind? Even Xu lacquer and donkey-hide glue suddenly disintegrate, how can clear dust and muddy water meet? Look at the green grass and the butterfly in the southern garden, they coexist harmoniously, and the flowers are also pleased. Even when mandarin ducks grow old, they do not separate, unlike the story of Autumn Hu who abandoned his wife! A beautiful woman from the east can weave silk as fine as snow and as strong as a phoenix's loom. Even if there is a hint of rain and clouds, one should not lightly agree, what will happen even if one's teeth are broken? In a deep, quiet alley, the wind and moon are idle, and the tears in a brocade tent and orchid lamp are like blood. Even after many years, the blood spot remains red, and it is still present in the knot of the heart.

    Zhou loved her talent and beauty, and his affection for her grew deeper. The beautiful woman also valued Zhou's literary talent, and she did not hesitate to pour out her heart. She said to Zhou, "Our previous couplets did not fully express our high emotions. Tonight, we should play soft music and dance slowly, drink lightly, and recite softly, and compose another poem, so that we can see each other as formidable rivals." She then lit incense in a duck-shaped incense burner, served wine with red clam meat, pulled the curtain to look at the moon, and sat together in front of the hall. Zhou said, "In the past, Han Yu and Meng Jiao had works such as 'Couplets in the South of the City,' 'Fighting Roosters,' 'Stone Cauldron,' and 'Autumn Rain,' which were grand words and dangerous rhymes, and were widely praised. For this composition tonight, we should compose a couplet about the moon at night, with fifty lines as a standard. Do you agree, madam?" The beautiful woman said, "That is my intention." Zhou then asked the beautiful woman to start by composing the first couplet.

    洙叱曰：“汝到吾家，随即出城，比吾归，汝已去矣，何得妄言？”仆曰：“我昨夜宿先生家，今日早饭罢方回；老广文亦甚惊讶，要自来相寻。”洙窘甚，颜色陡变。张曰：“先生如有私眷，当以实告，勿隐也。”洙弗能讳，乃具道本末，且愧谢曰：“此令亲见留，非贱子辄敢无礼。”张曰：“吾家何尝有亲戚在此？兼诸房姊妹亦无事平姓者，必祟也。今当自爱，不宜复往！”洙唯唯。抵暮，私诣美人，道此意。比至，美人已知，曰：“郎勿怨，盖冥数尽于此也。”与洙痛饮，且叙欢情。戒晓，美人语洙曰：“从此永别，后会难期，无以将意。”出洒墨玉笔管一枝为贶，云：“此唐物也，郎慎藏之。”遂饮泣而别。

    且所谓嫁平幼子康者，乃平康巷也。文孝坊者，城中亦无此额；而文与孝合为教字，谓教坊也。教坊，唐妓女所居，涛为蜀乐妓，故居教坊也。非涛而谁哉？况管上字刻高氏清玩，则唐西川节度使高骈千里所贮，当骈镇蜀，涛于诸妓中，最蒙宠待，笔与镇纸，皆骈赐也。兼所藏诸帖，又骈与元丞相、杜紫微最多，盖元与杜尝有诗赠之，即‘锦江腻滑峨眉秀，幻出文君与薛涛’是也。其为涛之灵无疑，而物出于骈者审矣。无庸深究！”百禄甚以为然，然恐其终为所惑，急遣还广中，宝藏数物，常以示人。后二年，洙亦入学，为生员，中洪武甲戌进士，授山东曹县知县，竟亦无他焉。

    Explanation

    90

    As for the term "嫁平幼子康," it refers to the name of a street, known as Pingkang Lane. There is no such sign or title for the Wenxiao Ward in the city; however, when "wen" (文) and "xiao" (孝) are combined, they form the character "jiao" (教), which means "teaching" or "instruction." This is what is referred to as the "Jiaofang" (教坊). The Jiaofang was an institution during the Tang Dynasty where courtesans resided. Zhao Yunjian (薛涛) was a courtesan from Sichuan who lived in the Jiaofang. Who else could it be but her? Furthermore, the inscriptions on the tube or scroll bear the mark of Gao's refined collection, indicating that these items were stored over a thousand miles away by Gao Pian, the military governor of Western Sichuan during the Tang Dynasty. When Gao Pian governed Sichuan, Zhao Yunjian was the most favored and treated with great respect among all the courtesans, receiving writing tools such as brushes and paperweights as gifts from him. Additionally, the various documents and writings in his collection, which were also bestowed upon Yuan Zhen and Du Mu, were the most numerous. Yuan and Du once wrote poems to her, such as "The smoothness of the Jinjiang River and the beauty of Mount Emei, conjuring forth Wenjun and Xue Tao." There is no doubt that the spirit or essence belongs to her, and it is certain that the items came from Gao Pian. There is no need to investigate further!" Bai Lu strongly agreed, but he feared that he might ultimately be deceived. He quickly sent the items back to Guangzhou, where he treasured them and often showed them to others. Two years later, Zhu also entered school, became a student, passed the imperial examination in the year Jia Xu of the Hongwu era, and was appointed as the magistrate of Cao County in Shandong. In the end, there was nothing else remarkable about him.

    青城舞剑录
    至正间，有道士真本无、文固虚，不知何许人。客威顺王门下，通剑术，晓兵，深于智略，号文武才。王虽畜之，未始奇也；惟樊口卫君美重之。一日，王游别苑，召二人侍，因从容讽曰：“方今天下太平日久，极盛而丰。在大王观之，固以为高枕肆志之日，惟声色狗马是务，焉知其他！在愚辈观之，盖有甚不然者。官里老而昏，奇氏宠而横，哈麻、雪雪之徒，又以演揲儿法蛊惑君心。贿赂公行，是非颠倒，天变于上而不悟，民困于下而不知。武备不修，朝政废弛，小人恣肆，君子伏藏。殆犹一发之引千钧，祸在旦夕，甚可畏也。

    Explanation

    91

    Qingcheng Dance Sword Record
    During the reign of Emperor Toghon Temür, there were two Daoists named Zhen Benwu and Wen Gu Xu, whose origins are unknown. They served under the Prince of Weishun, were proficient in swordsmanship, knowledgeable about military affairs, and had deep strategic insight. They were known as men of both literary and martial talents. Although the prince kept them, he never found them remarkable; only Fan Kou Wei Junmei valued them highly. One day, the prince went to a private garden and summoned the two Daoists to attend him. He then spoke to them in a leisurely manner:

    "Today, the empire has enjoyed long periods of peace and prosperity. In your view, it is a time to lie on a high pillow and indulge in pleasures, focusing only on music, women, dogs, and horses, without concern for anything else! But in our humble opinion, things are quite different. The emperor is old and senile, and his favored concubine Kui Shi is domineering. Officials like Hama and Xue Xue, who practice the yanzhai'er ritual, have corrupted his heart. Bribery is openly practiced, right and wrong are confused, the heavens are signaling calamity, but the emperor does not realize it. The people are suffering, but the emperor is unaware. Military preparedness is neglected, the court's governance is lax, corrupt officials act without restraint, and virtuous officials are suppressed. It is like a single hair pulling down a thousand catties, disaster is imminent, and it is very frightening."
