    苏老泉所谓：‘有乱之萌，无乱之形，是谓将乱。’大王朝廷懿亲，江汉藩屏，宜求贤纳士，选将练兵，节用储财，阴为之备。万一风尘草动，寰宇土崩，即便指麾义旗，率先赴难，上以纾君父之急，下以尽臣子之心，克复神州，光膺旧物。然后奉身而退，口不言功，恳请归藩，世守南纪。使执笔之臣，书为大元宗英，秘在金匮，垂之万年。岂不伟哉！岂不盛哉！”王怪之曰：“尔非病风狂痴耶！何言之不伦如是？吾将执尔送县官矣。”二人默然而退，计曰：“腐骨残肉，魂亡神耗者，尚何教以有为哉！盍求豪杰者而佐之。竖子不足谋矣！不去，祸且至。”于是题诗于黄鹤楼而遁。本无诗曰：

    Explanation

    92

    Su Shi once said: "When disorder begins to germinate but has not yet taken visible form, it is called impending chaos." The prestigious relatives of the imperial court and the strategic importance of the Jianghan region suggest that one should seek out talented individuals, select capable generals, train troops, conserve resources, and prepare secretly. If there is a sudden outbreak of unrest or rebellion, one should raise a just cause and lead the charge, relieving the emperor's distress and fulfilling one's loyalty as a subject, reclaiming the lost territories and restoring the former glory of the nation. After achieving success, one should retire from public life without boasting, request to return to one's fief, and guard the southern borders. Let the historians record one's deeds as a great hero, inscribed in the imperial archives for posterity. How great and splendid this would be! The king was surprised and said, "Are you not suffering from madness or delusion? Why do you speak so incoherently? I will have you taken to the county official!"     93

    平生智略满胸中，剑拂秋霜气吐虹。耻掉苏秦三寸舌，要将事业佐英雄。

    93

    Throughout my life, wisdom and strategies fill my chest, my sword gleams like autumn frost, and its aura shines like a rainbow. I am ashamed to use the three-inch tongue of Su Qin, but I aim to support heroes in their endeavors.

    Gu Xu composed these two poems:

    With bold courage in my seven-foot frame, would my ambitions make me a timid scholar? The teachings of the old man by the bridge are merely for show, but I have a scroll of the Lügong (Book of Military Strategy) for myself.

    The sword emerges from its scabbard, reflecting cold light, and its blade bears the shadow of blood from enemies. I knew early on that such efforts were futile, yet I was mistakenly treated as a hero by the king.

    94

    王知而求之，隐矣。未几乱作，悉如所言。

    至正乙未，倪文俊陷沔阳，威顺之子报恩奴与湖南元帅阿思蓝水陆并进讨之。至汉川，水浅胶舟。文俊用火筏烧船，报恩奴遇害。王思之，百计觅二人，不能得。陈友谅闻其往来光、黄间，具书礼请之。不至，翩然入蜀。既而明玉珍据四川，素闻二人名，物色不可得。天朝既平群寇，四海一家，君美兄君彦为西充县丞。君美往省候之。回途舟败，同船之人，尽葬鱼腹。独君美负得一板，浪滚及岸，因而不死。然行李盘缠，一时俱尽。偶腰间碎银数星在，急投近岸民家，觅火燎衣，买食充腹，踯躅彷徨，计无所出。民家翁视其辞貌，知非常人，颇善待之。留数日，因出纵步，忽二道士前揖曰：“卫君一寒至此哉！”视之，真、文二故人也。告以困苦之状。曰：“无忧也。”挟往其家，则青城山也。高墙华屋，深院曲房，苍头数人，列侍左右，俎豆备水陆之珍，歌舞极声容之盛。与君美话旧，欢若平生。

    Explanation

    94

    The king sought them, but they were hidden. Soon after, chaos erupted, exactly as he had predicted.

    In the year 1345 of the Zhizheng era, Ni Wenjun captured Mianyang. Wishun's son Baonu and the Hunan Yuan帅 Ashilan advanced both by land and water to attack him. They reached Hanchuan, where the shallow water caused their boats to become stuck. Wenjun used fire rafts to burn the ships, and Baonu was killed. The king mourned for him and tried every means to find the two men, but he could not. Chen Youliang heard that they had been traveling between Guang and Huang, and prepared letters and gifts to invite them. They did not come, and instead, they gracefully entered Sichuan. Later, Ming Yuzhen took control of Sichuan and had long heard of the two men's names, but he could not find them. After the Tianchao Dynasty had pacified all the bandits and unified the four seas, Junmei's brother Junyan became the magistrate of Xichong County. Junmei went to visit him. On his return journey, their boat capsized, and all the people on board were drowned. Only Junmei managed to grab a piece of wood, which was washed ashore, and thus he survived. However, his belongings and money were all lost. By chance, he had a few coins in his waistband, which he quickly used to seek shelter at a nearby household, where he found fire to dry his clothes, bought food to satisfy his hunger, and wandered aimlessly, unable to think of a solution. The old man of the household saw his demeanor and knew he was no ordinary person, so he treated him kindly. He stayed there for several days and then went out for a walk. Suddenly, two Taoist priests bowed before him and said, "How cold you are, General Wei!" Upon seeing them, he realized they were his old friends, Zhen and Wen. He told them of his plight. They said, "Do not worry." They took him to their home, which turned out to be Qingcheng Mountain. There were tall walls and splendid houses, deep courtyards, and winding rooms, with several servants standing on both sides. The food and drink were prepared with both aquatic and terrestrial delicacies, and the music and dance reached the height of their splendor. They talked about old times, and it was as if they had known each other for a long time.

    95

    因询其乱中出处，二人曰：“自辞黄鹤，即入黄牛。久隐青城，忽逢青眼，其为喜慰，殆不可言。所惜壮心凋落，一事无成，俯仰乾坤，飘摇萍梗，索居闲处，有愧故人。”乃与痛饮，饮酣气豪，论议蜂起。本无曰：“天下之事，在乎知几。几者事之微，吉凶之先见者也。《易》曰：‘知几其神乎？’又曰：‘君子见几而作，不俟终日。’子思子曰：‘君子知微’，皆谓是也。古今以来，豪杰之士不少，其知几者几何人哉？吾于汉得张子房焉。

    Explanation

    95

    They inquired about their whereabouts during the chaos, and the two men said, "After departing from Yellow Crane Tower, I entered Yellow Bull. I had been long hidden in Qingcheng, and suddenly encountered the green eye. The joy and relief were almost indescribable. What is regrettable is the decline of youthful ambitions. Looking up and down at the universe, living a life of uncertainty and instability, living in isolation, feeling ashamed before old friends."

    Then they drank deeply, and as they became drunk, their spirits soared, and debates erupted. Bennu said, "All matters of the world depend on knowing the signs. The signs are the subtlest aspects of things, the first indications of good or bad fortune. The Yijing says, 'Knowing the signs is divine?' It also says, 'A gentleman acts upon seeing the signs, without waiting until the end of the day.' Zisi said, 'A gentleman knows the subtle.' These all refer to the same idea. Since ancient times, there have been many heroes, but how many truly know the signs? I found Zhang Liang in the Han dynasty."

    96

    子房事载史册，不必赘论，盍相与论其几乎。夫汉祖之臣，莫逾三杰，而子房又三杰之杰者也。项羽杰于高祖，而为高祖所灭，子房之谋也。是子房非特三杰之杰，并杰于高祖、项羽矣。且高祖为是三杰之目者，忌之之萌也，子房知之，萧何、韩信不知也，故卒受下狱之辱，夷族之祸。子房晏然无恙，夫祸不在于祸之日，而在于目三杰之时。天下未定，子房出奇无穷。天下既定，子房退而如愚，受封择小县，偶语不先发，其知几为何如哉？诚所谓大丈夫也矣。

    Explanation

    96

    The deeds of Zhang Liang are recorded in history, so there is no need to elaborate further. Why not discuss his virtues? Among Emperor Gaozu's ministers, none surpass the Three Heroes, and Zhang Liang is the foremost among them. Xiang Yu was superior to Emperor Gaozu, but he was defeated by Emperor Gaozu, due to Zhang Liang's strategy. Thus, Zhang Liang is not only the foremost among the Three Heroes, but also surpasses both Emperor Gaozu and Xiang Yu. Moreover, Emperor Gaozu's listing of the Three Heroes was a sign of his jealousy. Zhang Liang understood this, but Xiao He and Han Xin did not. Therefore, they ultimately suffered the humiliation of imprisonment and the disaster of being exterminated. Zhang Liang remained unperturbed and unharmed. The disaster does not occur on the day of the disaster, but in the moment of recognizing the Three Heroes. When the world was not yet settled, Zhang Liang displayed boundless ingenuity. When the world was settled, Zhang Liang retreated as if he were foolish, choosing a small county for his fief, and refrained from speaking first. How perceptive was his understanding? Indeed, he is a true man of virtue.

    97

    ”固虚曰：“吾于宋得一人焉，曰陈图南。五代之乱，古所未有，不有英雄起而定之，则乱何时而已乎？图南窥见其几，有志大事，往来关、洛，岂是浪游，及闻赵祖登基，坠驴大笑，故有‘属猪人已著黄袍’之句，就已字观之，盖可见矣。既而拂袖归山，白云高卧，野花啼鸟，春色一般，远引高腾，不见痕迹，所谓寓大巧于至拙，藏大智于极愚，天下后世，知其为神仙而已矣！知其为隐者而已矣！孰得而窥其窔奥？方之子房，有过无不及。

    Explanation

    97

    "Gu Xu said: 'I met a person in Song, whose name is Chen Tunan. The chaos of the Five Dynasties was unprecedented in ancient times. Without a hero rising to bring order, when would the chaos ever end? Chen Tunan saw the signs of the times and had ambitions for great deeds. His travels between Guan and Luo were not aimless. When he heard of Zhao Zu ascending the throne, he laughed while falling off his donkey, thus uttering the cryptic phrase, “The person born in the Year of the Pig has already donned the yellow robe.” By examining the character “已” in the phrase, one can see its meaning. He then swept his sleeves and returned to the mountains, where he lay high among the white clouds, surrounded by wildflowers and singing birds, in the springtime scenery. He rose high and far, leaving no trace. This is what is meant by hiding great skill in the most simple and concealing great wisdom in the most foolish. In future generations, people will know him only as a sage or a hermit! Who can fathom his deepest secrets? Compared to Zhang Liang, he was equally or more remarkable.'"

    人亦有言，英雄回首即神仙，岂不信欤！”君美曰：“二公炼质名山，尘埃富贵，向闻高论，犹似未能忘情者，岂不为修行之累乎？”二人大笑曰：“卫君平日议论，如此之高，今之识趣，何如此之下？夫循行数墨，呫哔呻吟，儒之土苴。熊经鸟伸，导引服气，仙之糟粕，吾之所谓修行者，岂在是哉！”因引君美周视其家，锦绮充盈，金玉山积，各有美人掌之。最后，至一山岩中，有髑髅百枚，二人指曰：“此世间不义人也，余得而诛之。”君美为之吐舌，舌久不能收。

    Explanation

    98

    A saying goes, "When a hero looks back, they become a deity—how can one not believe this?" Jun Mei said, "The two gentlemen have refined themselves on famous mountains, yet they seem to still be attached to worldly wealth. Even after hearing your lofty words, they still seem unable to forget their worldly desires. Is this not a hindrance to their spiritual cultivation?" The two laughed loudly and said, "Jun Mei, your usual discussions are so high-minded, yet your current tastes and interests are so lowly. Those who mechanically follow rules and recite meaningless phrases are the dregs of Confucianism. Those who engage in physical exercises and breathing practices are but the remnants of Daoism. What we call spiritual cultivation is not found in such things!" They then led Jun Mei to view their home, which was filled with luxurious silks and brocades, mountains of gold and jade, each guarded by beautiful attendants. Finally, they arrived at a mountain cliff where there were hundreds of skulls. The two pointed and said, "These are the unjust people of the world, whom we have punished." Jun Mei was so shocked that he stuck out his tongue, and it remained that way for a long time.

    The next day, a grand banquet was held, with Jun Mei seated at the head table. Two beautiful women carried a tray filled with ten precious pearls and a hundred taels of gold as a gift. Jun Mei could not refuse and simply nodded in thanks. They then drank heavily and became drunk, at which point Jun Mei spontaneously composed a poem:

    99

    盖世英雄盖世才，关河百战起尘埃。辽东白鹤空留语，天下黄金谩筑台！壮志已成终古恨，残编付与后人哀！东风万斛曹瞒舰，尽化周郎一炬灰。

    固虚续吟曰：

    豪杰消磨叹五陵，发冲乌帽气填膺！眼前不是无豪杰，身后何须论废兴！当道有蛇魂已断，渡江无马谶难凭。可怜一片中原地，虎啸龙腾几战争。

    其诗大抵类此，则其人可想矣。君美知所吟不能出其右，乃制《喜迁莺》一阕，执杯酬谢于二公，自歌以侑焉。词曰：

    乾坤如昨，叹往事凄凉，长才萧索。景物都非，人民俱换，非是旧时城郭。世事恰如棋子，当局方知难著。胜与败，似一场春梦，何须惊愕！寥落，相见处，萍水异乡，烂熳清宵酌。说到英雄身同梦，涩尽剑锋莲锷。看破浮云变态，休问谁强谁弱！堪叹息，这一番归去，似辽东鹤。

    Explanation

    99

    A hero of the world, a talent of the world,
    Through countless battles across the lands, dust rises.
    The white crane of Liaodong leaves empty words behind,
    The gold of the world builds a futile platform!
    Grand ambitions have become eternal regrets,
    The remnants of my work will be left for future generations to lament!
    The mighty ships of Cao Cao, a million measures,
    Are all reduced to ashes by Zhou Yu's single fire!

    Continuing the poem, I say:

    Heroes are worn down, lamenting the Five Tombs,
    My hair stands on end, my chest filled with anger!
    There are still heroes before my eyes,
    Why bother to discuss the rise and fall after death?
    The snake that blocks the road has already been cut off,
    The prophecy of no horse crossing the river is unreliable.
    Pitiful is this land of the Central Plains,
    How many wars have there been with tigers roaring and dragons soaring?

    Such is the style of his poetry, and his character can be imagined.
    Youmei knows that his poetry cannot be surpassed, so he composed the Xǐ Qiānyīng (Happy Migration) tune, holding a cup to thank the two gentlemen, singing it himself to accompany them. The lyrics say:

    The universe is as it was yesterday,
    Lamenting the past, how desolate, the talents are sparse.
    The scenery is all different, the people have all changed,
    It is no longer the old city. The affairs of the world are like chess pieces,
    Only those in the game know how difficult it is to make a move.
    Victory and defeat, like a spring dream,
    Why be surprised! Lonely, meeting each other,
    Like萍water in a strange land, drinking freely in the clear night.
    Speaking of heroes, their lives are like dreams,
    The sword's edge and the lotus blade are all dull.
    Seeing through the changes of floating clouds,
    Do not ask who is stronger or weaker! It is worth sighing,
    This return, like the white crane of Liaodong.

    明日求归，二人曰：“唐有红线，今有碧线，当令送君也。”至则一好女子，其年可十七八，负竹箱，随真、文同送君美青城道上。顾谓曰：“后会难期，请为起舞。”碧线开箱，取白丸四，大如鸡卵，乃雌雄剑也。二人引而伸之，飞跃上下。须臾，天地晦冥，风云惨淡，惟于尘埃中见电光翕，交绕互缠。君美股战，行不成步，回望其居，皆陡壁穹崖，殊无有路。君美乃气不得出，目不得合，常若刃在其颈，心胆俱落。舞罢，失二人所在，独碧线旁君美立，倒皮囊中酒共饮。伺夜，握君美手东南而逝，将三更许抵家。但见金珠在榻，碧线亡去久矣，竟不知其何术也。洪武二十年，君美有婿单公铉为库官，间为人道妇翁事，亦与此吻合焉。

    100

    The next day, you requested to return. The two people said, "In the Tang Dynasty, there was Red Silk; now there is Green Silk. I will send you." When you arrived, there was a beautiful woman, about seventeen or eighteen years old, carrying a bamboo box, and she accompanied Zhen and Wen to escort you to the Qingcheng Road. She turned to you and said, "It will be difficult to predict when we will meet again. Please allow me to perform a dance for you." Green Silk opened the box and took out four white pills, each as large as a chicken's egg, which were the male and female swords. The two people drew them out and extended them, leaping up and down. In a moment, the sky and earth became dark and obscure, the wind and clouds looked gloomy, and only in the dust could one see flashes of lightning, interwoven and entangled. Your legs trembled, and you could not take a step. Looking back at their residence, you saw only steep cliffs and high precipices, with no path in sight. You were unable to breathe, unable to close your eyes, always as if a blade was at your throat, and your heart and courage both fell. After the dance, the two people disappeared, and only Green Silk stood beside you, pouring the wine from the skin bag and drinking together. Waiting until night, she took your hand and departed southeast, arriving home around the third watch of the night. You only saw gold and jewels on the bed, and Green Silk had been gone for a long time, finally, you did not know what kind of magic it was. In the 20th year of the Hongwu era, you had a son-in-law named Dan Gong Xuan who was a treasury official. Sometimes, he told people about your father-in-law's affairs, which also matched this story.

    秋夕访琵琶亭记
    洪武初，吴江沈韶，年弱冠，美姿容，诗学萨天锡，字学边伯京，皆为时辈所称许。尝和天锡《过嘉兴》诗韵，题吴中二首云：

    七泽三江通甫里，杨柳芙蓉映湖水。阊门过去是盘门，半卷珠帘画楼里。蘼芜生遍鸳鸯沙，东风落尽棠梨花。馆娃香径走麋鹿，清夜鬼灯笼绛纱。三高祠下东流续，真娘墓上风吹竹。西施去后屟廊颓，岁岁春深烧痕绿。

    东南形胜繁华里，一片笙箫拂江水。小姬白苎制春衫，桂楫兰桡镜光里。舞台歌榭临鸥沙，粉墙半出樱桃花。采香蝴蝶飞不去，扑落轻盈团扇纱。吴歌《子夜》凭谁续？柳阴吹彻柯亭竹。范蠡扁舟去不回，惟有春波照人绿。

    他诗皆类此。然以家富，不欲仕。人知其然，复利其贿，或欲举为孝廉，或欲保为生员，旁午纷纭，殊无宁月。韶虽不吝于财，实厌其扰。乃谋于妻兄张氏曰：“如之何其可？”张曰“惟有远游，差可避耳。”

    Explanation

    101

    Autumn Evening Visit to the Pipa Pavilion

    In the early years of the Hongwu era, Shen Shao from Wujian, at the age of twenty, was known for his good looks and was skilled in poetry under the influence of Sa Tianxi and calligraphy under the guidance of Bian Bojing. Both were praised by his contemporaries. He once composed a poem in response to Sa Tianxi's "Passing Through Jiaxing" and titled it "Two Poems on Wu":

    Seven lakes and three rivers connect to Fuli, willows and lotuses reflect in the lake water. Beyond the Gate of the West is the Gate of the East, with half-drawn pearl curtains in a painted building. Mǐwú grows throughout the sand where mandarin ducks live, the east wind has blown away all the pear blossoms. The scent of the path at the Guanwa pavilion is where deer wander, ghost lanterns made of red gauze glow in the clear night. The eastern flow continues at the Three High Officials Temple, the wind blows through the bamboo on Zhen Nang's tomb. After Xi Shi left, the wooden walkway fell into disrepair, the green marks of fire from year to year during deep spring.

    Southeastern regions, known for their beauty and prosperity, are filled with the sound of flutes and oboes playing near the river. A young girl makes a spring robe from white hemp, the reflection of the moonlight on the oars made of cassia wood and orchid wood. Stages and singing pavilions are near the sand where seagulls rest, the half-visible pink walls with cherry blossoms. The scent of butterflies that do not fly away, the delicate silk of a fan falling gently. Who can continue the Wu songs, specifically "Ziye"? The wind blows through the bamboo in the shade of willows at the Keting pavilion. Fan Li left in a small boat and did not return, only the spring waves reflecting green light.

    His other poems were similar in style. However, due to his wealth, he did not wish to enter public service. People knew this, and some sought to profit from his wealth, wanting to nominate him as a filial and upright official or to recommend him as a student. The situation was chaotic and confusing, with no peace. Although Shen Shao was not stingy with his wealth, he was truly annoyed by the disturbances. He then discussed with his brother-in-law Zhang, saying, "What can be done about this?" Zhang replied, "Only by traveling far away can one avoid it."

    102

    韶然其计。乃拉中表陈生、梁生，乘峨舸巨艑，载万亿重资，遨游襄、汉间。次于九江府，爱匡庐之秀，览彭蠡之清，留连郡郭，吊古寻幽。众稍讥之，韶不恤也。因叹曰：“吾侪幸家富年少，粗知文墨，兹行盖避人耳。岂能效王戎辈执牙筹，屑屑计刀锥之利哉？”游益数。偶秋雨新霁，水天一色。韶偕梁、陈二生，同访琵琶亭，吟白司马“荻花枫叶”之篇，想京城女“银瓶铁骑”之韵，引睇四望，徘徊久之。于时月明风细，人静更深，方取酒共酌。闻月下仿佛有歌声，乍远乍近，或高或低，三人相顾错愕。梁生戏曰：“得非商妇解事乎？”韶曰：“尔时乐天尚须千呼万唤，今日岂得容易呈身哉？”陈生曰：“老大蛾眉，琵琶哀怨，纵使尊前轻拢慢拈，适足以增天涯沦落之感，岂能醉而成欢耶？”韶曰：“且静听之。”良久而寂。酒罢回船，竟莫知其何故。

    Explanation

    102

    Zhao resolved upon his plan. He then invited his cousin Chen and Liang, and together they boarded towering and massive ships, carrying an immense fortune, and set out to wander freely between the Xiang and Han rivers. They stopped at the Prefecture of Jiuzhou, where Zhao admired the beauty of Mount Lu and viewed the clarity of Poyang Lake, lingering in the city walls and visiting ancient sites in search of secluded beauty. The others began to criticize him slightly, but Zhao paid no heed. He sighed and said, “We are fortunate to be wealthy and young, with a basic knowledge of writing and literature. This journey is merely to avoid people. How could we emulate Wang Rong and his ilk, who clasp the abacus and meticulously calculate the profit of knives and needles?” Their travels became even more frequent. One day, after the autumn rain had just cleared, the water and sky were one color. Zhao, accompanied by Liang and Chen, visited the Pipa Pavilion together, reciting Bai Juyi’s poem about “willow catkins and maple leaves,” recalling the melody of the “silver bottle and iron steed” from the capital girl. They looked around in all directions, lingering for a long time. At that time, the moon was bright, the wind was gentle, the people were quiet, and the night was deep. They then took wine and drank together. Suddenly, they heard a faint song under the moon, sometimes far, sometimes near, sometimes high, sometimes low. The three of them looked at each other in surprise. Liang joked, “Could it not be a merchant’s wife who understands the situation?” Zhao replied, “At that time, Bai Juyi still needed to be called upon a thousand times before he would appear; how could she present herself so easily today?” Chen said, “An old woman with delicate brows, playing the pipa with sorrowful tones—though she may gently pluck and stroke the strings before the guests, it would only increase the feeling of being a wanderer lost in the world. How could it lead to drunken joy?” Zhao said, “Let us listen quietly.” After a long while, it became silent. After finishing their wine and returning to the boat, they still did not know the reason for it.

    103

    独韶迭宕，好事多情。翌日，往究其实。踌蹰之间，了无所见，兴阑体倦，方欲言还。忽奇香馥郁，缥缈而来。韶异之，延伫以俟。茶顷，一丽人宫妆艳饰，貌类天仙。二小姬前导，一持黄金吊炉，一抱紫罗绣褥，冉冉登阶。意必贵家宅眷，临赏于此，隐壁后避之。小姬铺褥庭心，丽人席地而坐。顾姬曰：“何得有生人气？毋乃昨夕狂客在是乎？”韶惧其使人搜索，起出拜见，且谢唐突。

    103

    Shao, versatile and full of variation, is kind-hearted and full of emotion. The next day, he went to investigate the truth. In a moment of hesitation, he saw nothing, and his interest waned as his body grew tired; he was just about to say goodbye and return. Suddenly, a strange fragrance, very fragrant, came mysteriously. Shao found it strange and waited anxiously. After a short while, a beautiful woman dressed in palace attire and adorned beautifully, looking like a heavenly beauty, appeared. Two young maids led the way, one holding a golden incense burner and one carrying a purple embroidered cushion, slowly ascending the steps. Shao thought it must be a member of a noble family coming to enjoy the scenery here and hid behind the wall to avoid them. The young maid laid the cushion in the middle of the courtyard, and the beautiful woman sat on the ground. Turning to the maid, she said, "How could there be a living person's scent? Isn't it because there was a mad guest here last night?" Fearing that they might send someone to search, Shao got up and came out to pay respects and apologized for the intrusion.

    106

    When the song ended, the lady urged Shao to drink to the dregs.

    After several cups, Shao's bold and unrestrained demeanor emerged, his discourse lively and spirited. He spoke with the lady about the rise and fall of the great warlords at the end of the Yuan dynasty, recounting events as clearly as if he had seen them with his own eyes, and also inquired into the details of Lord Chen’s actions. The lady replied, “The Spring and Autumn Annals conceal the faults of the powerful and the beloved; such matters are not something I dare to know.” Shao said, “Let me then speak of his character: soft-spoken and lacking decisiveness, blind and oblivious to subtle signs. In appointing his ministers, he favored the unqualified, such as Chen Pingzhang and Yao Pingzhang, who were petty men of narrow minds, yet he entrusted them with the reins of power and command of the military. On the other hand, men of virtue and talent like Zhan Tongwen and Wei Qishan were relegated to insignificant posts and left in idle positions. The military officials indulged in wine and women, while the civil officials concerned themselves only with empty talk. The city gates were too narrow to admit a carriage, so they built a flying bridge; Jiujiang, though humble, aspired to be the capital, yet its former site remains. Examples like these are laughably numerous. Moreover, he secretly assassinated Shouhui and openly took his place, changing the era name and establishing a new title—like a brother trapped in a well, the son Yang. Narrow-minded and lacking in strategy, he was no more than a servant to Li Jing of the south. And yet he still struggled like a mantis against an eagle, resisting with futile force. His soldiers were slaughtered in the lake waters, his generals killed in the field; his great men were destroyed, his phantom body falling swiftly to the arrow’s point. One defeat, and heaven abandoned him; his six armies scattered like stars. As for those who secretly planned in the war tent and aided in times of crisis, there was only the Fifth Prince alone. Alas! In the time when the heroes were in turmoil, in the days of primitive chaos and dust, if the strategists, generals, capable officials, and talented men were so few and weak, how could he not have been defeated and perished?” The lady listened with sorrow, tears streaming down her face.

    The luxurious ships and dragon boats are now but a distant memory, their grandeur confined to the dreams and memories of the past. The sun sets over the yellow reeds, casting a warm glow over the decaying walls of an abandoned fortress, while the imperial palace, once a symbol of power and glory, is now overgrown with green grass and shrouded in cold mist.     113

    是年冬初，丽人无故忽潸然泪下，悲不自胜。怪而问之，初则隐忍弗言，继则举声大恸。韶慰解万方，乃一启齿曰：“与郎冥契，尽在来朝，故不觉悲伤至此耳！”韶闻知，凄惶感怆，欲自缢于隧间。丽人不可曰：“郎阳寿未终，妾阴质未化。倘更沉溺世缘，致君非命，冥司必加重谴，彼此牵缠，何时是了？兼之定数，举莫能逃，纵曰舍生，亦为徒死。”韶乃止。金雁、钿蝉辈亦依依不忍舍，咸设饮食，与韶送程。既晓，丽人奉赤金条脱一双，明珠步摇一对，付生曰：“表诚寓意，睹物思人，再会无期，愿郎珍重。”亲送至大门之外，掩袂障面而还。韶犹悲不自已，残泪盈眶，顾盼之间，失其所在。乃重寻原店安下，收拾归吴。越数日，梁生至自襄阳，陈生客死房县，方咎韶负约，韶密以告，弗信也，出条脱、步摇示之，乃惊曰：“此非尘土间物，奇宝也，诚子之遇仙矣。”韶叮咛谆切，使勿轻言，故人无知者。

    113

    In the early winter of that year, the lady wept suddenly without cause, overwhelmed with sorrow. Surprised, he asked her, but at first she remained silent, enduring her pain. Then, she burst into loud weeping. Shao tried to comfort her in every way possible, and she finally spoke, saying, "I have a fated connection with the young man, which will be fulfilled in the next day, hence I cannot help feeling so sad!" Hearing this, Shao was deeply distressed and sorrowful, and he wanted to hang himself in the tunnel. The lady stopped him, saying, "Your earthly life is not yet over, and my spiritual essence has not yet transformed. If you were to indulge further in worldly attachments, leading to your untimely death, the underworld would surely impose severe punishment, entangling us in endless complications. Moreover, fate is inescapable; nothing can escape it. Even if you were to sacrifice your life, it would be in vain." Shao then stopped. Jinyan and Dianchan, too, were reluctant to part, and they all prepared food to see Shao off. By morning, the lady presented him with a pair of gold bracelets and a set of jeweled hair ornaments, saying, "These gifts express my sincerity and meaning. Seeing them, you will think of me. We will never meet again, so please take care." She personally saw him off to the gate, covering her face with her sleeves as she returned. Shao was still deeply saddened, with tears streaming down his face. In the blink of an eye, she disappeared from sight. He then relocated to the original inn and prepared to return to Wu. A few days later, Liang came from Xiangyang, and Chen died as a guest in Fang County. They blamed Shao for breaking his promise, but he kept it secret. When he showed them the bracelets and hair ornaments, they were astonished and said, "These are not ordinary objects; they are extraordinary treasures, indeed evidence that you have encountered a fairy!" Shao earnestly advised them not to speak lightly, and thus no one else knew about the encounter.

    114

    同舟归家，及门，则妻死久矣，乃以条脱一枚，投回回肆中卖之，得镪万锭，于虎丘静处建坛，请道士鹤林周玄初设灵宝炼度三昼夜。荐妻正斋之夕，伺道士行朝皆退，亲写心词一封，潜于香炉焚之，以资丽人冥福。醮罢，玄初梦二妇人，一姓张，一姓郑，从二小娃来谢曰：“妾辈俱承善果，已授瑶台金母侍宸矣。” 言讫，驾祥云向西而去。翌日，玄初诘韶曰：“君昨所荐，只主阃张氏，何又有郑氏等三人焉？”韶心知为丽人、钿、雁，佯为不解曰：“吾梦亦如之，然不知彼三人谁也？”卒不以告。知此事者，惟梁生一人。故生有《琵琶佳遇》诗，并附于此。诗云：

    Explanation

    114

    Returning home by boat, upon reaching the gate, he discovered that his wife had been dead for a long time. He then sold one piece of jewelry in a foreign shop and obtained ten thousand taels of silver. In a quiet place in Tiger Hill, he built a platform and invited Taoist priest Zhou Xuanzhu of He Lin to perform the Lingbao ritual for three days and nights. On the evening of the main ritual for his wife, he waited until all the Taoist priests had left, wrote a heartfelt letter, burned it secretly in the incense burner, to benefit the deceased woman in the afterlife. After the ritual, Zhou Xuanzhu dreamed of two women, one surnamed Zhang and one surnamed Zheng, accompanied by two little girls, who thanked him saying, "We have all received good results and have been appointed as attendants to the Queen Mother of the Jade Platform." After they finished speaking, they rode on auspicious clouds westward. The next day, Zhou Xuanzhu questioned Shao, "You only recommended the lady Zhang from the inner chamber, why are there also three others like Zheng?" Shao realized it referred to the beautiful woman, the pearl, and the goose, but pretended not to understand, saying, "My dream was also like that, but I don't know who those three people are." Finally, he did not tell. Only Liang Sheng knows this. Therefore, Liang Sheng wrote the poem 'Pipa Jia Yu' and appended it here. The poem says:

    Poem: Pipa Jia Yu (琵琶佳遇)

    (Translation of the poem would follow here, if provided in the original text.)

    115

    忆昔少年日，加冠礼初成。春衣紫罗带，白马红樊缨。吴中自昔称繁华，回环十里皆荷花。窥红问绿谢游冶，与余共泛星河槎。星槎留连湓浦边，空亭醉访琵琶弦。银篦击节不堪问，锦袜生尘殊可怜！庐山月上犹未去，娉婷玉貌湖边遇。追随钿雁双娇娆，直入金屏最深处。春风东来绽牡丹，洞房香雾滃椒兰。含情惯作雨云梦，鸳枕生愁清夜阑。前朝佳丽夸环燕，图出千人万人羡。太真颜色赵肌肤，绣帐恋灯几回见。情缘忽断两分飞，归来如梦还如痴。缥囊留得万金赠，凄凉忍看徒伤悲！徒伤悲，难再得！当初若悟有分离，此生何用逢倾国！

    Explanation

    115

    Remembering the days of my youth, when I first underwent the coming-of-age ceremony. In spring, I wore a purple silk sash and rode a white horse with red reins. Wuzhong has always been known for its prosperity, with lotus flowers blooming for miles around. I interacted with young women, and we sailed together on a celestial boat. We lingered by the Poyang Lake, getting drunk in an empty pavilion and playing the pipa. I hit a silver comb to keep time, an act that was hard to ask about, and my shoes were covered in dust, which was particularly pitiful! The moon rose over Mount Lu, and I met a graceful and beautiful woman by the lake. I followed a pair of beautiful women, entering the most intimate part of a luxurious setting. The spring breeze brought forth blooming peonies, and in the fragrant and luxurious bedroom, I often dreamed of romantic encounters, which filled me with sorrow in the quiet of the night. The beautiful women of the past were admired by many, and Yang Guifei's beauty was a favorite subject. I repeated my visits to a luxurious setting, where I loved the light. Our emotional bond was suddenly severed, and we separated. Returning, it felt like a dream, and I was as lost as a fool. I received a valuable gift, but the sorrowful feelings were overwhelming! How pitiful, and how impossible to regain! If I had realized there would be separation, why would I have encountered such a captivating beauty in this life!

    116

    韶从此不复再娶，投礼玄初为师，授五雷斩勘之法，往来两浙间，驱邪治病，祷雨祈晴，多有应验。后失所在。近时有人于终南及嵩山诸处见之，疑其得道云。

    鸾鸾传
    赵鸾鸾，字文鹓，东平赵举女也。幼时，家人以香屑杂饮食中啖之，长而体香，故又名香儿。有才貌，喜文词，尤精于剪制刺绣之事。父欲以嫁近邻之才子柳颖，而鸾亦深愿事焉，许而未聘。会颖家坐事，日就零替，鸾母悔之，以适缪氏。缪虽富室，而子弟村朴，目不知书。鸾既嫁，而郁郁不得志，凡佳辰令节，异卉奇葩，辄对之掩镜悲吟，闭门愁坐。景之接于目，事之感于心，一寓于诗，积而成帙，名曰《破琴稿》。既三月，而缪生死，鸾回父母家。次年冬，颖亦丧耦，乃遣人复申前约，而求娶之。举夫妇弗许，颖必欲成其姻，盖闻鸾之贤，而悦鸾之貌也。

    Explanation

    116

    Shao did not marry again after this point. He submitted gifts to Xuan Chiu as his teacher and was taught the Five Thunder Slash and Examine methods. He traveled back and forth between the Two Zhe regions, exorcising evil spirits and treating illnesses, praying for rain and clear skies, and there were many instances of success. Later, he disappeared. Recently, some people saw him in various places in Zhongnan and Songshan Mountains, and it is believed he attained the Dao.

    Biography of Luan Luan
    Zhao Luan Luan, courtesy name Wen Yuan, was the daughter of Zhao Ju from Dongping. In her childhood, her family mixed fragrant powder into her food, and she grew up with a fragrant body, hence she was also called Fragrant Child. She was talented and beautiful, fond of literature, and especially skilled in cutting, sewing, and embroidery. Her father wanted to marry her to the talented scholar Liu Ying, a neighbor, and Luan also deeply wished to marry him, and they agreed but were not yet formally engaged. However, Liu's family fell into misfortune, and their situation deteriorated day by day. Luan's mother regretted it and arranged for her to marry the Miao family. Although the Miao family was wealthy, their children were rustic and uneducated. After marrying, Luan was depressed and unfulfilled. On every festival and holiday, when she saw rare flowers and plants, she would hide her face and weep, then shut herself in her room and sit in sorrow. Scenes that touched her eyes and events that moved her heart, she expressed in poetry, accumulating into volumes, titled 'The Broken Zither Manuscripts.' Three months later, the husband of Luan died, and she returned to her parents' home. The following winter, Liu also lost his wife, so he sent someone to renew their previous agreement and seek to marry Luan again. Zhao Ju and his wife refused. Liu insisted on completing the marriage, because he heard of Luan's virtue and was attracted to her beauty.

    117

    乃廉得穿珠匠妇王妈妈者，出入赵氏甚熟，且言听计从，重贿妈妈，求劝亲焉。兼使私问于鸾，微观其意。妈妈许诺，往赵氏说之曰：“老身久怀一事，屡欲奉告于君，以多故未暇，今适其时，不容更缓，未审公夫妇尊意若何？”举曰：“何事？”妈妈曰：“贤女孀居，服将阕矣。薄闻柳氏复举前盟，公坚执不从，不知成算何向？且始先开口，出自名门。因其家为事贫窘，遂负初意。两下各自缔姻，固已绝望矣。谁想令爱丧夫，颖亦丧妇，殆出前定，似非偶然。况颖学问文才，视昔缪生百倍，不可同年而语。鸾鸾心事，谅必无嫌，更其家温裕，大胜曩时，如颖少年，岂终困者？有婿若此，何忍弃乎？”举闻语，慨然而从。妈妈复密劝于鸾曰：“颖之慕尔，若大旱之望云霓。今尊君既许，好事即谐。然既遇知音，尔不可无一语以答其深意。第恐他日相从，悔之迟矣。”鸾甚然之，而难于启口，乃作书附妈妈曰：

    Explanation

    117

    Thus, a bead worker named Wang Mama, who frequently visited the Zhao family and was known for her obedience and trustworthiness, was discovered. She was heavily bribed to advise the Zhao family on a matter of marriage. Additionally, a private inquiry was made to Luan to observe her intentions. Wang Mama agreed and went to the Zhao family to say, "I have long harbored a matter, wishing to inform you, but due to many reasons, I have not had the time. Now is the right time, and I cannot delay further. I wonder what your esteemed couple's intentions are?" Zhao asked, "What is it?" Wang Mama replied, "Your daughter is a widow, and her mourning period is almost over. I have heard that Liu intends to renew his previous proposal, but you firmly refuse. I wonder where your plans are leading? At first, he proposed, coming from a distinguished family. Because of his family's financial difficulties, he betrayed your initial intentions. Both sides have since married others, and you have already lost hope. Who would have thought that your daughter lost her husband, and Ying also lost his wife? This seems to be predestined, not accidental. Moreover, Ying's scholarship and literary talent are a hundred times greater than those of the past Mu, and they cannot be mentioned in the same breath. Luan's feelings, I believe, will certainly have no objections. Furthermore, his family is more abundant and prosperous than before, and Ying, being young, will not remain in a difficult situation forever. With a son-in-law like this, how can you bear to abandon him?" Zhao heard this and resolutely agreed. Wang Mama then secretly advised Luan, "Ying admires you, like a rainbow after a great drought. Now that your esteemed father has agreed, the good thing will be successful. However, since you have met a true friend, you cannot lack a word to respond to his deep meaning. Only fear that one day when you follow him, it will be too late to regret." Luan agreed wholeheartedly, but found it difficult to speak, so she wrote a letter to attach to Wang Mama, saying:

    118

    妾本良家，幼承慈训，调铅傅粉，深处中闺。执枲治丝，谨循内则。惟知纫针而补缀，未解举案以齐眉！天与荣华，亲怜巧慧。冰为神而玉为骨，蝤如领而手如荑。正及芳年，遴选佳婿，讵期薄命，竟配下流。遂尔辜其出众之才，屈其倾城之貌。敛兹怨悔，寓阙诗词。对月白之宵，遇风清之旦。强与语，强与笑，鸾伴山鸡；触于目，触于心，鹓随野鹜。孰料庸才短折，孱质孤嫠。土木形骸，恶况暂空于眼底；风花情性，幽悰尚郁于尊前。徒怀蔡琰之悲，永抱淑真之恨。已甘弃置，过辱聘求，盖以伸前时之好言，作后日之佳话。诚愿托身贵族，委质明公，挽桓君之鹿车，吹秦娥之凤管。愿毕志以偕老，冀投身而相从。未侍光仪，先申愚悃，惟高明其谅之！

    Explanation

    118

    I am from a respectable family, raised from childhood with kind teachings, applying cosmetics and remaining secluded within the inner chambers. I handled hemp and worked with silk, carefully following the rules of the inner chamber. I only knew how to sew and mend, never understanding the custom of raising a tray to the level of one’s brow. Heaven granted me honor and splendor, and my family cherished my cleverness and intelligence. My spirit was as clear as ice, my bones as pure as jade; my neck was like a蝤, and my hands like tender shoots. At the height of my beauty, I was chosen for a fine husband, yet who could have foreseen my fate—short-lived, ending up married to a man of low station. Thus, my outstanding talent was wasted, my beauty reduced to that of an ordinary woman. I gathered these sorrows and regrets and expressed them in poetry. On moonlit nights and on days with clear winds, I forced myself to speak, forced myself to smile, like a phoenix paired with a pheasant; what struck the eyes and the heart was like a halcyon following a wild goose. Who could have foreseen that a mediocre man would die young, leaving me a weak and lonely widow? My body was but a lifeless form of earth and wood, the bad condition temporarily absent from my sight; yet my romantic and emotional nature still lingered before the wine cup. I carried only the sorrow of Cai Yan, and forever bore the sorrow of Shu Zhen. I have long accepted being cast aside, and it is an overkindness to seek my hand again, for the sake of fulfilling past kind words and creating a tale of virtue for the future. I sincerely wish to entrust my life to a noble family, to submit myself to a wise official, to draw the deer cart of Huán Jūn and to play the flute of Qín É. I wish to complete my aspirations and grow old together, hoping to follow you in death. Before I have had the chance to serve your presence, I first express my humble heart. May the wise and enlightened forgive me.

    妈妈还贺曰：“可谐矣！请以百金为赏。”颖曰：“若余事济，百金岂敢吝惜！”乃出鸾简付颖。颖读而雀跃曰：“真所谓窈窕淑女，吾其可不以琴瑟友之乎？”即卜日纳聘，而续其弦焉。

    119

    The mother congratulated, saying, "It is harmonious! Please offer a hundred gold coins as a reward." Ying replied, "If the matter is successful, how could I be stingy with a hundred gold coins!" He then took out the scroll and gave it to Ying. Ying read it and leaped with joy, saying, "Truly the virtuous and graceful lady, how could I not befriend her with a lute and a zither?" They immediately chose a day to arrange the betrothal and tied the knot.

    On the night of the wedding, Luan privately told Ying, "I am a widow, but I am still a maiden. You must not be unaware." Ying was surprised and asked, "What do you mean?" Luan said, "In the case of Mu Sheng, who was ill, he could not be close to women. Although he was married to her for four months, there was no consummation, and he eventually died. But this matter is known only to my mother; others do not know it." Ying did not believe her, and Luan asked to verify it, and indeed it was not a mistake. After returning home, Ying showed filial piety to her in-laws, was harmonious with her sisters-in-law, treated servants with kindness first, and assisted her husband with diligence and frugality as the foundation. For neighbors who were poor, she helped them according to her ability; for relatives who visited, she treated them with courtesy. Thus, both inside and outside the family praised her. In her leisure, she played with Ying, recited and discussed the Shijing and Chuci, and chanted and expressed emotions. Not worth discussing were her beauty like Wu Jiangxian and her poetic thoughts like Cao Zijian. Ying's cousins, who returned from the capital, recorded six playful verses by the scholar Guan, titled Lanfang.
