    121

    明年，至正戊戌，田丰破东平，颖与鸾相失，莫知所在。已而毛贵复陷东昌，留伪将俞左丞者镇守，俞颇知道理，凡所掠男女，出榜召人识认给还。颖闻之，意鸾或者在彼，冲冒白刃中，求而未得。正忧窘间，有指女冠院语之曰：“盍不于此访求乎？”颖如言去，果见妇女十余人，累然监系；颖问鸾姓名存殁，一妇人答云：“数月前唤去，不在此，盖贤妇人也。可惜！可惜！”颖又问：“娘子何以悉之？”曰：“妾亦良家遭虏，与赵氏处者五阅月。其他人家宅眷，皆污辱于寇，辄得放还。独吾与赵氏及在此数人，誓死不辱，故被囚禁。何时复得见天日也！”言讫，泪下如雨。颖亦洒泣，低声语妇云：“赵氏，余妻也，不知今在何处？”妇曰：“闻有周万户者领去，莫测所之。但临行时，知君必来相觅，留书托我，俾以授君。”即于衣领中取付颖，使急持去，盖恐监者知觉，必遭菙骂。颖开而读之，果妻手笔也。书云：

    Explanation

    121

    The following year, during the fifth year of the Zhizheng era (1348), Tian Feng conquered Dongping. Ying lost track of Luan and did not know where she was. Soon after, Mao Gui reconquered Dongzhou and left a pretend commander named Yu, the Left Chancellor, to garrison the area. Yu was quite knowledgeable about the principles of righteousness and issued a public notice to return all captured men and women to their families. Ying heard of this and suspected that Luan might be there, so he rushed into the danger of sharp blades to search for her but was unable to find her. Just as he was in a state of worry and hardship, someone pointed to the nunnery and said to him, "Why not search for her here?" Following the advice, Ying went to the nunnery and indeed saw more than ten women, all tired and imprisoned. Ying asked about Luan's name and whether she was alive or dead. One woman replied, "She was called away several months ago and is not here. She was a virtuous woman. What a pity! What a pity!" Ying then asked, "How do you know all this?" The woman said, "I too was from a good family and was captured. I lived with Zhao for five months. The family members of other households were all defiled and humiliated by the enemy and were immediately released. Only I, Zhao, and a few others here swore to die rather than be defiled, so we were imprisoned. When will we see the light of day again?" After she finished speaking, tears fell like rain. Ying also shed tears and spoke softly to the woman, "Zhao is my wife. I don't know where she is now." The woman said, "I heard that a man named Zhou, the Commander, took her away, and I cannot predict where she is. But when he left, he knew you would surely come to look for her, so he left a letter with me to give to you." She immediately took the letter out from her collar and handed it to Ying, urging him to take it quickly, for fear that the guards would notice and they would be beaten or scolded. Ying opened and read the letter, which was indeed written by his wife. The letter said:

    122

    妾鸾，爰从出适，忽值凶徒，颠沛流离，艰难痛苦，残骸余喘，与死为邻。备历危疑，幸存贞节。皇天后土，实所鉴临！将殒灭微躯，则自经沟渎。将混同末俗，则亵慢纲常。是以毁坏形容，偷存视息，虽落花无主，暂尔随风；而畜犬丧家，终然恋主。怆惶四顾，憔悴半生。肢体苟完，心胆俱丧。每遇穷檐夜雨，古道秋风。但有凝望眼穿，忆归肠断。壁灯半灭，泪尽眼枯；战鼓争喧，魂飞魄散。已分膏涂野草，血染沙泥。宁饲肉于乌鸢，肯委身于狗彘？效投崖之烈女，慕断臂之贞妻。讵意复被播迁，忽闻消耗，知君无恙。赎妾有期，敢遽捐生，遂更忍死。妾即今见在济南，周其姓氏，万户其官，缘系汉人，差若良善。君得书之后，速备金帛来赎。不宜迁延稽缓，恐一时调拨，则转移他处矣。百年伉俪，一旦分张。覆水再收，拳拳盼望。所宜深虑，早致良图，毋俾妾为阳台不归之云也。伏楮凄断，不知所云。

    Explanation

    122

    Lady Luan,

    Since I left home to marry, I have encountered bandits and experienced a life of hardship and wandering. I have suffered greatly, on the brink of death. I have faced many dangers and doubts, but I have managed to preserve my chastity. Heaven and Earth, indeed, have witnessed my plight! If I were to perish, I would choose to hang myself in a ditch. If I were to merge with the vulgar customs, I would show disrespect to the fundamental principles of society. Thus, I have damaged my appearance and barely survived. Though I am like a flower without a master, carried by the wind, and a dog that has lost its home, I still long for my master. I look around in a state of panic and distress, worn out for half a life. My body is barely intact, and both my heart and courage are lost. Whenever I encounter the hardships of a poor and isolated life and the passage of time, I have intense longing and deep sorrow. The wall lamp is half-extinguished, and I have cried until there are no more tears; the sound of battle drums competes with each other, and my soul and spirit fly apart. I have already accepted that I may be covered with fat on the wild grass and stained with blood in the sand and mud. Rather than be fed to crows and vultures, I would not submit myself to dogs and pigs. I emulate the heroic women who threw themselves off cliffs and admire the chaste wives who cut off their own arms. Who could have thought of being displaced again, suddenly hearing news that you are safe. There is a time to redeem me, and I dare not give up life immediately, thus enduring death even more. I am currently in Jinan, Zhou is my surname, and Wanhu is my official title. Originally a Han person, I am relatively good and kind. After you receive this letter, prepare gold and silk to redeem me. Do not delay, for if I am moved at once, I may be transferred elsewhere. A hundred-year marriage, suddenly separated. Trying to gather spilled water, I hope earnestly. What is needed is deep consideration, achieving good plans early, and not making me a cloud that does not return to the overhang. Writing with great sorrow, I do not know what to say.

    123

    颖得书，则又间关跋涉，达于彼中。万户方拥重兵，赫然声势，未敢轻进，投其邻而安下焉。

    越数日，缉知鸾之在也，而无由以通消息，乃日伺于门。见一巫媪，往来频数，意必府中之亲信人也。候媪出，潜随至家，奉银一锭为寿，而以情告焉。媪曰：“将军夫人妒忌，所掳妇女，皆处于别室，除浣洗衣裳，炊造饮食之外，不容辄出。近亦有给还其亲属者。令妻若在，吾当为玉成。”次日，媪诣第潜问，果得鸾而私报焉。鸾密出一缄，付媪。媪持出以授颖，题曰：《悲笳四拍》。读之流涕，乃就恳媪请于夫人赎鸾。夫人曰：“吾无所用，况其夫在，何忍留之？当即遣还。”颖乃奉珍珠耳榼、黄金排钗各一事于夫人，夫人即呼鸾使颖领去，于是夫妇相携拜辞而出。其曲亦录于此。

    Explanation

    123

    Upon receiving the letter, Ying once again endured a difficult and arduous journey to reach that place. The ten-thousand-household lord was mustering a large force, with a formidable presence, and thus dared not advance lightly; instead, he cast himself upon the mercy of his neighbors and settled there.

    After several days, he learned that his wife Luan was still alive, but had no way to communicate with her. So he waited by the gate every day. He saw an old woman fortune-teller who came and went frequently, and he suspected she must be a trusted person in the household. Waiting for her to leave, he secretly followed her home, presented her with a锭 of silver as a gift, and then told her his situation. The old woman said, "The general's wife is jealous, and all the women she has captured are kept in separate rooms. Apart from washing clothes and preparing meals, they are not allowed to leave even for a moment. Recently, some have been returned to their families. If your wife is still here, I will help you succeed." The next day, the old woman secretly went to the residence to inquire, and indeed found Luan, then privately reported back to Ying. Luan secretly handed over a sealed letter to the old woman, who took it out and gave it to Ying, labeling it: Four Pieces of the Lamenting Flute. As he read it, Ying wept, and then earnestly asked the old woman to request the lady to redeem Luan. The lady replied, "I have no use for her, and besides, her husband is here—how could I bear to keep her? I will send her back at once." Ying then presented the lady with a pair of pearl ear ornaments and a pair of golden hairpins. The lady immediately called for Luan and sent her with Ying. Thus, the couple departed hand in hand, bowing and taking their leave. The melody of Four Pieces of the Lamenting Flute is also recorded here.

    124

    我生之初尚无为，我生之后元运衰。夫与妻兮忽仳离，父与母兮生死安可知！狼烟四起兮沸鼓鼙，锋镝成林兮盛旌旗。人民涂炭兮城郭坏，礼义灭亡兮法度隳。身流落兮天一涯，肠欲绝兮心孔悲！山可平兮河可塞，妾怨苦兮无穷期！

    右一拍

    蜂蚁屯聚兮豺虎嗥，心毒狠兮体腥臊。烟尘澒洞兮人窜逃，寒沙暴骨兮没蓬蒿。亡家遇乱兮伤吾曹，义重命轻兮如鸿毛。誓捐此生兮期不污，仰天俯地兮独烦劳。

    Explanation

    124

    At the beginning of my life, there was still no action; after my birth, the great fortune declined. Husband and wife, suddenly separated; father and mother, who knows if they are alive or dead! Wolf smoke rises all around, drums and gongs resound; spears and arrows form a forest, flags are abundant. The people suffer, cities are destroyed; rituals and righteousness are lost, laws are destroyed. My body is lost, far away in the world; my intestines are about to tear, my heart is deeply sorrowful! Mountains can be leveled, rivers can be blocked; my grievances and sorrows are endless!

    To the right, one beat.

    Bees and ants gather, tigers and wolves howl; the heart is cruel, the body is foul-smelling. Smoke and dust fill the air, people flee; cold sand is covered with bones, buried in weeds. Losing our homes in chaos, we are deeply hurt; duty is heavy, life is light, like a feather. I swear to dedicate my life, hoping not to be tainted; looking up to the sky and down to the earth, I am alone and troubled.

    125

    右二拍

    弃贤俊兮逐凶愚，东西转徙兮卒无宁居。贪淫是乐兮杀戮是娱，所在剽掠兮所过为墟。发冢墓兮焚毁室庐，闺门孱弱兮被虏驱。舍生取义兮捐微躯，谁云女妇兮丈夫弗如？

    右三拍

    行处坐处兮，思念我乡曲。地角天涯兮，不见我骨肉！姑亡舅殁兮家倾覆，逃窜苟活兮被驱逐！伉俪离背兮何时复？幸兹陋躯兮免污辱。谁为义士兮挥金玉？歌行路兮妾身赎。

    右四拍

    颖、鸾既复合，乃相与谋曰：“世方离乱，人不聊生。吾夫妇虽重得团 ，而前途向去，端未可保。莫若远遁于深林大壑中，少避氛埃，以需时泰。”乃隐于徂徕山麓，夫耕于前，妻耘于后，同甘共苦，相敬如宾，冀缺、梁鸿、庞公、王霸，亦未可以优劣论也。乡闾远近，颇化其风。一日，颖出城负米，遇贼获之。曰：“闻公名久矣！当送田将军，任以官职，不患不富贵也。”颖瞠目大骂曰：“斫头贼！吾岂从汝反哉？”贼怒，杀之道上。

    Explanation

    125

    Right Second Section

    Abandoning the wise and virtuous while pursuing the wicked and foolish, wandering east and west, ultimately finding no place of rest. Taking pleasure in greed and lust, and finding entertainment in killing, plundering wherever one goes, leaving ruin in one's wake. Opening tombs and burning down houses, enslaving the weak and vulnerable, sacrificing one's life for righteousness, giving up one's insignificant body. Who says that women are not as capable as men?

    Right Third Section

    Wherever I walk or sit, I think of my hometown. From the ends of the earth, I cannot see my family! My aunt and uncle have died, and my family has been destroyed, fleeing and barely surviving, being driven away! My husband and I are separated, when will we be reunited? Thankfully, my humble body has been spared from dishonor. Who is the righteous person who will spend gold and jade? Singing on the road, I redeem my own body.

    Right Fourth Section

    Ying and Luan have reunited, and they discussed together: "The world is in chaos, people cannot survive. Although we have been reunited, our future is uncertain. It would be better to flee to the depths of the forest and ravines, temporarily avoiding the dust and waiting for better times." They hid in the foothills of Culaishan, the husband plowed in front, the wife followed with planting, sharing both hardships and joys, treating each other with the respect of guests, equally admirable as Jiqie, Liang Hong, Pang Gong, and Wang Ba. Nearby and distant villagers were influenced by their example. One day, Ying left the city to fetch grain and was captured by bandits. They said, "We have heard of your name for a long time! We will send you to General Tian, who will give you an official position, and you will not worry about poverty or lack of wealth." Ying stared in anger and shouted, "Head-chopping bandit! I would not follow you in rebellion!" The bandits were angry and killed him on the road.

    126

    邻舍奔告鸾，鸾走哭，负其尸以归，亲舐其血而手殓之，积薪焚颖，焰既炽，鸾亦投火中死焉。见者惊骇，为之竦然，曰：“古称烈妇，何以加之！”火灭，邻里拾其遗骸葬之，伐石表其冢曰：“双节之墓。”君子曰：“节义，人之大闲也，士君子讲之熟矣。一旦临利害，遇患难，鲜能允蹈之者。鸾幽女妇，乃能乱离中全节不污，卒之夫死于忠，妻死于义。惟其读书达礼，而赋质之良，天理民彝，有不可泯。世之抱琵琶过别船者，闻鸾之风，其真可愧哉！”

    Explanation

    126

    Neighbors rushed to tell Luan of the tragedy, and Luan ran and wept, carrying her body home. He personally licked her blood and dressed her body with his own hands. He then piled firewood and set Ying’s body ablaze. When the flames grew fierce, Luan also threw himself into the fire and died. Those who witnessed the event were shocked and filled with awe, saying, “How can the ancient term chastity heroine be adequate to describe her?” After the fire was extinguished, the neighbors gathered her remains and buried them, carving a stone tablet to mark her tomb, inscribed: “The Tomb of the Two Chaste Ones.” The gentleman said, “Loyalty and righteousness are the great moral boundaries for people; scholars and gentlemen have spoken of them at length. Yet when faced with danger or hardship, few are able to truly uphold them. Luan, a secluded woman, was able to preserve her virtue and remain unstained in times of chaos and separation. In the end, the husband died for loyalty, the wife for righteousness. Only because she read widely and understood propriety, and because her nature was good, could the principles of heaven and humanity not be erased. Those in the world who carry their pipa to other boats, upon hearing of Luan’s virtue, should indeed feel ashamed!”

    127

    凤尾草记
    洪武中，有龙生者，本建康人。远祖仕宋为京官，从隆祐孟太后南迁，留家江右。子孙蕃衍，世守诗书。生行第八，六七岁时，长者教以诗，辄能成诵。九龄晓属对，作五、七言绝句诗皆可观，众以聪明许之。生有姑适祖氏者，特爱生，生往来姑家甚熟。祖有异母兄弟，同居各爨。兄殁，惟嫂练氏及二子三女存。长女、次女皆适人，惟幼女在室，绝有姿容，长生三岁。生虽少年，颖敏而驯谨，不好玩弄，且善伺人意，故祖氏一家闻生来，莫不欢喜。女亦视生如弟兄，不复回避。

    Explanation

    127

    凤尾草记

    During the Hongwu period, there was a man named Long Sheng, originally from Jiankang. His distant ancestor served as an official in the Song capital and followed Empress Dowager Shèngmǔ southward when she relocated the court, leaving his family in Jiangyou. His descendants multiplied, and generations have guarded the classics. Long Sheng was the eighth in his lineage; at the age of six or seven, the elders taught him poetry, and he could recite it immediately. At the age of nine, he understood how to compose couplets, and his five-character and seven-character quatrain poems were all commendable. People regarded him as intelligent. He had an aunt who married into the Zu family, and she particularly loved him. He visited his aunt's house frequently. The Zu family had half-siblings who lived together but had separate hearths. His elder brother died, and only his sister-in-law, Lady Lian, and two sons and three daughters remained. The eldest daughter and second daughter were married, but only the youngest daughter was unmarried and exceptionally beautiful, being three years older than Long Sheng. Although young, Long Sheng was sharp and intelligent yet obedient and cautious, did not like to play, and was good at reading people's intentions. Therefore, when the Zu family heard that Long Sheng was coming, they were all happy. The youngest daughter also regarded him as a brother and no longer avoided him.

    128

    女母闻生姑称生长进好学，深欲婿生，女亦眷眷属目。祖中庭植凤尾一株，已百年，生吟啸其侧。女窥无人，出就生凤尾下，谓生曰：“老母闻令姑说子聪明，欲以我结好，我亦愿为子妻，托令姑主张。第未审子父母之意然否？倘因缘会合，得为夫妇，虽死无憾！不然，我之嫁人，非商家郎，则耕家子，纵金玉满堂，田连阡陌，不愿也。”生应曰：“得子为配，足慰平生。”因指凤尾誓之曰：“若余事成，开花结子；事若不成，根枯叶死。”誓毕，散去。生盘桓祖氏，大小悦之，女尤敬慕。尝亲奉茶与生，生取茶，戏曰：“茶已吃矣，不患不成。”家人闻之，亦不问也。

    Explanation

    128

    The daughter's mother heard that the son-in-law was praised by his mother-in-law for his diligence in learning and deeply desired to marry him. The daughter also looked at him with affection. In the courtyard, there was a phoenix tail plant that had already been there for a hundred years, and the son-in-law recited poetry beside it. Seeing no one around, the daughter came out to the son-in-law under the phoenix tail plant and said, "The grandmother heard that the mother-in-law praised you for your intelligence and wanted to make a good match. I also wish to be your wife, entrusting the mother-in-law to arrange it. But I am unsure if your parents agree. If fate brings us together and we can be husband and wife, I will have no regrets even if I die. Otherwise, I will only marry a merchant's son or a farmer's son, even if the house is filled with gold and jade, and the fields stretch far and wide, I would not want it." The son-in-law replied, "If I can have you as my partner, it will be enough to satisfy my life." He then pointed to the phoenix tail plant and swore, "If the matter succeeds, the plant will bloom and bear fruit; if it fails, the roots will wither and the leaves will die." After the oath, they parted. The son-in-law stayed at the grandmother's house, and everyone was pleased with him, especially the daughter who admired him greatly. She once personally served tea to the son-in-law, and he took the tea, playfully saying, "The tea has been drunk, so there is no worry that the matter will not succeed." The family heard about it but did not question it.

    129

    会生姑与练妯娌参商，阳为怂恿，阴实沮之，故生父母犹豫，女未知也。生以告女曰：“子既未便开亲，我亦不即纳聘，当与老母谋，必得子为妇而后已。”女家贫，未尝有缯纩之饰，粉黛之施，而荆钗布裙，略无垢污，下至足缠，亦洁白如雪。兼之赋性和柔，婉娩特甚，机杼之精，剪制之巧，为一族冠。二嫂酷妒之，女不较也。生重其为人，愈有伉俪意，然艰得良媒，姑又不力赞，两下迁延，迟迟岁月。生既冠，去事举子业，女家踪迹稀矣。然女念生，未尝去怀，惟母知其情，喻之曰：“吾又遣人往彼，谈汝姻事，早晚当有定议，汝勿煎熬，徒损容貌。”逾时，生至，虽主姑家，而意在于女。留数日，二嫂俱归宁，女独纺小楼上。楼下一深巷，通后园，巷半砖砌磴道以登。生从园中还，闻女纺声，径奔女所。女见生来，喜气溢面，辍纺叙礼，与生对坐，且纺且谈。因以己年庚告生，使生推算，卜其谐否。又与生话家事甚悉。生感其意，口占一诗赠之。诗曰：

    Explanation

    129

    The bride's mother and her sister-in-law were at odds, appearing to encourage the marriage while secretly hindering it. As a result, the groom's parents were hesitant, and the bride was unaware of the situation. The groom told the bride, "Since you are not yet ready to marry, I will not immediately propose. I will discuss this with my mother, and we will only proceed once you agree to be my wife." The bride's family was poor, and she had never worn fine silk or applied makeup. She wore a simple pine hairpin and a cotton skirt, which were always clean, and even her foot bindings were as white as snow. She was gentle and submissive, and her skills in weaving and sewing were unmatched in her clan. Her two sisters-in-law were very jealous of her, but she did not hold it against them. The groom admired her character and grew more affectionate towards her, but finding a good matchmaker was difficult, and his mother did not offer much support. Both sides delayed, and the matter dragged on for a long time. After the groom came of age, he pursued a career in government service, and the bride's family rarely visited. However, the bride always thought of him, and only her mother knew her feelings. She advised her, "I will send someone to talk about your marriage. We will have a decision soon. Do not worry, as it will only damage your appearance." After some time, the groom returned, though he lived with his mother-in-law, his thoughts were always with the bride. He stayed for a few days, and both sisters-in-law returned to their parents' homes. The bride was alone on the upper floor, spinning thread. Below was a deep alley that connected to the back garden, with half of it paved with brick steps. The groom returned from the garden and heard the sound of the bride spinning. He ran straight to her. The bride saw him and her face was filled with joy. She stopped spinning, greeted him, and sat opposite him, continuing to spin and talk. She told him her birth year, asking him to calculate if they were compatible. She also spoke in great detail about her family affairs. The groom was moved by her sincerity and composed a poem to give her. The poem said:

    [The poem would follow here, but since it is not provided in the source text, it is omitted in this translation.]

    130

    曲栏深处一枝花，秾艳何曾识露华？素质白攒千瓣玉，香肌红映六铢纱。金铃有意频相护，绣幄无情苦见遮。凭仗东皇须着力，向人开处莫教差。

    女不甚读书，识字而已，语生曰：“子宜解说，俾我闻之。”生一一敷绎其义。女笑曰：“他日得侍房帏，子必教我，我虽愚暗，久当能之。”生曰：“妇人女子，偏是聪明，以子慧心，学之易易。”因代为答诗曰：

    Explanation

    130

    In the deep recesses of the winding railing, a single flower blooms, its rich color never knowing the grace of dew. The pure white petals gather like a thousand jade petals, and the fragrant flesh is red and shines like a six-zhu silk. The golden bell has an intention to frequently protect it, but the embroidered canopy, though beautiful, cruelly hides it. Rely on the eastern king to exert strength, and when it opens to people, do not let it be wrong.

    The woman did not read much, knowing only a few characters. She said to the man, "You should explain it to me so that I can understand." He explained the meaning step by step. The woman smiled and said, "One day when I serve in the inner chambers, you must teach me. Though I am foolish and dim, I will surely learn it after some time." The man replied, "Women are particularly clever. With your wise heart, learning it will be easy." He then composed a poem on her behalf, saying:

    (Translation of the poem would follow here if provided in the original text.)

    131

    深谢韶光染色浓，吹开准拟倩东风。生愁夕露凝珠泪，最怕春寒损玉容。嫩蕊折时飘蝶粉，芳心破处点猩红。金盘华屋如堪荐，早入雕栏十二重。

    生复缕缕为详诗意。女曰：“常闻子才调敏捷，今观信然，使我倾仰弥切！”因目生久之，曰：“子精神意气，决非庸人，后当贵显。我欲以蒲柳之质为托者，非有他也，以父早亡，母年渐老，长兄书写公门，次兄陷身吏役，二嫂悍恶，子所深知。但得远离凶犷，获托丝萝，子纵无官，不为命妇，亦不失为士君子妻。万一流落俗子手中，有死而已！惟子念之图之。”生自初悦其貌，不料其淑懿有识若此，自是拳拳婚议，惟恐蹉跎。俄而女兄果以吏败，家事亦落。生父母无意缔盟，谢而辞之，遂觖望矣。生私作长歌一篇寄焉。歌曰：

    Explanation

    131

    Deeply grateful that the bright spring light has colored her so intensely, I await the gentle east wind to blow it open. I give rise to sorrow as evening dew condenses into pearl-like tears, and most fear that the spring cold will mar her jade-like beauty. When the tender buds are broken, they scatter like butterfly dust; where the fragrant heart is broken, it leaves a spot of scarlet red. If the golden plate and splendid house are suitable for offering, may she soon enter the twelve-tiered carved railings.

    The young man then carefully explained the meaning of the poem. The woman said, “I have often heard of your quick wit and eloquence; now I see it is indeed as they said, and I admire you even more!” She gazed at him for a long time and said, “Your spirit and bearing are certainly not those of an ordinary person; you will surely rise to wealth and honor. I wish to entrust my humble self to you, not out of any other reason, but because my father died early, my mother is growing old, my eldest brother serves in officialdom, my second brother is trapped in bureaucratic duties, and my two sisters-in-law are harsh and cruel—these are things you already know well. If only I may escape from such a harsh fate and find refuge in your embrace, even if you have no official rank, you will not be a lady of rank, but you will not lose the status of a wife of a scholar or gentleman. Should I ever fall into the hands of a vulgar man, I would rather die! Please, then, think of me and consider my fate.” At first, the young man had been pleased by her beauty, but he had not expected her to be so virtuous and wise. From that moment on, he was earnestly devoted to the idea of marriage, fearing only that it might be delayed. Soon after, the woman’s elder sister indeed fell due to corruption in office, and the family’s fortunes also declined. The young man’s parents had no intention of forming an alliance, and so they politely declined, leaving him in despair. In private, he composed a long song to send to her. The song said:

    132

    我昔正髫年，笑骑竹马君床边。手持青梅共君戏，君身似玉颜如莲。爱我聪明耽笔砚，枿棨文章紫骝健。风鬟雾鬓绯染唇，凤尾丛边几回见。层楼窈窕洞房深，春纤缕缕抽冰线。蹇修不来奈若何？罗带同心竟乖愿！绣襦甲帐隔天涯，未解离魂学张倩。君知许嫁谁人家，我行射策黄金殿。回首清河梦寐中，目断巫山泪如霰。

    一日，女母留姻戚家，二嫂寻衅，与女大闹。女深处闺阁，性复良善，莫敢出言，又不能骂，然不胜愤。兼之秦约晋盟，遽然断绝，凄凉憔悴，踽踽无聊。是夕，竟缢死楼上。母归，哭之恸，手自洗殓，于胸前得一绣囊，密贮杏笺一幅，视之，乃生所寄之诗也。母不违其意，仍置棺中。生闻女死，托以省姑，走吊焉。至则珠沉璧碎，玉殒花飞，将入木矣。生涕泪如雨，悲不能堪，送归葬所，掩圹成坟而归。

    Explanation

    132

    I was once a child, my hair tied in a topknot, laughing and playing with you on the bed with bamboo horses. Holding green plums, we played together, your body as pure and delicate as a lotus flower. You admired my intelligence and my dedication to writing, my articles as strong and healthy as a purple steed. Your hair styled like wind and mist, your lips dyed red, we met many times by the phoenix tail. In the deep and secluded inner room, my delicate fingers worked with fine threads. If the matchmaker does not come, what can be done? The red sash and the heart's promise were broken! The embroidered robe and the military tent were separated by great distances, I did not understand the soul's departure like Zhang Qian. Do you know whom you are betrothed to? I passed the imperial examination in the golden hall. Looking back in my dreams, my tears fell like snow on Mount Wu.

    One day, the girl's mother left her at the home of her relatives, and her two sisters-in-law provoked her, causing a big commotion. The girl, deep in her inner room, was inherently kind, dared not speak, and could not curse, yet she was overwhelmed with anger. Moreover, the Qin alliance was suddenly broken, leaving her desolate and weary, wandering aimlessly. That night, she hanged herself in the upper room. Her mother returned, wept bitterly, washed and dressed her body herself, and found a embroidered bag on her chest, containing a secret note with a plum-colored paper, which turned out to be a poem I had sent her. Her mother honored her wish and placed the poem in the coffin. I heard of her death, excused myself to visit my aunt, and went to mourn her. Upon arrival, it was like a pearl sinking and a jade breaking, a flower falling and a gem shattering, about to be buried. My tears flowed like rain, I was heartbroken, sent her back to her burial place, covered the grave, and returned.

    133

    后数年，生果高科要职，烜赫于时，虽别娶妻妾，意不忘女。常与天师无为张真人论鬼神，偶及女事。真人见生切切，为飞章拔之。载数日，生梦女曰：“妾从辞世，二十余年，阴府查籍，以妾当生三子，寿至六十，数未克终，卒于非命，俾再为女人，了其夙业。而昨蒙真人道力，天符忽下，今往河南府洛阳县在城胡氏家为男子矣。感君深爱，生死不忘，但恨无以奉报耳。然君方当富贵，位极人臣，福寿丰隆，子孙昌盛。”言讫，拜谢而去，行数步，复回顾曰：“郎善自珍，妾永逝矣！”倏然而灭。生既觉，殆无以为怀。遣人往女家，视凤尾，枯死已数年矣。生遂作《哀凤尾歌》云：

    Explanation

    133

    After several years, the man indeed attained a high-ranking and important position, becoming famous and influential at the time. Although he took other wives and concubines, his feelings for the woman did not change. He often discussed ghosts and spirits with the Taoist immortal Master Zhang Wuwei, and accidentally mentioned the woman's affairs. The immortal saw that the man was deeply concerned and wrote a petition to heaven to rescue her. After several days, the man dreamed of the woman, who said, "I left the world more than twenty years ago. The underworld checked the records and found that I should have given birth to three sons and lived to sixty years old, but the number was not completed, and I died prematurely. I was reborn as a woman to complete my past karma. But yesterday, I was rescued by the immortal's spiritual power, and a heavenly decree suddenly came down. I have now been reborn as a boy in the Hu family in the city of Luoyang, Henan. I am deeply grateful for your love, which I will never forget, even in death. But I regret that I have nothing to repay you. But you are now in a position of wealth and honor, holding the highest office, enjoying great fortune and longevity, and having many prosperous descendants." After finishing her words, she bowed and left. After walking several steps, she turned back and said, "Take good care of yourself, and I will go on forever!" Suddenly, she disappeared. After waking up, he felt deeply moved. He sent someone to the woman's home to see the phoenix tail, which had been dead for several years. He then composed the "Lament for the Phoenix Tail" song, saying:

    134

    有草有草名凤尾，仙人种在丹山里。世间百卉避芳菲，珊瑚宝树差堪比。鬖髿绝似凤凰翎，号以佳名同凤称。海上行迟珠露湿，洞箫品彻彩云停。娟娟旎旎犹贞静，琉璃刻叶琅玕柄。九苞健翮时下来，五色奇文烂相映。日影照耀晴筛金，盛夏翛翛风满林。艳阳不作桃李态，晚岁实坚松柏心。华堂清处摇新翠，曾与飞琼翠阴会。倚丛未许暂偷香，指树惟期终作配。那知万事终非真，幽芳淑质俱成尘。绮槛灵根凋百岁，绣房丽色殒三春。凤兮偶昨来过此，弄玉台倾凤尾死。鸳鸯瓦落野棠青，孔雀屏欹土花紫。感时抚旧恨悠悠，碧羽琼蕤万古休。败砌颓垣蛩吊月，荒烟老树鸟啼秋。花草重栽春又绽，镜破钗离永分散。因歌凤尾寓深衷，留与多情后人叹。

    Explanation

    134

    A Plant Named Phoenix Tail

    There is a plant called Phoenix Tail, sown by immortals in the mythical Dan Mountain. In the world, all flowers avoid its fragrance, and it can be compared to coral trees. Its appearance is extremely similar to the tail of a phoenix, and it is given a good name, named after the phoenix. On the sea, it moves slowly, and its dew is like pearls. The sound of a flute playing under the colorful clouds stops, and it remains graceful and elegant, maintaining purity and tranquility. Its leaves are carved like glass, and its stem is like jade. Occasionally, the phoenix with its strong wings descends, and its five-colored patterns brightly reflect. Sunlight shines through the leaves like gold, and a gentle breeze fills the forest during summer. It does not have the appearance of peach and plum blossoms, but in its later years, it is as steadfast as pine and cypress trees. In a splendid hall, it sways with new green, and it has met with flying jade in the green shade. Leaning on it, one is not allowed to briefly steal its fragrance, and pointing to the tree, one only hopes to eventually become a match. How could one know that all things are not truly real, and its subtle fragrance and good quality turn to dust? The spiritual root withers over a hundred years, and the beautiful color perishes in three springs. The phoenix came here yesterday, and the phoenix tail died on the platform for playing music. The wild tangerine is green, and the peacock screen leans with purple soil flowers. Feeling the time and touching the past, there is endless regret. Green feathers and jade clusters forever rest. Ruined steps and collapsed walls, crickets mourn the moon. Desolate smoke and old trees, birds sing in autumn. Replanting and spring blooming again, a broken mirror and separated hairpin, forever separated. Because of singing about the phoenix tail, expressing deep feelings, leaving for future generations to lament.

    135

    武平灵怪录
    齐仲和，名谐，漳州人。本富家子，粗有学问，颇能文章。然豪侠不羁，用财如粪土。至正壬辰，红巾寇乱，家业为之荡然。遂东西奔走，寄食于人。尝往来武平项子坚家为馆客。子坚故微，骤然发迹，欲光饰其门户，故婚嫁必攀援阀阅，炫耀于人。名宗右族之贫穷不振者，辄与缔姻，此则慕其华腴，彼则贪其富贵。书翰、启札、奁册、衣录之类，皆仲和粉饰，不知者谓为真衣冠家矣。洪武五年，子坚死，二子荣可、贵可特盛襄事，葬子坚监汀山中，距其居五十里。仲和为述行状，请铭于宋太史景濂，且筑归全庵于墓侧，宏伟壮观，俨然一坊，割田二百亩饭僧，仍请南华本如真公主庵事。状元金溪吴伯宗记之。仲和往返，庵适当途，过必留宿。是岁有小干，往福州，为人留馆者数载。已而贵可辟孝廉，除嘉兴府同知。倭夷登岸，失不以闻，被罪，死秋官狱中。家产籍没，庵田入官，僧悉散去。

    Explanation

    135

    The Wuping Record of Strange Events
    Qi Zhonghe, whose given name was Xie, was from Zhangzhou. Originally the son of a wealthy family, he had a basic education and was quite skilled in writing. However, he was a bold and unrestrained man, spending money as freely as if it were dirt. In the year Renchen of the Zhizheng era, during the Red Turban Rebellion, his family's estate was completely destroyed. He then wandered east and west, living off the generosity of others. He often stayed at the home of Xiang Zijian in Wuping as a guest scholar. Xiang Zijian was originally humble, but suddenly rose to prominence, wanting to adorn his family's reputation. Therefore, he insisted on marrying into noble families, showing off to others. He would marry the poor and unprosperous members of prominent clans, who admired their wealth, while they coveted his riches. Letters, invitations, marriage contracts, and other documents were all embellished by Zhonghe, and those who did not know him thought he came from a true gentry family. In the fifth year of the Hongwu era, Xiang Zijian died, and his two sons, Rongke and Guike, made a grand funeral arrangement, burying him in the Jianting Mountain, fifty miles from their residence. Zhonghe wrote an account of his life and asked Song Lian, the historian, to compose an epitaph for him. He also built the Guquan Temple beside the tomb, which was grand and impressive, resembling a pavilion. He set aside two hundred acres of land to provide food for the monks and requested that Nanhua Benru, a nun, manage the temple's affairs. The imperial scholar Wu Bozong from Jinxixi recorded this. Zhonghe would travel back and forth, and the temple was conveniently located on the route, so he would always stay there when passing by. That year, there was a minor official named Xiaogan who went to Fuzhou and stayed as a guest scholar for several years. Later, Guike was appointed as a scholar-official and became the deputy magistrate of Jiaxing Prefecture. When Japanese pirates landed on the coast, he failed to report it, was punished, and died in the prison of the Ministry of Punishment. His family property was confiscated, the temple's land was taken over by the government, and the monks all dispersed.

    136

    洪武乙丑，仲和归，往访项氏，抵庵暮矣，遂假宿焉，不知项亡而庵废。行入方丈，寂无人声，遍视僧房，或开或阖。最后，至一室，僧坐榻上，闻人足音，讶曰：“谁耶？”仲和告以姓氏，僧暗中应曰：“然则故人也，请坐！”仲和询僧名，对曰：“山僧初有幻体，君及见之，今已忘之耶？”仲和莫晓为何等语，复诘：“余僧安在？”曰：“偶赴水陆斋会于施主家，惟山僧久患风痹，不能下床，故在庵耳。惜行童俱出，不意公来，茗供俱无，乏物奉待。”仲和告以未饭，僧曰：“案上有残豆数合，公若不嫌，请取食之。”仲和馁甚，撮而嚼焉。因问项氏动履。

    Explanation

    136

    In the year Gengwu Yichou of the Hongwu era, Zonghe returned home and went to visit Xiang, arriving at the hermitage in the evening. He stayed for the night, unaware that Xiang had died and the hermitage had been abandoned. He entered the main hall, which was silent with no human sound, and looked around the monk's rooms, noting that some were open and some were closed. Finally, he entered a room where a monk was sitting on a couch. The monk heard footsteps and asked, "Who is there?" Zonghe identified himself, and the monk, in the dark, replied, "Then you are an old acquaintance, please sit!" Zonghe asked the monk his name, and the monk responded, "This mountain monk once had an illusionary body. You have seen it, but have you forgotten it already?" Zonghe did not understand what the monk was talking about and asked again, "Where are the other monks?" The monk said, "I happened to attend a water and land feast at a layperson's house. Only this mountain monk has been suffering from rheumatism for a long time and cannot get out of bed, so I am here at the hermitage. I regret that the novice monks are all out, and I did not expect you to come, so there is no tea or offering." Zonghe informed the monk that he had not eaten, and the monk said, "There are several handfuls of leftover beans on the table. If you do not mind, please take and eat them." Zonghe, being very hungry, picked them up and chewed them. He then asked about Xiang's movements.

    137

    僧曰：“故无恙。”仲和倦，欲求寝。僧曰：“此中有数客，每夕来就山僧闲谈，少选当至，恐公不安。”仲和问：“何人？”曰：“皆近村良家，亦有与项宅亲戚者。”仲和喜曰：“若然，幸甚！”须臾，二人先入，五人继到。僧曰： “今日偶值项宅旧客下顾，留宿于此，诸公勿讶！”仲和就请众宾清誉。先至者曰：“余石子见、毛原颖也。”继至者曰：“余金兆祥、曾瓦合、皮以礼、上官盖、木如愚也。”仲和谢曰：“烛灯俱无，不敢行礼，乞不见罪。”众应曰：“既为项氏馆宾，又是山门熟客，相与一家，何罪之有？”遂共僧讲论，辩若悬河，亹不休，深造佛谛。

    Explanation

    137

    The monk said, "Therefore, there is no harm." Zonghe was tired and wanted to sleep. The monk said, "There are several guests here who come every night to chat with me in idleness. They will soon arrive, and I fear it may make you uncomfortable." Zonghe asked, "Who are they?" The monk replied, "They are all from nearby respectable families, and some are related to the Xiang family." Zonghe was pleased and said, "If that is the case, how fortunate!" Soon after, two people entered first, followed by five more. The monk said, "Today, some former guests of the Xiang family have come to visit and will stay overnight. Please do not be surprised!" Zonghe then asked the guests for their names and reputations. The first group said, "We are Shi Zijian and Mao Yuanying." The second group said, "We are Jin Zhaoxiang, Zeng Waha, Pi Yili, Shangguan Gai, and Mu Ruyu." Zonghe apologized, saying, "There are no candles or lamps, so I dare not perform the ritual. Please do not hold it against me." The guests responded, "Since we are all like one family, what blame could there be?" They then joined the monk in a discussion, arguing as if a river were hanging, unceasingly, and deeply attaining the truth of Buddhism.

    138

    僧曰：“诸公久得禅悦，当避机锋，然文士在席，何不且辍空谈，更裁佳句，以为清宵欢乐之资乎？”众曰：“诺！”子见先吟曰：

    尝擅文房四宝称，尽夸鸲眼胜金星。华笺法帖长为侣，圆镜方琴巧制形。铜雀坠台成凤咮，玉蟾吐水带龙腥。莫欺钝寿浑无用，曾与维摩写佛经。

    原颖诗曰：

    Explanation

    138

    The monk said, "You have long attained the joy of meditation; you should avoid sharp, pointed questions. However, since scholars are present, why not temporarily stop idle talk and instead compose better verses to provide entertainment for a clear, joyful night?" The group replied, "Agreed!" Subsequently, one of them began to recite:

    "Once renowned for the four treasures of the study, it boasts eyes sharper than gold stars. Fine paper and calligraphy scrolls are constant companions, while round mirrors and square zithers are skillfully crafted. The fallen tower of the copper bird becomes the beak of a phoenix, and the jade toad spits water with a dragon's scent. Do not underestimate my dull and long-lived self; I have once written Buddhist scriptures for Vimalakirti."

    The original poem by Yuan Ying said:

    139

    早拜中书事祖龙，江淹亲向梦中逢。远夸秦代蒙恬巧，近说吴兴陆颖工。鸡距蘸来香雾湿，狸毫点处腻朱红。于今赢得留空馆，老向禅龛作秃翁。

    兆祥诗曰：

    身残面黑眼生沙，弃置尘埃野衲家。僧病几回将煮药，客来长是使煎茶。无缘不复劳烹饪，有漏从教老岁华。昔日炎炎今寂寂，莫将冷热向人夸。

    瓦合诗曰：

    家贫无庇欲依谁？散木微躯久觉衰！孔圣绝粮宁敢愠，范丹乏米岂辞饥。当年坠地无须顾，此日生尘不可炊。榾柮烟消灰烬冷，蒸蒸跨灶欲何为？

    以礼诗曰：

    幻身如絮太轻松，惯覆卢能与赞公。里裂不因儿恶卧，缯穿只为匠难逢。尘灰积久无人洗，虮虱生多欠火烘。零落半归虫鼠蠹，固知色相本来空。

    上官盖诗曰：

    常人髹漆贵人朱，生者憎嫌死者需。除是飞升无用我，若还解化也须余。能函盖世英雄骨，解殓倾城艳冶躯。寄语劳劳尘世客，百金莫惜预先储。

    Explanation

    139

    Early appointed to a high office serving under Emperor Qin Shi Huang, I once met Jiang Yan in a dream. Praising the skill of Meng Tian from the Qin dynasty and Lu Ying from Wu, the brush dipped in ink, the mist of fragrance wet, the cat's whisker pen point filled with rich red. Now, I have won the right to stay in an empty hall, growing old in a temple as a bald monk.

    Zhaohang's poem says:

    My body is broken, my face blackened, my eyes like sand, abandoned in the dust of the world, a wild monk's home. The monk has been sick several times, ready to boil medicine, visitors always make tea. Without opportunity, there is no need to cook, impermanence teaches the passage of time. Once fiery, now silent, do not boast about the cold and heat to others.

    Waihe's poem says:

    Poor and without shelter, who can I rely on? A weak and scattered body has long felt old! Confucius, despite hunger, did not dare to be angry, Fan Dan, lacking rice, would not refuse hunger. When I fell to the ground, I did not need to care, today, covered in dust, I cannot cook. The firewood smoke dissipates, the ashes grow cold, the steam rises from the stove, what is the point?

    Yili's poem says:

    My body is like a light, too easily blown away, used to cover the simple monk and the praise of the master. The fabric tears not because of the child's bad sleep, the silk wears through because the craftsman is hard to find. Dust accumulates for a long time, no one cleans, lice and fleas multiply, lacking fire to dry. Half decayed, returned to the worms and mice, it is known that form and appearance are inherently empty.

    Shangguan Gai's poem says:

    Common people use lacquer, nobles use vermilion, the living hate, the dead need. Unless I fly to immortality, I have no use for my body, if I am to be transformed, I must still use it. Able to preserve the bones of heroes, able to preserve the bodies of beautiful women. I advise the busy people of the world, do not hesitate to spend a hundred gold to prepare in advance.

    140

    如愚诗曰：

    长须古鬛骨棱棱，心腹虚空不减增。早悟有身应有患，可堪无佛更无僧。频依鹫室行将腐，久想龙门去未能。朽木枯骸禅寂味，一宵清话胜闻经。

    吟毕，抚掌大笑，旁若无人。忽风约云开，月光穿户，隐隐见诸人状貌，或矮而体方，或瘠而头锐，或墨面而一臂甚长，或乌帽而一躯极短，徐行者翩翩然而披毡，屹立者亭亭焉而倚壁。最后一老，颈若生鳞，仲和异之。方欲谛视，僧忽曰：“清风先生罗本素至矣。”众皆起迎。

    遥见一叟，缟衣竹杖，态度闲雅，两袖翩翩，摇摆而行。揖众客而言曰：“诸友今夕之吟，乐乎？”原颖曰：“先生何后也？”各诵所作呈之。先生曰： “诸公自道甚佳，但不免为外客所怪。”以礼曰：“客虽未耄，然早晚当与上官公同载矣，抑又何伤？”先生语僧曰：“吾师何故吝作？”曰：“待公来同赋耳。” 乃朗吟曰：

    Explanation

    140

    As Ru Yu said in his poem:

    With long, ancient whiskers and a bony, rugged appearance, my heart and belly are empty, neither increasing nor decreasing. Early on, I realized that having a body entails suffering; how can I bear it when there are no Buddhas or monks to guide me? I have frequently stayed in a hermitage and am now on the verge of decay, yet I have long desired to go to the Longmen Grottoes but have not been able to do so. Like a decaying piece of wood and a dried-up skeleton, I still experience the taste of Zen. A single night of clear conversation is more valuable than hearing scriptures.

    After finishing, he clapped his hands and laughed loudly, as if no one else were around. Suddenly, the wind dispersed the clouds, and moonlight streamed through the door, faintly revealing the appearances of others. Some were short and stocky, some were thin with sharp heads, some had black faces and one very long arm, and some wore black hats and were extremely short. Those who walked slowly did so with grace and wore felt robes, while those who stood upright did so and leaned against the wall. The last person was an elderly man with a neck that seemed to have scales, which surprised Zhong He. As he was about to closely examine him, a monk suddenly said, "Mr. Qingfeng Luobensù has arrived." Everyone rose to greet him.

    From a distance, they saw an old man in white robes and a bamboo staff, with a leisurely and elegant demeanor. His sleeves fluttered as he walked, swaying gracefully. He bowed to the guests and said, "Did my friends enjoy their poetry tonight?" Yuan Ying replied, "Why did you arrive so late, Mr.?" Each recited their own works and presented them. Mr. Qingfeng said, "Your self-praise is good, but it is not without fault as it may be strange to outsiders." Yi Li said, "The guest is not yet old, but they will eventually be in the same carriage as Mr. Shàngguān, and there is no harm in that." Mr. Qingfeng said to the monk, "Why is my teacher reluctant to compose?" The monk replied, "I will compose together with you when you arrive." Then, he loudly recited:

    厌见阎浮劫火红，荒山独守化人宫。三千世界都成幻，百二山河尽属空。衣藓乱生悲佛毁，床头不扫笑僧慵。难寻物外逃禅侣，罕遇桥边入社翁。猛虎每游莲座下，怪禽多宿绣幡中。青苔满院新经雨，黄叶飘龛乍起风。一对金刚蜗篆面，几尊罗汉鼠穿胸。残经缺字函函损，古器成精件件雄。广殿窗开留月照，闲门锁脱倩云封。谩怜衰朽烟霞骨，莫起摧颓土木躬。良夜岂期佳客集，清吟况与故人逢。案间残豆充饥腹，梁上深煤染病容。行入轮回归败坏，不须辛苦笑疲癃。庄严未必成三昧，游戏何妨运六通。梅子熟时圆觉性，松枝偃处记遗踪。欲知吸尽西江意，只听晨鸡与暮钟。

    Explanation

    141

    Weary of seeing the red fire of the world-ending conflagration in Jambudvipa, I stand alone in the desolate mountains, guarding the palace of the transformed. The three thousand worlds have all become illusion, and the hundred and twenty rivers and mountains are all empty. Moss grows wild on the robes, grieving the destruction of the Buddha; the monk's bed remains untidy, and he laughs in lazy apathy. Hard to find are those who have fled to Chan practice beyond worldly concerns, and rare indeed to meet the elders who have joined a society by the bridge. A fierce tiger often roams beneath the lotus seat, and strange birds often dwell within the embroidered banners. Green moss covers the courtyard, freshly washed by rain; yellow leaves drift through the shrine as a sudden wind arises. A pair of Vajras bear faces like snail carvings, and several Arhats have rats piercing through their chests. Damaged scriptures, missing characters—each scroll is in disrepair; ancient artifacts have become spiritual, each one mighty. The wide hall’s windows open, letting the moonlight remain; the idle door, unfastened, is sealed by the clouds. In vain do I pity the withered bones of those who once wandered through mist and clouds; do not let the decay of wood and stone stir sorrow in you. On this fine night, could I have expected a gathering of noble guests? To sing in quiet harmony is to meet with old friends. A few beans remain on the table, filling my hungry belly; deep soot on the beams stains my sickly face. To walk into the wheel of samsara is to return to decay; there is no need to toil and suffer for the weak and worn.庄严未必成三昧, 游戏何妨运六通. When the plum ripens, the nature of perfect enlightenment is revealed; where the pine branch lies fallen, the trace of the past is remembered. To know the full meaning of drawing in the waters of the Western River, listen only to the morning cock and the evening bell.

    The Gentle Wind Master highly praised its marvels and also sang, saying:

The shape encircles and embraces, winding around in harmony, indeed a creation of heaven and earth. At that time, the two filial sons of the Xiang family buried their father here and guarded the tomb. They rebuilt the monastery and invited the True Master from afar to be the abbot.     After a brief while, the moon set and its light faded, the distant rooster crowed to announce the dawn, and the guests suddenly dispersed, not knowing where they had gone. Zhonghe stepped outside and saw a desolate, empty hermitage. Returning to search for the sick monk, he found only a clay statue. Looking at the date inscribed on the back, he realized it was the statue he had seen when he first stayed in the hermitage, now worn away. He finally understood the mountain monk's words, "This is an illusionary body, which you have witnessed." Entering another room, he found only a broken inkstone propped against the door and a worn-out brush lying on the ground, with mouse droppings piled up on the desk. He thought about the leftover beans he had eaten, realizing they must have been the source. There was also a worn-out quilt and an old fan, a steamer covered in dust and almost broken, a pot with no handle and half worn through, a wooden fish hanging from the pillar, and a coffin lid leaning against the wall. Zhonghe was greatly frightened and ran out of the door. Walking for miles, he finally came across a house and sought refuge there. The host said, "This place is deserted and full of strange occurrences. Where did you stay last night?" Zhonghe explained everything. The host replied, "How dangerous it was! Your life was at risk."

    He was then told: "The Xiang family has suffered misfortune; their tomb has collapsed and been destroyed. The official's cover became a coffin, and the plain cloth became an old fan. These items you saw have been turned upside down and have caused confusion. Recalling the words 'I will travel with the official,' he realized he would not recover and refused medical treatment. Taking medicine and seeking medical treatment is only self-torture!' After another half a month, he finally died. Alas! Can one not call Zhonghe a broad-minded and open-hearted man?"

    琼奴传
    琼奴，姓王氏，字润贞，常山人。二岁而父殁。母童氏，携琼奴适富人沈必贵，沈无子，爱之过己生。年十四，雅善歌辞，兼通音律，德、言、容、功，四者咸备，远近争求纳聘焉。时同里有徐从道、刘均玉者，请婚尤切。徐本华胄而清贫，刘实白屋而暴富。徐之子名苕郎，刘之子名汉老，皆仪容秀整，且与琼奴同年。必贵欲许刘，则鄙其阀阅之卑微；欲许徐，则虑其家道之穷迫，犹豫迟疑，莫之能定。

    The Biography of Qiong Nu

    Qiong Nu, surnamed Wang, courtesy name Runzhen, was from Changshan. At the age of two, her father died. Her mother, surnamed Tong, brought Qiong Nu to marry into the wealthy family of Shen Biguai. Shen had no children of his own and loved Qiong Nu more than his own child. At the age of fourteen, Qiong Nu was excellent at poetry and lyrics and also proficient in music theory. Virtue, speech, appearance, and talent, all four were present in Qiong Nu. People from far and near competed to offer marriage proposals for her. At that time, in the same village, there were Xu Congdao and Liu Junyu, who proposed marriage especially urgently. Xu Congdao was of noble lineage but poor, while Liu Junyu was from a humble background but suddenly rich. Xu Congdao's son was named Tao Lang, and Liu Junyu's son was named Han Lao. Both were elegant and well-groomed in appearance, and they were the same age as Qiong Nu. Shen Biguai wanted to agree to Liu Junyu but looked down on his lowly lineage; he wanted to agree to Xu Congdao but worried about his poor family situation. He hesitated and wavered, unable to make a decision.

    一日，谋于族人之有识者，彼为之画策曰：“但求佳婿，勿论其他。”必贵曰：“然则何以知其佳乎？”曰：“易耳！子盛为酒食，特召二生，仍请前辈之善藻鉴者，使潜窥之，一则观器量之如何，二则试词翰之能否，择其善者而从焉，于选婿乎何有！”必贵深然之。至二月花晨，开筵会客，凡乡里之号名胜者，咸集于庭。均玉、从道，亦各携其子而至。汉老虽人物整然，雍容应对，而登降揖让，未免矜持。苕郎则眉目清新，言谈儒雅，衣冠朴素，举止自如。

    One day, he consulted with knowledgeable relatives, and they devised a plan: "Just seek a good son-in-law, without considering other factors." Mr. Biqu asked, "But how can we know if he is good?" They replied, "It's easy! Prepare a feast, especially invite two young men, and also invite elders who are good at discernment to secretly observe them. First, observe their demeanor and capacity; second, test their literary skills. Choose the best one and follow him. What difficulty is there in choosing a son-in-law?" Mr. Biqu agreed wholeheartedly. On a flower-filled morning in February, he opened a banquet to entertain guests. All the well-known scholars and gentlemen from the village gathered in the courtyard. Junyu and Congdao also brought their sons. Despite his composed and dignified appearance, Old Han was somewhat stiff in his greetings and bows. In contrast, Tao Lang had fresh and clear features, spoke in a scholarly manner, dressed simply, and moved with ease.

    Among the guests was one named Gengyun, the clan leader of the Shen family, renowned for knowing people. Upon seeing the two young men, he silently discerned their merits and demerits. He then publicly declared to the crowd, "My nephew will surely be noble, and he has a daughter of marriageable age. Mister Xu and Mister Liu, who wish to seek a good match, are both excellent in character and appearance, but it is uncertain which one will be the match." The nephew stood up and replied, "If this matter is handled by the elders, it will be good." Gengyun said, "In ancient times, there were customs such as shooting at screens, pulling threads, and setting up mats, all of which were used to select a husband. I differ from these methods." He then called the two young men forward and pointed to the four paintings hanging on the wall: "Spring Morning with Early Flowers," "Night Moon and Late Sleep," "Moon in Hand from Water," and "Scent of Flowers on the Clothes." He said, "Younger Brother, please express your thoughts and try to compose verses. Winning the eyes or taking the clothes, all depends on this one attempt." How unfortunate that Han Laosheng, living in a wealthy household, is lazy about poetry and books, and upon hearing the command, looked around for a long time without responding. Tiaolang, however, calmly took up his brush and completed the task in a moment. When he presented it, Gengyun praised it repeatedly. The poem read:

    The dawn breaks through the petals of the peach blossom,
    Heavy dew falls like snow from the fragrant tea plant.
    Vivid purple shades the embroidered window,
    Soft red hues cast a slanting shadow on the swing ropes.
    The sound of the well wheel startles me awake from my dream,
    I rise to comb my hair, but have no time to stand before the dressing table.
    Laughing, I call the maid to hold the bright candle,
    First to see if the crabapple blossoms have opened.

    149

    Tong's family member was slightly unwell, and Tao entered to inquire about the illness. While Qiongnu was attending to her mother with medicine and soup, she was unaware of Tao's arrival and was unable to avoid him, leading to their meeting at the mother's bedside. Tao, upon seeing her, was struck by her exceptional beauty. He secretly felt delighted and enclosed a sheet of red paper, sending a maid to deliver it to Qiongnu. When she opened it, she found it blank. With a smile, she composed a poem in response to Tao:

    "Scarlet sunset paper illuminates the face with a blush,
    What is the matter, jade man, with too much emotion?
    Elegance is not without good verses,
    But the two characters of longing cannot be written."

    Tao, holding the poem, boasted about it to Hanlao. Hanlao, however, was jealous of Tao's growing affection for Qiongnu and accused him of being too emotional. He then falsely accused Tao of wrongdoing, leading to Tao and his family being exiled to Liaoyang and Shenzhen, respectively. At the time of their departure, they were heartbroken, and those who witnessed the scene could not help but shed tears. They then parted ways, and news of each other ceased. Later, Tong's family fell into decline, and only Tong's mother and daughter remained, living in a humble inn by the roadside, selling wine to passersby. Although they were in hardship, Qiongnu's beauty had faded, but her youthful grace remained extraordinary. A Wu commander, admiring her, wished to marry her as a concubine, but Tong refused, as she had already been promised to another.

Fu submitted a memorial to report the matter. After two months, approval was granted, and an official was ordered to interrogate the case, but the body could not be found. During the investigation, a whirlwind rose before the hall. The official prayed, "If the spirit of the deceased knows, guide me there." The family of the woman also received official support and was provided for throughout their lives.

    The Record of Meeting Immortals at Manting Pavilion

    Du Zengcheng, a reclusive scholar from Baqiu, was residing in Jianyang. He had a noble and lofty spirit, and he cherished the mountains and forests. He owned a small boat, in which he kept a writing desk, a tea stove, fishing gear, and a wine jar. He often wandered leisurely along the Nine Bends of the Clear Stream, and people also praised him for his distinctive and admirable character.

    One day, during the eighth month, after the rain had cleared, a cool breeze filled his sleeves. Du Zengcheng followed the current, drifting along the river, and let himself be guided by the flow. Soon, his boat came to rest by a rock. Looking up at the rock, he saw green vines and emerald tendrils, red osmanthus and dark bamboo, with lush shade and a faint, pleasant fragrance. He tied up his boat and stepped ashore, walking leisurely without a specific destination. Suddenly, a stone gate appeared before him, and the path was flat. Du Zengcheng realized he had entered a strange and unusual place, and he was delighted and excited to move forward. He felt the warm and bright sun, the clear and fresh air, and truly, it was a different and favorable place. After about two li, he entered a large city. The city was grand and imposing, with strict guards and a golden plaque that read, "The True Realm of Manting Pavilion," indicating that it was governed by the deity of Wuyi Mountain. After another li, he saw tall trees, beautiful houses, and high walls, with flowing water, flying flowers, and the sounds of roosters and dogs. He saw a distant building with a high-pitched roof, overlooking a clear pool, and the sign read, "The Qingbi Daoist Temple." Du Zengcheng approached the temple, where monkeys and cranes were tame and docile, and the fragrance of orchids and lilies was浓郁. Under the shade of willow trees, two children stood. Du Zengcheng bowed to them and asked where they were. The children replied, "The Master Qingbi has been waiting for you for a long time."

    156

    ”因入白。须臾，复出，导僎成前进。经数处，云窗雾阁，敻异人间；瑶树琼林，自同天上。最后抵一轩馆，清碧幅巾大带，容貌俨雅，坐于中间。僎成再拜。清碧曰：“汝知人间有京兆杜伯原乎？吾是矣。汝，吾族子也。小子识之。”僎成跪谢：“晚生不及承教训。”久之，问宗党及虞、杨、范、揭诸君子后裔之详。僎成应对，历历可听。清碧若有喜色。少焉，童子进百花茶，僎成啜罢，略不知饥。迨暮，宿之别室，楮衾练帐，石枕竹床，风露凄然，睡不成寐。惟棂间明月窥人，飞雪入户，自非神完气充，骨坚志定者，弗能居也。明日，召僎成饭，鹿脯一盘，胡麻一器，然芳馨甘美，味实非常。饭毕，将辞而出，清碧曰：“此中群仙别馆，诸执丈皆游戏于兹。来日当集吾舍，将乞其诗文，送汝归去，姑少俟。”僎成又大喜过望。

    "Entering to report, he soon reappeared and led 僎成 forward. Soon, a young boy brought in a pot of tea made from a hundred flowers, which 僎成 drank, barely feeling hungry. As evening fell, he was given a separate room for the night, with paper bedding and linen curtains, a stone pillow and bamboo bed, the wind and dew chilling, making it impossible to sleep. Only the moonlight through the window and the snowflakes entering the room made it clear that one must be spiritually and physically strong, with firm resolve and determination, to endure such conditions. The next day, the figure summoned 僎成 for a meal, presenting a plate of venison and a bowl of sesame seeds, which were fragrant and delicious, truly extraordinary.     157

    次早，果有褒衣巍冠，瑶琚玉佩者七人至，皆风度凝远，气象超凡。清碧起迎，长揖而坐。僎成鹄立拱手，屏息户外。一仙忽顾之曰：“是儿何为来哉？” 清碧云：“族子僎成也。吾昔居世，累辞征辟，而潜心著述，今皆散逸。独《春秋诸传正义》四十八卷仅存，平生精力，尽在此书，皆诸公所知者。故尝贮以石函，锁以金钥，藏于玉笥覆箱峰之北岩。近因蛟蜃作孽，水激穴开，而函露矣。深惧愚夫窃发，盖冥数未可以传于人代，故召来命归窒之耳。”因相与论诸传之得失。一仙曰：“《春秋》宣父手笔，不比他经，而诸儒以管窥蠡测，拘拘然指一字为褒贬，岂圣人之心乎？大抵圣经所书，有常有变，难执一而论。首王人，次封爵，常也。主会主兵，谋纵谋逆，几于变矣。

    Explanation

    157

    The next morning, indeed there were seven people who arrived, all dressed in broad, loose robes and tall, majestic hats, adorned with jade ornaments. Each had a dignified and extraordinary presence. Qingbi rose to greet them, bowed deeply, and then sat down. Zhencheng stood like a crane, bowing with clasped hands, holding his breath outside. One of the immortals suddenly turned to him and asked, "Why is this child here?" Qingbi replied, "He is my nephew, Zhencheng. I once lived in the world, repeatedly declining official appointments, and devoted myself to writing. Now, all my works have been lost, except for the Commentary on the Spring and Autumn Annals in forty-eight volumes, which contains all my life's efforts. This is something all of you are familiar with. I once stored it in a stone box, locked with a golden key, and hidden in a cave on the north side of Fubao Peak. Recently, due to the disturbances caused by dragons and sea monsters, the water surged and opened the cave, exposing the box. I am deeply afraid that ignorant people might steal it, as fate has not yet allowed it to be passed on to human generations. Therefore, I summoned you to seal it up." They then discussed the merits and flaws of the various commentaries. One of the immortals said, "The Spring and Autumn Annals is the work of Confucius himself, unlike other classics. Yet, scholars try to interpret it through narrow perspectives, rigidly assigning meanings to individual words, which is not in line with the mind of a sage. Generally, the sacred texts record both constant and changing matters, making it difficult to interpret them with a single viewpoint. For example, the first entries are about kings and envoys, followed by titles and fiefs, which are constant. However, when it comes to hosting meetings, leading armies, plotting rebellion, or conspiring to overthrow, these are matters of change."

    158

    然而托始立法，拳拳宗周，王必曰天王，正必曰王正，文、武、成、康之威灵，俨乎其对越，拨乱反正，盖为天下后世计，而以为为鲁而作，岂圣意哉？”一仙曰：“伯原公之意如何？”清碧曰：“昔人谓三传作而《春秋》散，散则散矣，然三传亦未容以轻议也。盖《公羊》《穀梁》专释经，而《左氏》专载事，至唐啖氏、赵氏，始毫分缕析，辨明义例，合三家之要而归之一。

    Explanation

    158

    Though it begins by establishing laws, it is earnestly devoted to the Zhou dynasty; the king is necessarily called the "Son of Heaven," and righteousness is necessarily called the "king's righteousness." The spiritual power of Kings Wen, Wu, Cheng, and Kang is solemnly present before us. To restore order and correct wrongs is done for the sake of the world and future generations — yet to suppose that it was written solely for Lu, could this be the intention of a sage? One sage said, "What was the view of Master Boyuan?" Qingbi replied, "Ancient scholars said that when the Three Commentaries were composed, the Spring and Autumn Annals became scattered. Though they are scattered, the Three Commentaries themselves are not to be lightly criticized. The Gongyang and Guliang Commentaries focus solely on interpreting the text, while the Zuo Commentary focuses solely on narrating events. It was not until the Tang dynasty scholars Dàn and Zhao that they began to dissect every detail, clarify the principles of interpretation, and unify the essential insights of all three into one."

    159

    陆淳亲承赵氏之学，又著《纂例》《辨疑》《微旨》三书，其文可谓粲然，而其学可谓粹然矣。宋朝诸儒所述，皆明白正大，词严义密，无余蕴，但胡康侯主于讽谏，‘高宗复仇’，未免微有牵强处。故朱子尝曰：胡氏说《春秋》，已七八分，但未到洒然处。良有以也。又若张洽之传，王氏《谳议》等书，皆能发先儒之未发，论其精妙，而无遗憾则未也，其至者惟伊川乎！”已而设宴，笾豆具陈，肴则黄精玄芝，乐则朱弦绿绮。郁金鬯，迭劝更酬，侍从使令，执事有恪，莫敢少謦咳。饮既撤，乃重焚香篆，再进茶瓯。

    Explanation

    159

    Lu Chun personally inherited the teachings of the Zhao school and wrote three books, Zuanli, Bianyi, and Weizhi. His writings can be described as clear and bright, and his scholarship can be described as pure and refined. The works of the scholars of the Song dynasty are all clear and straightforward, with precise language and closely reasoned meanings, leaving nothing unsaid. However, Hu Kanghou, who focused on admonition, had a slight degree of forced interpretation in his discussion of "King Gaozong's Revenge." Therefore, Zhu Xi once said: "Hu Kanghou's interpretation of the Spring and Autumn Annals is about 70-80% correct, but it has not reached a state of complete clarity." There is good reason for this. Zhang Qia's commentary and Wang's Yan Yi and other works all reveal new insights from previous scholars, discussing their subtleties, but they are not yet complete. The ultimate authority lies in the teachings of Cheng Yi. Afterward, a banquet was set up, with ritual vessels and dishes arranged.     The Biography of Hu Meiniang

    Huang Xing was a postal station attendant in Xinzheng. One day, he went out and returned at night, feeling tired and resting under a tree. He saw a fox pick up a human skull and wear it, bowing to the moon. Suddenly, the fox transformed into a woman, about sixteen or seventeen years old, who was extremely beautiful. She was crying on the road in Xinzheng, crying while walking. Huang followed her from behind, observing her. The fox did not expect to be seen by Huang, so she acted cute. Huang thought to himself, "This is a valuable commodity that can be kept." He then asked, "Who is this woman, and why is she walking alone at night?" She replied, "I am from Hangzhou. My surname is Hu, and my name is Meiniang. My father was transferred to Shaanxi, and we were robbed by bandits in the village. My parents and siblings all died at the hands of the bandits, and all my possessions were lost. Only I hid in the tall grass and survived until now. Now I am alone and have no place to rely on, and I will throw myself into the water to die, so I am crying here." Huang said, "My family is poor, but we still have enough food. My wife is kind and good, and she can accept you. Can you stay with us?" The woman bowed and thanked him with tears, saying, "Seeing your kindness, you are truly like a second father and mother to me." She followed Huang to his home, and he repeated the previous words to Huang's wife. The wife saw that the woman was gentle and compliant, and she treated her well, but Huang never mentioned the reason.

    时进士萧裕者，八闽人，新除耀州判官。过新郑，与新郑尹彭致和为中表兄弟，因访致和。致和宿之馆驿。黄兴供役驿中，见裕年少，迭宕非端士，且所携行李甚富，乃语妻曰：“吾贫行可脱矣。”因欲动裕，数令媚娘汲水井上，使裕见之。裕果喜其艳也，即求娶为妾。兴曰：“官人必欲娶吾女，非十倍财礼不可。” 裕不吝，倾赀成之，携以抵任。媚娘赋性聪明，为人柔顺，上自太守之妻，次及众官之室，各奉绿罗一端，胭脂十贴。事长抚幼，皆得其欢心。由是内外称誉，人无间言。其或宾客之来，裕不及分付，而酒馔之类，随呼即出，丰俭举得其宜。暇则躬自纺绩，亲缲蚕丝，深处闺房，足不履外阈。裕有疑事，辄以咨之，即一一剖析，曲尽其情。裕自诧得内助，而僚采之间，亦信其为贤妇人也。

    上清杀伐雷府分司，照得：二气始判，而天高地下，自此奠其仪；三才已分，而物化人生，亦各从其类。念幅员之既广，慨狐魅之滋多。缉木叶以为衣，冠髑髅而改貌。击尾出火以作祟，听冰渡水而致疑。所以百丈破因果之禅，大安入罗汉之地。再思多佞，难逃两脚之讥；司空博闻，能识千年之怪。况萧裕乃八闽进士，七品命官，而敢荐尔腥臊，夺其精气。投身驿传之卒，作配缙绅之流。恣乌合而弗惭，怀豕心而未已。绥绥厥状，紫紫其名，过可文乎？言之丑也！郡城隍失于觉察，权且姑容。衙土地乃尔隐藏，另行究治。其青丘之正犯，论黑簿之严刑，押赴市曹，毙于雷斧。使虎威之莫假，庶兔悲而有惩。九尾尽诛，万劫不赦。耀州衙速令清净，新郑驿永绝根苗。长闭鬼门之关，一准酆都之律。布告庙社，咸使风闻。

    Explanation

    169

    上清杀伐雷府分司，照得：二气始判，而天高地下，自此奠其仪；三才已分，而物化人生，亦各从其类。念幅员之既广，慨狐魅之滋多。缉木叶以为衣，冠髑髅而改貌。击尾出火以作祟，听冰渡水而致疑。所以百丈破因果之禅，大安入罗汉之地。再思多佞，难逃两脚之讥；司空博闻，能识千年之怪。况萧裕乃八闽进士，七品命官，而敢荐尔腥臊，夺其精气。投身驿传之卒，作配缙绅之流。恣乌合而弗惭，怀豕心而未已。绥绥厥状，紫紫其名，过可文乎？言之丑也！郡城隍失于觉察，权且姑容。衙土地乃尔隐藏，另行究治。其青丘之正犯，论黑簿之严刑，押赴市曹，毙于雷斧。使虎威之莫假，庶兔悲而有惩。九尾尽诛，万劫不赦。耀州衙速令清净，新郑驿永绝根苗。长闭鬼门之关，一准酆都之律。布告庙社，咸使风闻。

    The Office of Punishment in the Upper Pure Thunder Palace decrees: When the two primary forces (yin and yang) first differentiated, heaven became high and earth low, thus establishing their order; when the Three Talents (heaven, earth, and humanity) were distinguished, all things and human life followed their respective categories. Considering the vastness of the territory, one laments the proliferation of foxes and demons. They weave leaves into clothing and wear skulls to alter their appearance. They strike their tails to produce fire and cause mischief, and listen to ice crossing water to create suspicion. Thus, Master Baizhang broke the cycle of karma in his Zen teachings, and Dashi entered the realm of Arhats. Reishin, who was overly flattering, could not escape ridicule from his two legs; Sikong, with his broad knowledge, could recognize strange phenomena from a thousand years ago. Moreover, Xiao Yu, a scholar-official from Fujian with a seventh-rank appointment, dared to recommend you, a stinking demon, to steal their vital energy. They took on the form of postal servants and mingled with the gentry. They freely gathered without shame, harboring the heart of a pig and not ceasing. Their appearance is despicable, and their names are vile; can such actions be justified? They are indeed shameful! The city god failed to detect this, and so we temporarily tolerate it. The local land deities hid you, and so we will investigate and punish them separately. The chief culprit from Qingxiu will be judged by the strict laws of the Black Register, dragged to the marketplace, and killed by the thunderbolt axe. To ensure that the tiger's power is not abused, we hope to deter even the timid rabbit. All nine-tailed foxes will be exterminated, and they will not be forgiven for a thousand kalpas. The office of Ya Zhou must be quickly cleansed, and the New Zheng Post Station must be forever rid of its roots. They will be permanently closed off at the gate of Ghost City, following the laws of Fengdu. This will be announced in temples and shrines, so that all may hear of it.

    170

    俄而黑云滃墨，白雨翻盆，霹雳一声，媚娘已震死阛阓矣。守卒僚属往视，乃真狐也，而人髑髅犹在其首。各家宅眷，急取其所赠诸物观之，其绿罗则芭蕉叶数番，胭脂则桃花瓣数片，以示于裕，裕始释然。尹公命焚死狐，瘗之僻处，镇以铁简，使绝迹焉。然后取丹砂、蟹黄、篆香与裕服，而拂袖归山，飘然不顾矣。裕疾愈，始以娶媚娘事告太守，遣人于新郑问黄兴。兴已移居，家道殷富，不复为驿卒。盖得裕聘财所致耳。始略言嫁狐之实于人。询者归，具以告太守。众乃信狐之善惑，而神澹然之术焉。

    Explanation

    170

    Shortly after, dark clouds rolled in like ink, and heavy rain poured down as if from an overturned pot. A thunderclap shook the earth, and Méiniáng was struck dead in the bustling market. The guards and officials went to investigate and found that she was a real fox, with a human skull still attached to her head. The families quickly retrieved the gifts she had given them and examined them. The green silk was revealed to be several layers of banana leaves, and the rouge was just a few peach blossom petals. They showed these to Yù, who finally felt relieved. The magistrate ordered the dead fox to be burned and buried in a remote place, with an iron tablet placed over it to prevent her from returning. Then, he took cinnabar, crab roe, and seal incense for Yù, and with a sweep of his sleeves, he returned to the mountains, leaving without a care. Yù recovered from his illness and then informed the magistrate about his marriage to Méiniáng, sending someone to Xinzheng to inquire about Huáng Xīng. Huáng Xīng had already moved to a new residence, and his household was now prosperous, no longer serving as a postal worker. It was said that his wealth came from the dowry provided by Yù. Yù briefly explained the truth of marrying a fox to the people. The inquirer returned and reported everything to the magistrate. The townspeople then believed that the fox was skilled at deception, and they were amazed by the mysterious and calm technique of Dàndàn.

    洞天花烛记
    天历二年，己巳之岁，于潜秀才文信美，偶出游。至半道，忽有二使，布袍葛屦，联袂而来。长揖于前曰：“华阳丈人薰沐奉请。”文仓卒辞避曰：“信美，天目之鄙人；华阳，地肺之灵境。仙凡既隔，造诣何由？”二使曰：“已办轩车，愿无多让！”遂与同行，果有竹兜子一乘候道左。信美既上，舁去如飞，顷刻即至。使者偕信美入。丈人玉冠绡衣，秉简出迓，且致辞云：“僭越奉邀，曲承枉顾，幸勿以牵率见罪也。”与之抗礼，并坐于堂。茶罢，出杯，珍馔罗列，丈人亲执盏于信美前曰：“老夫叨处洞天，久思闲逸。而男婚女嫁，尚尔关心。今弱息及笄，议姻震泽，将纳其次子为婿。佳期式届，聘礼已临，诸事皆备，惟回书未得人耳。稔闻名士，尤擅才华，特此攀迓，无非借重。”命左右取笔、砚、鸾笺，置于几案之上。信美肘若神运，思如泉流，挥洒无停，略不经意。其词曰：

    Explanation

    171

    The Record of Heavenly Lanterns

    In the second year of the Tianli era, during the year of Jisi, the scholar Wen Xinmei from Yuqian went out for a walk. Halfway through his journey, suddenly two messengers appeared, dressed in simple robes and wearing straw sandals, walking side by side. They bowed deeply before him and said, "The Master of Huayang invites you respectfully after bathing and dressing in clean clothes." Wen Xinmei hastily declined, saying, "I am but a humble scholar from Tianmu; Huayang is a sacred realm of the earth's core. The realms of immortals and humans are separated; how can one reach such a place?" The messengers replied, "We have prepared a carriage for you; please do not refuse!" They then accompanied him, and indeed, a bamboo palanquin was waiting on the side of the road. After Wen Xinmei got in, they carried him away like a bird in flight, and in an instant, they arrived at their destination. The messengers led Wen Xinmei inside. The master wore a jade crown and a silk robe, holding a bamboo tablet as he welcomed them, and said, "I have overstepped my bounds by inviting you; I humbly accept your visit. Please do not blame me for being compelled." He treated Wen Xinmei with respect, and they sat together in the hall. After tea, the master poured wine, and a feast of delicacies was laid out. He personally held a cup in front of Wen Xinmei and said, "I have long lived in this heavenly realm and have been longing for leisure. However, I still care about matters of marriage. My youngest daughter is now of marriageable age, and we have arranged her marriage to Lake Tai. We will take our second son as her husband. The auspicious day is approaching, and the wedding gifts have arrived. Everything is ready, except for the reply letter, which we have yet to find someone to deliver. We have heard of your fame, especially your talent, and we specially invite you to assist us."

    He then ordered the attendants to fetch a brush, inkstone, and fine paper, placing them on the table. Wen Xinmei wrote as if guided by a divine hand, his thoughts flowing like a spring, writing continuously without stopping, seemingly without much effort. The words he wrote were:

    [The text of the poem or literary work would follow here, but it is not provided in the source text.]

    172

    福地阴阳合，洞天谐二圣之缘；龙池岁月深，水府缔万年之好。专凭兔颖，虔覆鸾缄。恭维震泽主者顺济昭祐王亲家阙下：乾坤粹气，星斗寒芒。果证真仙，受穹质于上界；位齐海渎，膺显号于明时。为霖运仁静之施，体道存智动之用。涓流必纳，廓其量于有容；众派爰归，汇其涯于无际。久著朝宗之望，夙推润下之功。视事坐鱼鳞堂，班行肃睦；休退宴玳瑁殿，歌舞婵妍。官联天上之豪华，庙食吴中之绵远。民虔崇于香火，世尊仰于威灵。福禄攸同，商农均赖。某志耽冲素，体法谦虚。通籍金门，生杀忝司于下土；秉钧玄省，朝参幸近于清光。既交邻壤之欢，仍羡华腴之盛。如令嗣某颙卬闻望，允为白面绣衣郎；小女某婉娩听从，讵谓红楼富家女？仁厚慕象贤之公子，肃雍愧下嫁之王姬。自顾何人，敢辞非耦。宜其家，宜其室，纳征式谨于初盟；投以桃，投以李，将意莫酬于厚贶。长春不老，永世齐芳。

    Explanation

    172

    In the blessed land where yin and yang harmonize, the celestial realm aligns the destinies of the two saints; the dragon pool, with its deep years, establishes a bond of a thousand years in the aquatic realm. Relying solely on the rabbit's brush, I respectfully cover the phoenix's seal. I respectfully address the ruler of the Lake of the Thunder God, the benevolent and auspicious King, and his family: the pure essence of heaven and earth, the cold brilliance of stars and constellations. Truly becoming a true immortal, receiving the essence of the heavens from the upper realm; holding the position equal to that of the rivers and seas, receiving a distinguished title in clear times. Implementing the benevolent and tranquil influence of rain, embodying the way and preserving the use of wisdom and action. Even the smallest streams must be included, broadening its capacity through inclusiveness; all streams converge, gathering their shores into the boundless. Long-standing reputation for loyalty and devotion, early recognition of the nourishing power of water. Administering affairs in the Fish Scale Hall, with a solemn and harmonious order; retiring to the Tortoise Shell Palace for feasts, with graceful dances and beautiful music. Holding a position linked to the heavenly splendor, enjoying a temple feast in the distant Wu region. The people devoutly worshiping incense and fire, the world venerating the divine power. Blessings and fortunes are shared, merchants and farmers equally rely on it. I am devoted to simplicity and humility, embodying the law of modesty. Holding a position at the Golden Gate, managing life and death in the lower realms; holding the balance in the Dark Province, fortunate to attend court close to the clear light. Having established friendly relations with neighboring lands, I still admire the splendor of the prosperous regions. My son, with a distinguished reputation, is indeed a young man in fine robes; my daughter, gentle and obedient, is not a rich girl from a high-rise building. Kind and respectful, I admire the noble young man; solemn and elegant, I feel humble to marry the princess. Considering myself, who am I to refuse such a match? Suitable for his family, suitable for his home, the initial engagement is solemnly observed. Returning a peach with a plum, the generous gift cannot be adequately repaid. Eternal youth, forever fragrant.

    173

    丈人读既，称叹再三，遂留宿，以光华烛之会。于是遣价赍书，遍请附近洞府群仙，壮观礼席。

    至日骈集，车马之多，旗麾之盛，盖世所未有。丈人顶九旒之冠，佩五岳之图，被赤霜之服，肃客于别殿。俄而千驺万骑，迭鼓鸣笳。翠盖文旍，拥雕鞍之先后；绣裳衮服，俨珠履之尊崇。灯烛辉煌，笙歌嘹亮。侍者走报：“新婿及门也。”群从起迎，引入幕次。忽内间传命，索催妆诗甚急，而婿所带相行之人，艰涩殊甚。从者数十辈，络绎不绝。婿缉知信美在座，私下遣人致浼。信美即代之为诗曰：

    玉镜台前亸绿鬟，象牙梳滑坠床间。宝钗金凤都簪遍，早出红罗绣幔看。

    十八鬟多气力娇，妆成不觉夜迢迢。风流自有张生笔，留取双眉见后描。

    媒将以入，众皆喝采。但见红妆百队，画烛两行，箫管喧阗，香风淡荡，引婿入洞房合卺。执事者又忘将撒帐文来，左右皆失色。婿呼媒耳语，复使出致浼信美。信美立撰付之曰：

    Explanation

    173

    The elder had finished reading, and he praised it repeatedly, then stayed overnight, joining the splendidly illuminated gathering. He then sent messengers with letters to invite all the immortals from nearby caves and palaces, creating a grand and magnificent spectacle.

    On the day of the event, they gathered in a line, with an overwhelming number of carriages and horses, and a splendid display of flags and banners, something unprecedented in the world. The elder wore a ceremonial crown with nine tassels, carried a map of the Five Great Mountains, and donned a red, frost-like robe, receiving guests respectfully in a separate hall. Soon, a thousand horsemen and riders, with rhythmic drumming and horn blowing, arrived. They were followed by green canopies and embroidered banners, and the guests, dressed in embroidered robes and ceremonial garments, were led into the tent with great respect. The lights were bright, and the music was melodious. A servant ran to report, "The new groom has arrived at the door." The groom's entourage rose to greet him and led him into the private area. Suddenly, a message was sent from inside, urgently requesting a poem to hasten the bride's makeup. However, the groom's attendants found the task extremely difficult. Dozens of people came and went continuously. The groom realized that his trusted advisor, Xian Mei, was present and privately sent someone to ask for help. Xian Mei immediately composed the following poem and handed it over:

    Before the jade mirror stand, the green hairpins droop,
    The ivory comb slides down to the bed. With golden hairpins and phoenix ornaments, she is fully adorned,
    Come out early to see through the red brocade and embroidered curtains.

    With eighteen hairpins, she is full of youthful vigor,
    Unaware of the long night, the wind and charm are all in Zhang Sheng's pen,
    Leave the double eyebrows to be painted after the makeup is done.

    The matchmaker led her in, and everyone cheered. They saw a hundred rows of red-dressed women, two lines of painted candles, loud music, and a gentle fragrance, leading the groom into the bridal chamber for the wedding ceremony. The attendant forgot to bring the scattering text, and everyone was startled. The groom whispered to the matchmaker, asking her to send someone to ask Xian Mei for help. Xian Mei immediately composed the following text and handed it over:

    174

    伏以絪昷未判，固溟涬之无形；清浊既分，便刚柔之有对。粤从开辟之始，已生配匹之名，至道所存，大婚尤谨。恭维震泽新婿郎君，华阳元姬淑女，早钟间气，夙孕真姿。礼乐文章，端可作吴彩鸾之倩；功容言德，允宜为王君迥之妻。绯桃自泛于灵源，红叶肯题于流水。天作之合，神相其成。惟化工不离于阴阳，而道妙造端乎夫妇。曲房窈窕，罗帏翠被郁金香；盛服辉光，火浣单衣绣方领。揭盖露珠冠之饰，交杯互玉斝之尝。锦褥平铺，软衬金莲之袜；黛螺浓染，轻描偃月之眉。二姓百年，一双两好。燕婉既谐于伉俪，绸缪宜合于瑟琴。于以采蘩，于以采苹，克谨烝尝之荐；载弄之璋，载弄之瓦，行膺莞簟之祥。合欢讵让于名花？并蒂宛同于奇果。哕哕似朝阳之凤，嗈嗈类春渚之鸿。响动帏屏，幔蹙龙鳞之轻细；梦回鸳枕，口含鸡舌之芳馨。奇逢已遂于结褵，善颂更陈于撒帐。请歌词语，庸助欢声。

    Explanation

    174

    Considering the primordial chaos, when the formless void had yet to be divided, and the clear and turbid had not yet separated, there was no distinction between hard and soft. Since the beginning of creation, the concept of pairing and matching has arisen; where the ultimate Dao resides, the great marriage is especially solemn. May the newlywed groom from Zhenze and the virtuous maiden of Huayang, born under auspicious celestial influences and endowed with true beauty from birth, be praised. Her grace in ritual, music, and literature is truly worthy of comparison to Wu Cailuan’s elegance; her virtue, appearance, speech, and morality make her eminently suitable as the wife of Wang Junjiang. Like a red peach blooming from the sacred spring, and a red leaf inscribed with poetry upon the flowing stream, their union is a match made by heaven, with the divine aiding in its fulfillment. The workings of nature are inseparable from the dual forces of yin and yang, and the subtle mysteries of the Dao originate in the union of husband and wife. In the secluded chamber, embroidered curtains and fragrant green silk bedding fill the air; her radiant attire includes a robe washed in fire and embroidered with a square collar. She lifts the veil, adorned with dew-like ornaments, and shares a cup of wine from jade goblets. A richly embroidered cushion lies beneath her soft silk socks, designed for the delicate beauty of her golden lotus feet; with deep black powder, he gently draws the shape of her crescent moon-like eyebrows. Two families united for a hundred years, one pair in perfect harmony. Their union is already harmonious in marriage, and their intimacy is as fitting as the harmonious sounds of the zither and the lute. In the ritual of offering fán and píng, they proceed with careful reverence in the ancestral rites; as they play with the jade and the tile, they are destined to receive the blessings of the mat and bedding. Can their union be compared to any famous flower? Are they not as rare and united as twin blossoms on a single stem? Graceful as the morning phoenix, harmonious like the swan of spring. The sound stirs the curtains, the silk light as dragon scales; in the dream, upon the pillow of the mandarin duck, her breath carries the fragrance of the chicken tongue herb. The rare encounter has been fulfilled in the wedding ceremony, and with the custom of the bed cover being cast, blessings are now proclaimed. Let us sing and recite words, to add to the joyous occasion.

    撒帐东，罗帏绣幕围春风（唐李贺）。红绽樱桃含白雪（唐李商隐），元精耿耿贯当中（唐李贺）。

    Eastward, the wedding bed is set, surrounded by luxurious curtains and drapes as the spring breeze flows (Tang Li He). The red cherry blossoms hold the purity of snow (Tang Li Shangyin), and the essence of the bride shines brightly at the center (Tang Li He).

    Westward, music and dance keep people entertained as the moon sets quickly (Tang Chu Guangxi). The lotus flower awakens with fresh and vibrant energy (Tang Li He), and her graceful posture in the wind enchants the spring (Tang Yong Tao).

    撒帐北，云楼半开壁斜白（唐李贺）。小语低声问玉郎（唐裴谱），春色恼人眠不得（宋王介甫）。
