    Explanation

    176

    In the north of the bed, clouds adorn the half-open walls with a pale white hue. A soft voice whispers to the young man, and the beauty of spring makes it hard to sleep.

    On the bed, two women in red dresses smile at each other. Light clouds and rain gently touch the high tower, and upon waking, the new moon has risen without notice.

    Below the bed, the night is filled with a full moon and east wind. A cold bamboo mat and silver bed prevent dreams from forming, and beautiful wine and clear music fill the song room.

    I wish that after the bedspread ceremony, the couple will be happy, and the household will be harmonious. A sip of nectar, just like the strange encounter of Pei Hang; five pairs of white jade, which can indicate the hidden virtue of Yong Bo. Even if the stone crumbles and the sea dries up, the sky will be long and the earth will last forever. Crickets chirp in order, and the feet of the unicorn are strong! How unfortunate that the groom's attendants use Fuzhou dialect, are unskilled in reading, and call out "Wen Xiucai." Upon entering the inner chamber, jewels and silk shine, with many women having rosy cheeks and soft necks. Except for the bride and groom sitting on the elephant bed, it is impossible to tell who the bride is. A beautiful and graceful recitation, with proper intonation and rhythm, is well-received by the audience. The ceremony is completed and the person leaves. Soon, the groom sends a matchmaker to deliver two pieces of ice silk and two pearls, which the person receives and then attends the banquet. The food served is not ordinary, and its names cannot be recognized.

    177

    丈人遍告坐宾，赞誉信美之才调。且作而言曰：“惟兹嘉礼，旷劫罕遇，今文士贲临，群仙光降，愿留珠玉，以为洞天之重，不识可乎？”信美乃献洞天花烛诗曰：

    玄黄初分鋋灵壤，峭壁穹崖绝来鞅。深严不遣俗人到，窈窕惟宜法宫敞。重重叠叠峙华构，画栋凌霄挂金榜。丈人华盖钧轴相，佐治蓬莱生杀掌。神明自与世人异，婚嫁本无情欲想。阴阳动静含橐龠，示有耦配非惚恍。高闲孰是可作对？震泽尊居百川长。时良日佳车辆多，琼树瑶柯顿成两。烹龙炰凤设宾筵，考鼓挝钟震霆响。蹇予凡陋忝司笺，利市平分珠与镪。雍容喜得厕衣冠，傧相宁期近屏幌！庭丁络绎进珍羞，座客纷纭杂谈讲。饮河鼹鼠愧盈腹，止鲁鶢鶋惭厚享！幸观花烛献新篇，留与千秋洞天赏。

    Explanation

    177

    The elder informed all the guests and praised the talent and temperament of Xin Mei. He then said, "This auspicious ceremony is rarely encountered over a long period. Today, scholars and immortals have graciously come to grace the occasion. I wish to leave behind precious writings to honor this heavenly abode. May I ask if this is acceptable?" Xin Mei then presented the poem "The Divine Lanterns of the Heavenly Abode":

    In the beginning, the primordial elements separated, creating the spiritual land. Steep cliffs and high walls cut off the paths of traffic. Deep and strict, it does not allow ordinary people to enter. Secluded and beautiful, it is only suitable for the grand palace to be open. Layer upon layer, grand structures stand, with painted beams reaching the sky and hanging golden plaques. The elder, with his ornate canopy and central axis, assists in governance, holding the power of life and death in Penglai. Gods and spirits naturally differ from ordinary people, and marriage originally lacks desire and passion. Yin and yang, movement and stillness, contain the breath of life, showing a couple that is not vague or uncertain. Who is suitable as a match for such a noble individual? Residing in a place respected by all rivers, Zhenze is highly esteemed. On this good day, many vehicles arrive, and precious trees and branches instantly become two. Dragons and phoenixes are cooked, and a banquet for guests is set up, with drumming and bell striking creating a thunderous sound. My humble self, ordinary and lowly, humbly serves as a scribe, equally dividing profit and wealth. Gladly, I am among the scholars and officials, not expecting to be close to the attendants! Servants in the courtyard continuously bring precious delicacies, and guests have various mixed discussions and lectures. A mole drinking from the river feels ashamed of a full belly, and a small bird from Lu feels ashamed of being well-fed! Fortunately, we see the flower candles and present a new poem, to be appreciated in the heavenly abode for thousands of years.

    178

    众宾传玩，咸赞瑰奇。宴罢酒阑，扶携而出。明日，丈人于玄清内殿，特待新婿，专命信美陪席；信美固让不敢当，翁婿交请，乃就坐。酒三行，美人捧红罗二端，文锦二匹为谢。既终宴，遣前二使送出。

    还家，家人惊怪，失已半月矣。信美悉裒诸物货卖，遂成富室。子孙甚盛。号遇仙文氏。于潜人至今称之不绝。

    泰山御史传
    宋圭，字孟瓒，山东之益都人。世农家，至其父始读书为畯儒。圭生而俊伟，长而端严，能勤于学，日记数千言。居贫，自食其力。隐田里间，以教授为业。非义不为，人敬惮之。省臣以孝弟力田荐，不报。集贤大学士阿鲁浑撒里言其守节静退，不求仕进，宜用以励奔竞，又不报。圭皆漠如也。性严毅，不能容人之过。每面折之，至颜赪发指，不少恕。而人亦服其规诲，无有与之为怨者。

    Explanation

    178

    The guests passed the object around, all praising its rarity and wonder. After the feast ended and the wine was finished, they were helped out. The next day, the father-in-law, in the inner hall of Xuanqing, specially treated the new son-in-law, and appointed Xinmei to accompany him at the table. Xinmei firmly declined, but the father-in-law and son-in-law both invited him, so he sat down. After three rounds of wine, a beautiful woman presented two pieces of red silk and two bolts of brocade as a gift. Once the feast concluded, she sent the two attendants to escort him out.

    When he returned home, his family was surprised and worried, as he had been missing for half a month. Xinmei collected all the items and sold them, thus becoming a wealthy household. His descendants were numerous. They were called the Wen family who met a fairy. The people of Yuqian still praise them to this day.

    The Biography of the Imperial Censor of Mount Tai

    Song Gui, courtesy name Mengzan, was from Yidu, Shandong. His family was of farming background, but his father began to study and became a scholar. Song Gui was handsome and tall from birth, and became dignified and solemn as he grew up. He was diligent in his studies, memorizing thousands of words each day. Living in poverty, he supported himself. He lived in the countryside, teaching as his profession. He did not do anything that was not righteous, and people respected and feared him. The provincial officials recommended him for filial piety, diligence in farming, and did not receive a response. The Grand Scholar Aruqunsali spoke of his adherence to principles, quiet retreat, and lack of desire for official advancement, suggesting he should be used to encourage those who rush for office, but again, there was no response. Song Gui remained indifferent to all of this.

    He was strict and resolute, unable to tolerate others' mistakes. He would often criticize them directly, causing their faces to redden and their hair to stand on end, showing no leniency. But people also respected his guidance and teachings, and no one held a grudge against him.

    179

    至正二十年秋八月望，圭家居，忽见黑云四合，迷亘其屋，旌幢麾节，拥一神人，若凡间贵官之状，呼圭出曰：“岳帝闻子经明行修，不偶于世，特召子为泰山司宪御史。”圭莫测所以，俯伏听命。神人即宣制曰：

    东岳天齐大王府：盖闻备束帛以征贤，朕每艰于得士；正朝纲而执法，汝克称于其官。顾兹耳目之司，实荷聪明之寄。旁求草泽，峻陟华阶。儒士宋圭，公直以无私，刚严而有断。方笃志探诗书之赜，而含章著易象之贞。安贫以乐箪瓢，味道而甘韦布。显荣常在于身后，优除真拜于乌台。纠察每侍于帝傍，谠论伫闻于白简。期迈揽辔范滂之右，肯居乘骢桓典之间。正色而谀佞寒心，飞章而奸回破胆。毋负清华之选，思酬特达之知。於戏！斧钺下青冥，禄未沾于人世；绣衣立霄汉，名更重于岱宗。咨尔夙儒，服我新命，可拜司宪御史。

    Explanation

    179

    On the 15th day of the eighth month in the autumn of the 20th year of the Zhi Zheng era, while Cui was at home, he suddenly saw dark clouds gather, enveloping his house. Banners, flags, and symbols of authority surrounded a divine figure, appearing like a high-ranking official of the mortal world. The figure called out to Cui, saying, "The Lord of Mount Tai has heard that you are well-versed in the classics and have a refined character, unmatched in the world. He specially summons you to serve as the Inspector of Justice in the region of Mount Tai." Cui was unable to understand the reason and bowed in submission, accepting the command. The divine figure then proclaimed:

    From the Eastern Emperor of Mount Tai, Lord of the Great Temple of the East: It is said that offering silk to attract the wise is difficult, and I often struggle to find true talent; maintaining the proper order and enforcing laws, you are fit for the role. Considering this position of oversight, you truly bear the trust of intelligence. Seeking talents from the common people, you ascend to high positions. Scholar Cui, you are impartial and without bias, strict and decisive. You diligently explore the depths of the classics and contain the essence of the Yijing (Book of Changes). Content with poverty and happy with simple food, you find joy in the simple and humble. Honor and glory often come after death, and you are appointed to a high position in the imperial court. Always serving the emperor in the role of inspector, you await the hearing of just and righteous words. Expecting to surpass the achievements of Fan Pang, you are willing to stand among the likes of Huandian. With a stern face, you make flatterers feel cold, and with swift and forceful words, you break the hearts of the wicked. Do not disappoint the choice of a noble selection, think of repaying the special knowledge. Alas! The axes and halberds descend from the heavens, the salary has not yet reached the mortal world; standing in embroidered robes in the heavens, your name is even more revered than Mount Tai. Admonish you, the learned scholar, accept my new command, and you may take the position of Inspector of Justice.

    180

    听毕，圭再拜曰：“帝命有严，其何敢避？但乞少缓耳。”神人颔之，反旆而去。圭知必死，即处置家事，沐浴更衣，迨夜半，逝矣。

    又数年，其友秦轸罢闽中尉，归次泰安州，遇圭于逆旅。相与道旧，沽酒而饮之。轸审知为鬼，且悉其死时事，因问曰：“地下官府，与人世类乎？”圭曰：“吾与君幽明异路，亦何用知？然念旧交，复是儒者，说亦何害。大抵阴道尚严，用人不苟。惟是泰山一府，所统七十二司，三十六狱，台、省、部、院、监、局、署、曹，与夫庙、社、坛、、鬼、神，大而冢宰，则用忠臣、烈士、孝子、顺孙，其次则善人、循吏，其至小者，虽社公、土地，必择忠厚有阴德之民为之。而尤重词职。向修文馆缺官，遍处搜访，不得其人。

    Explanation

    180

    After hearing, Gui bowed twice and said, "The imperial decree is stern; how dare I evade it? I only ask for a little delay." The divine being nodded and turned back to leave. Gui knew he would die, so he immediately arranged his affairs, bathed, changed clothes, and by midnight, he passed away.

    After several years, his friend Qin Zhen, who had been dismissed from his post as the governor of Minzhong, returned to Taian Prefecture and met Gui at an inn. They reminisced about old times and bought wine to drink together. Zhen realized that Gui was a ghost and knew all the details of his death, so he asked, "Is the government of the underworld similar to the human world?" Gui replied, "I and you are on different paths, so how could I know? However, thinking of our old friendship and that you are a scholar, what harm is there in telling you? Generally, the underworld is strict and does not use people lightly. Only in the Tai Shan (Mount Tai) government, which oversees seventy-two departments, thirty-six prisons, and various offices and temples, do they use loyal ministers, martyrs, filial sons, and obedient grandchildren. Next are good people and virtuous officials, and even the smallest positions, such as village deities and land gods, are filled by those who are honest and have hidden virtues. Especially, they value literary positions. Recently, the Literary Office was short of officials, and they searched everywhere but could not find anyone suitable."

    181

    亦有荐三数公者，虽甚文采，而在世之时，不修士行，或盗名欺世，或昧己瞒人，狗媚狐趋，皆有疵之可议。不得已，就其中择彼善于此者一人，为司言上卿。近又被墓灵冢伯诉其生前撰述死者铭志不实，广受润笔之资，多为过情之誉，以真乱赝，以愚为贤，使善恶混淆。冥官最所深恶。往往照依绮语妄言律科罪，付拔舌地狱施行。此为儒者深戒，虽有他美，莫得而赎焉。圣帝以其近臣，曲加贷宥。而复荒迷杯酌，失误表文，罪恶贯盈，灵祇共愤。吾纠而弹之，天齐震怒，遂下于狱。随即奏闻上穹，已正典宪。汝可录吾弹文，归示乡里，使知幽冥法度，更是谨严。凡在章述，务惇诚实，不可谓生前作事，地府罔知。《度人经》云：‘诸天记人功过，毫分无失。’断非虚语也。”即出稿，使轸抄之。

    Explanation

    181

    There are also those who recommend several individuals, although they possess great literary talent. Yet, while they were alive, they did not cultivate virtuous conduct. Some deceived the world by stealing a name, others obscured themselves and deceived others. They fawned like dogs and flattered like foxes, all of them having flaws that can be criticized. Unavoidably, one must choose the best among them, and thus, one was selected as the chief minister of speech. Recently, the tomb spirits and grave lords have accused him of falsifying the epitaphs of the deceased he wrote before death, widely receiving payment for his work, and often exaggerating praise. He confused the real with the fake, considered the foolish as wise, causing good and evil to become mixed. The underworld officials deeply detest this. They often punish according to the laws against false and vain words, sending him to the Hell of the Torn Tongue for punishment. This is a deep warning for scholars; even if there are other merits, they cannot redeem him. The Holy Emperor, considering him a close minister, showed leniency. But he again became lost in drink, made mistakes in official documents, and his crimes have reached the limit. The spirits and deities are all angry. I will investigate and impeach him, and the Heavenly Emperor is furious, so he was sent to prison. He immediately reported to the highest heaven, and the laws have been corrected. You can record my impeachment document, and show it to the villagers, so they know the laws of the underworld and how strict they are. In all writing, one must be sincere and honest, and one cannot say that actions in life are unknown in the underworld. The Book of Deliverance says: "The heavenly beings record people's merits and faults without error." This is certainly not an empty statement. He then presented the draft and asked Zhen to copy it.

    182

    文载于此：

    泰山司宪御史臣宋圭，为纠核事：臣闻设职建官，本阴阳之通制；操觚执翰，实臣子之当为。苟废务以怀奸，必正名而论罚。罪莫大于慢上，律莫重于欺君。恶既难容，讨奚容后？窃照修文馆司言上卿某人，庸庸俗士，贸贸迂儒，生前误玷于清流，巧于谀墓；死后谬驰于雅望，善于得名。妄矜袜线之才，猥试铅刀之利。拔自下鬼，擢于近臣，乃被冢伯之讼言，合在狱卒之投畀。过蒙原宥，特赐保全。所宜竭力宣忠，感恩图报。而本官虎皮羊质，狼子野心，弗思载笔摛辞，尽其职业。惟务饮酒食肉，苟度岁时。以偃蹇为当然，率轻狂而自若。

    Explanation

    182

    In writing, it is recorded as follows:

    Duke Song Gui, the Imperial Censor of Mount Tai, on the matter of investigation and correction: I have heard that setting up positions and appointing officials is based on the universal principles of yin and yang; holding a brush and writing is indeed the duty of officials and subjects. If one neglects duties for deceitful purposes, they must be corrected and punished. No crime is greater than disrespecting superiors, and no law is more severe than deceiving the sovereign. Evil cannot be tolerated, and punishment must follow immediately. I have observed that the High Minister of the Literary Bureau, a certain person, is an ordinary and foolish scholar, who falsely associated himself with the literati and wrote insincere eulogies. After his death, he falsely gained a high reputation and was adept at gaining fame. He falsely boasted of mediocre talents and unworthily attempted tasks. Promoted from the lowest ranks and elevated from the inner circle, he was accused by the head of the clan and should have been cast out. Yet, he was pardoned and protected. He should have shown loyalty and gratitude, but the official has a tiger's skin with a sheep's nature and a wolf's heart. He did not fulfill his duties in writing but only indulged in drinking and eating, living carelessly. He acts proudly and recklessly, as usual.

    183

    踪迹诡秘，贿赂公行。擢发不足以数其罪，粉身不足以胜其诛。旁若无人，但知有己。怙终不省，累恶不悛。乃于圣帝降诞之辰，神鬼而入称贺，三界之灵毕集，列岳之使偕来，钟鼓在悬，冕旒升殿，进表文而祝颂，献礼制之故常，却乃连日酗酣，临期失误，使百辟仓皇骇愕以失色，聚众人捏合掇拾以成文。 慢不恭，肆刑书之具在；劝惩示戒，盖王法之必诛。再照司言亚卿某人，视犹心腹，事若父兄，进拔出于其门，动静囿于其术，每忘规谏，屡献谄谀，立身未免于附腥，示戒固宜于连坐。合将各犯拿送酆都，明正其罪，以锄奸慝，以正宪纲。缘系命官，伏候裁处。

    Explanation

    183

    Secretive and corrupt, bribery is openly practiced. Even pulling out all one’s hair wouldn’t be enough to count their crimes, and even if their bodies were ground into powder, it wouldn’t be enough to bear the punishment. They act as if no one else exists, knowing only themselves. Stubbornly refusing to repent, they accumulate evil deeds without reform. On the day of the Holy Emperor’s birth, they entered in a mysterious, supernatural manner to offer congratulations. The spirits of the three realms gathered, and the messengers of the mountains arrived together. Bells and drums hung, and the crown with a train ascended the throne. They presented memorial texts to offer blessings and praises, following the customary rituals of offering gifts. Yet, they indulged in prolonged heavy drinking, leading to mistakes at the appointed time. This caused the officials to panic and be horrified, losing their composure. They hastily gathered people to fabricate and assemble a text. Lacking respect and seriousness, the instruments of punishment are at hand; to encourage good and punish evil, to warn and instruct, it is the king’s law that demands execution. Furthermore, regarding a certain Sub-Councilor of State, they are regarded as close as one’s inner organs, treated as if they were one’s father and elder brother. They were promoted through their door, and their actions and reactions are confined by their methods. They often forget to offer advice, repeatedly offering flattery. Their conduct is not free from being tainted by corruption, and it is appropriate to punish them collectively for the sake of warning. It is appropriate to arrest and send the offenders to Fengdu (the underworld), to clearly punish their crimes, to eradicate evil, and to uphold the laws. Due to their status as officials, they await judgment.

    184

    抄毕，轸告之曰：“某忝冒士流，叨窃禄食。兹者罢职回乡，竟不知前程之事果必如何，今幸遇公，愿乞指示。”圭曰：“天厌夷德久矣！将有真人龙兴于淮、泗间，君不及见。君之子孙，当享太平之福。”轸曰：“若然，则时事早晚大谬耶？必有兵革之祸，吾其死于兵戈乎？”圭曰：“尚远，勿虑也。”轸固问之，乃援笔写八句云：“逢衢禄进，遇安禄槁，火马行迟，金鸡叫早，门心掘井，花首去草，左阴右阳，后释前老”。竟莫晓其所说，遂收置囊间。复谓轸曰：“珍重故人！勉旃为善！”遂揖别而去，倏然不见。

    Explanation

    184

    After copying, Zhen told him, "I humbly occupy a position among scholars, ingratiate myself with salary. Now that I have resigned and returned to my hometown, I do not know what my future will surely be like. Fortunately, I have met you, and I wish to ask for guidance." Gui said, "Heaven has long been weary of the barbarian's virtue! There will be a true person who will rise to power in the Huai and Si regions, but you will not live to see it. Your descendants will enjoy the blessings of peace." Zhen said, "If so, will there be great chaos in the world soon? There will surely be war, and will I die in battle?" Gui said, "It is still far off, do not worry." Zhen insisted on asking, and Gui picked up a pen and wrote eight lines: "Encounter a crossroad for advancement, meet peace for a meager salary, fire horse moves slowly, golden rooster calls early, dig a well at the heart of the door, remove grass from the flower head, left is yin, right is yang, later release, earlier old." Ultimately, no one understood what it meant, so he put it away in his bag. He then said to Zhen, "Take care of your old friend! Strive to be good!" He bowed farewell and left, suddenly disappearing.

    185

    其后轸，用荐者再起，为衢州录事，则“逢衢禄进”之说验矣。未几，有委摄西安县，得风痹之疾，数月不愈，停俸医治，则“遇安禄槁”之说又验矣。轸甚忧其病，无何，竟卒。好事者追详其死之年，实丙午冬，丙属火，马肖午。殁之日，乃辛酉旦，辛属金，酉肖鸡，行迟言腊之尽，叫早言晨之初，悉与语合。但后四句莫喻。孰知轸任录事时，娶一妻，乃开化人。乱离不能北归，因归轸柩葬开化。以字观之，门中置井成开，花头去草成化。瘗处左则外母坟为阴，右则妻兄墓为阳。按山有道观废址，非前老之谓乎？靠山有佛堂败屋，非后释之谶乎？轸既殡，妻子留居墓下，遂为开化人。天朝平定群雄，民乐熙洽。轸有孙，仕至工部尚书者。圭之言，虽若迂怪，然无一不验。是知人之穷通出处，寿夭兴衰，生死葬埋，皆有一定之数，莫得而改移。或者乃欲以智力胜之，多见其不知量矣。

    Explanation

    185

    Afterward, Zhen was recommended again and took up the position of recorder in Quzhou, thus verifying the saying "Encountering Quzhou brings advancement." Not long after, he was temporarily appointed to oversee Xi'an County, where he contracted a wind-biased illness that persisted for several months without healing, leading to a suspension of his salary for medical treatment, thus fulfilling the prophecy of "Encountering An's fortune withered." Zhen was deeply concerned about his illness, and soon he passed away. Those interested in such matters later investigated the year of his death, which was indeed the winter of Bingwu (丙午), with Bing associated with fire and Wu with the horse. On the day of his death, Xinyou (辛酉) dawn, Xin is associated with metal and You with the rooster, corresponding to the end of the year and the beginning of the morning, all aligning with the prophecies. However, the meaning of the last four lines remains unclear. Who knew that while Zhen served as a recorder, he married a woman from Kaihua. Due to the chaos and upheaval, he could not return north and thus returned Zhen's coffin to be buried in Kaihua. Examining the characters, placing a well in the gate forms "open" (开), and removing grass from the flower forms "transform" (化). The burial site had his mother's grave to the left, representing yin, and his brother-in-law's tomb to the right, representing yang. On the mountain, there was a ruined Taoist temple, which might refer to the old man mentioned earlier? Nearby, there was a ruined Buddhist hall, which could be a prophecy of the future? After Zhen's burial, his wife and children stayed at the gravesite and eventually became residents of Kaihua. The Heavenly Dynasty pacified the heroes, and the people enjoyed peace and prosperity. Zhen had a grandson who rose to the position of Minister of Works. The words of Gui, though seemingly bizarre, proved to be accurate in every detail. This shows that one's fortunes, misfortunes, life and death, and burial are all predetermined and cannot be altered. Those who try to overcome fate with intelligence and strength often show a lack of understanding of their limitations.

    186

    江庙泥神记
    蜀之眉州，去城一舍许，小市濒江，人烟数百家，商贾物货之所聚，买卖甚旺。江上古庙一区，相传为花蕊夫人费氏之祠，迨今颇著灵迹。庙近大姓钟声远者，富而好礼，喜延名师。声远女兄有子曰谢生琏者，亦巨室，来舅家就学。生仪容秀整，风韵清高，略无寒儒迂腐态，群众咸喜之。相与弈棋饮酒，谈笑赋诗，惟恐生之或去也。钟西塾后，创一园特盛，建碧漪堂、水月亭、玩芳亭、醉春馆、翠屏轩于其内。生爱园幽雅，寓息其间，将近期月矣。一日，偶自外回，忽见四女郎，年近初笄，娉婷窈窕，嬉戏于玩芳亭畔。生谓是诸表妹，遽前揖之，至则皆非也。女殊不羞避，笑语自若。

    Jiang Temple Muddy God Record

    In the prefecture of Mei (眉州) of Shu (蜀), about a li from the city, there is a small market by the river, with hundreds of households and a bustling trade. On the riverbank stands an ancient temple complex, which is said to be the shrine of Empress Huairui, Lady Fei. To this day, it is quite famous for its miraculous occurrences. Nearby is a wealthy family named Zhong Shengyuan (钟声远), who is both affluent and fond of propriety, and likes to invite renowned teachers. Zhong Shengyuan's sister's son, Xie Sheng Lian (谢生琏), is also from a prominent family and comes to his aunt's house to study. Xie Sheng Lian has an elegant and dignified appearance, a graceful and noble demeanor, and lacks the awkward and pedantic demeanor of a poor scholar. Everyone likes him. They play chess, drink wine, talk, and recite poetry together, fearing that he might leave. Zhong Shengyuan's western academy has a particularly splendid garden, with the Green Ripple Hall, Water Moon Pavilion, Play Fragrance Pavilion, Spring Drunken Pavilion, and Jade Screen Pavilion built within it. Xie Sheng Lian loves the garden's tranquility and stays there to rest, having been there for nearly a month. One day, he returned from outside and suddenly saw four young ladies, about 15 years old, graceful and slender, playing around the side of the Play Fragrance Pavilion. Xie Sheng Lian thought they were his cousins and hurriedly bowed to them. But they were not his cousins. The girls were not at all embarrassed or avoiding, laughing and talking as usual.

    187

    生问之曰：“小姐辈误此来耶？”中一人应曰：“吾姊妹，东邻花氏之女也。久闻芳园胜丽，奇卉芬敷，故相携就此一赏玩耳。不料为郎所窥，幸勿深讶！”生意是邻居女子相往还，亦不以为怪矣。至夜将睡，忽闻窗棂轧轧作声，若有人敲推者。起视，乃日间所见诸女之一，闯然入户。向生施礼，和颜悦色，款语低声，云：“奴等蒲柳陋姿，丹铅弱质，偶得接见于光范。陡然忽动其柔情，莫或自持，是不可忍，故冒禁而相就，遂犯礼以私奔。肃抱衾裯，只荐枕席。”言讫，即邀生入寝，相与媾欢。生戏问曰：“彼三人何在？安得独来？” 女曰：“姑俟来宵，分此乐与诸妹耳。”遂口占一诗曰：

    The man asked them, “Have you ladies made a mistake by coming here?” One of them replied, “We are the daughters of the Huā family from the eastern neighbor. As night approached and he was about to sleep, he suddenly heard the window frame creaking, as if someone were knocking or pushing. He got up to look, and it was one of the women he had seen earlier that day, who suddenly entered the room.     From this point onward, the women took turns, and every night two of them attended to him. He then composed a poem titled E'mei Ancient Sentiment to celebrate himself. The poem reads:

    E'mei, the ancient prefecture, is renowned as the mightiest under heaven, with misty mountains and snowy peaks numbering in the thousands. The winding paths through the birds' trails connect to the lands beyond the Sword Gate, while the distant smoke signals of war reach into the barbarian regions. This land, with its strategic advantages, is known as our own, with countless mansions adorned with red doors and spears.     There is a virtuous woman, a beauty of the state, wearing the moon as a pendant and binding herself with orchids and sweet flag. The embroidered seat is adorned with pearl hairpins. She twists and turns, beautiful and charming, her beauty is unparalleled, and her grace is beyond description. They took a jade flute and gave it to her, saying, "You are deeply skilled in this, wish not to be stingy. Your sister will sing along, isn't that good?" The sister leaped up, saying, "Indeed!" After a short while, she played the flute three times. Its sound was clear and harmonious, gentle and charming, melancholic and quiet, like the cold cicada in the evening dew, like the fresh breeze riding the autumn clouds. The sister also gathered her eyebrows, sang and harmonized. She sang:

    Fingers like jade, face like ice, expressing deep thoughts and revealing inner feelings. The lingering sound lingers on, stopping the colorful clouds in the bright moon.

    195

    再歌曰：

    珠露零兮箫韵清，幽修凤语兮和且平，欢乐未极兮空复情。

    三歌曰：

    紫箫咽兮夜无哗，宝篆微袅兮烛垂花。河欲没兮夜欲阑，聊逍遥兮暂为欢。脱花钿兮收明榼，舒衾裯兮归洞房。齐交颈兮如鸳鸯，银漏短兮欢娱长。但悲白日兮上扶桑！

    正倾听间，忽角起谯楼，钟鸣梵宇，推枕欠伸，乃是南柯一梦。而且具忆其词，因起而录之。即托以卒业，往舅家。

    诸女幸生再至，眷顾倍加于昔。生与说梦中事，女曰：“此夫妇相念之深，故形诸梦寐，无足怪者。”生留恋女，只在斋房中，凡半月余，不与舅相见。舅疑之。一夕潜出，窥生所为，只见生共诸女玩月，谈笑方浓。遽入呼生，倏然惊散。随加诘问，终不肯言其详。舅谓妗曰：“园圃宽阔，竹树繁多，岂无花月之妖，或有水石之怪。琏又英俊，人物整齐，岂不为其所惑？急须遣归，恐久则致疾也。”乃令仆送生还。既抵家，不半载，以思女之故，果成重疾。

    Explanation

    195

    The second song goes:

    Dewdrops fall, and the sound of the flute is clear; the soft and harmonious call of the phoenix, gentle and peaceful, echoes through the air. Joy has not yet reached its peak, yet emotions linger.

    The third song goes:

    The purple flute sounds mournfully, and the night remains silent; the fragrant incense stick burns slowly, and the candlelight casts shadows. The river seems to be about to disappear, and the night draws to a close. Let us enjoy ourselves casually for a moment. Removing the ornamental hairpins and gathering the clear vessel, spreading out the bedding and returning to the inner chamber. Lying close together like a pair of mandarin ducks, the shortness of time indicated by the water clock contrasts with the length of enjoyment. Only feeling sad as the sun rises over the mythical tree of the sun.

    Just as I was listening, suddenly the horn sounded from the watchtower, and the bells rang from the Buddhist temple. Pushing aside the pillow and stretching, I realized it was all a dream in the South柯. I remembered the words of the songs and wrote them down. I entrusted the completion of the task to my uncle and went to his house.

    The girls were fortunate to have me return, and their affection for me was even greater than before. I told them about the dream, and one of them said, "This is because the couple misses each other deeply, so it appears in dreams. There is nothing to be surprised about." I became attached to them and stayed only in the study room for more than half a month, not seeing my uncle. My uncle suspected me. One night, he secretly left and observed what I was doing. He saw me playing with the girls under the moon, talking and laughing, enjoying ourselves. He suddenly entered and called out to me, and we were startled and scattered. He then questioned me, but I finally refused to explain in detail. My uncle told his wife, "The garden is wide, and there are many trees and bamboo. Could there not be spirits of flowers and the moon, or water and stone monsters? Lian is also handsome, with good looks, and could he not be bewitched by them? He must be sent back immediately, or he will fall ill if he stays too long." So he ordered a servant to send me home. After arriving home, within half a year, due to thinking of the girls, I indeed fell seriously ill.

    196

    神情恍惚，言语支离，伏枕淹淹，久而不愈。声远躬往视之，备以前事告于生父母。生父询问再三，乃吐实，且出所得诗及金掩鬓等物，视之，皆泥捏成者。父知其被祟，乃偕舅访于园中，并无踪迹。因往花蕊庙卜签，过东廊一小室，帏幔蔽亏，人迹稀到，揭而观之，题曰巫山神女之位，塑四美姬象于其中。东坐者失一掩鬓，右二人臂缺二镯，耳亡双榼，左一人面脱花钿两枚。其父大惊，取泥捏之物，置于旧处，皆吻合。即手碎其象，命仆沉之江中而归。自此月余，生疾亦愈，怪魅遂绝。

    Explanation

    196

    He was in a dazed state, his speech incoherent, and he lay in bed for a long time without recovery. Soundfar went personally to see him and reported all previous events to his adoptive parents. After repeated questioning, the sick person finally revealed the truth and showed the objects he had taken, including poems and a hairpin made of clay. Upon seeing them, his adoptive father realized he was being haunted. They then visited the garden together with the maternal uncle, but found no trace. They went to the Flower Petal Temple to draw a fortune-telling sign and passed by a small room in the east corridor, which was dimly lit and rarely visited. Upon entering, they saw an inscription reading "Position of the Goddess of Mount Wu," with four beautiful women sculpted inside. The eastern woman was missing a hairpin, the two on the right were missing bracelets on their arms, the two on the left were missing earrings, and one on the left had two flower decorations missing from her face. His adoptive father was greatly alarmed, took the clay objects, and placed them back in their original positions, where they matched perfectly. He then broke the image by hand and ordered the servant to throw it into the river. After this, the sick person recovered within a month, and the strange and ghostly phenomena ceased.

    197

    芙蓉屏记
    至正辛卯，真州有崔生名英者，家极富。以父荫，补浙江温州永嘉尉，携妻王氏赴任。道经苏州之圌山，泊舟少憩，买纸钱牲酒，赛于神庙。既毕，与妻小饮舟中。舟人见其饮器皆金银，遽起恶念。是夜，沉英水中，并婢仆杀之，谓王氏曰：“尔知所以不死者乎？我次子尚未有室，今与人撑船往杭州，一两月归来，与汝成亲，汝即吾家人，第安心无恐。”言讫，席卷其所有，而以新妇呼王氏。王氏佯应之，勉为经理，曲尽殷勤。舟人私喜得妇，渐稔熟，不复防闲。将月余，值中秋节，舟人盛设酒肴，雄饮痛醉。王氏伺其睡熟，轻身上岸，行二三里，忽迷路。四面皆水乡，惟芦苇菰蒲，一望无际。且生自良家，双弯纤细，不任跋涉之苦。又恐追寻至，于是尽力狂奔。

    Explanation

    197

    The Screen of the Lotus Flower

    In the year Xinhao of the Zhizheng era, there was a man named Cui Ying from Zhenzhou, who was extremely wealthy. Due to his father's influence, he was appointed as the military commander of Yongjia in Wenzhou, Zhejiang, and took his wife Wang with him to assume office. On their way, they passed by Tianshan Mountain in Suzhou, where they moored their boat for a brief rest, purchasing paper money, sacrificial animals, and wine to offer at a temple. After completing the offering, they had a small drink together in the boat. The boatman saw that their drinking vessels were all made of gold and silver, and suddenly conceived evil thoughts. That night, he drowned Cui Ying in the water and killed his maidservants and servants. He then told Wang, "Do you know why you are not being killed? My second son has not yet taken a wife. Now, he is rowing a boat to Hangzhou with others, and he will return in one or two months to marry you. You will then be part of my family, so just be at ease and have no fear." After saying this, he took all their possessions and referred to Wang as his new wife. Wang pretended to agree, and she tried her best to manage the affairs, showing utmost kindness and consideration. The boatman secretly rejoiced at having obtained a wife, and gradually became familiar with her, no longer being wary or cautious. After about a month, it happened to be the Mid-Autumn Festival. The boatman prepared a lavish banquet of food and drink, drinking heavily and getting drunk. Wang waited until he was asleep, then cautiously got out of the boat and walked for two or three miles, suddenly losing her way. All around were watery marshes, with only reeds and water plants stretching as far as the eye could see. Moreover, she was from a good family, with slender and delicate legs, unable to bear the hardship of traveling. Fearing that they might come looking for her, she then ran as fast as she could.

    198

    久之，东方渐白，遥望林中有屋宇，急往投之。至则门犹未启，钟梵之声隐然。少顷开关，乃一尼院。王氏径入，院主问所以来故，王氏未敢以实对，绐之曰：“妾真州人，阿舅宦游江浙，挈家偕行，抵任而良人殁矣。孀居数年，舅以嫁永嘉崔尉为次妻，正室悍戾难事，棰辱万端。近者解官，舟次于此。因中秋赏月，命妾取金杯酌酒，不料失手坠于江，必欲置之死地，遂逃生至此。”尼曰：“娘子既不敢归舟，家乡又远，欲别求匹配，卒乏良媒。孤苦一身，将何所托？”王惟涕泣而已。

    Explanation

    198

    After a long time, the eastern sky began to lighten, and looking far into the woods, Madam Wang saw houses and hastened to seek refuge there. Upon arrival, the gate was still closed, and the faint sound of bells and chanting could be heard. After a short while, the gate was opened, and it turned out to be a nunnery. Madam Wang entered directly, and the abbess asked the reason for her arrival. Madam Wang dared not tell the truth and instead said, "I am from Zhenzhou. My father-in-law traveled to Jiang-Zhe for official business and brought the family along. He arrived at his post but my husband passed away. I have been widowed for several years. My father-in-law then remarried me to the magistrate of Yongjia as his second wife. The first wife is fierce and difficult to deal with, subjecting me to countless beatings and insults. Recently, he resigned from his position, and the boat is moored here. Because of the Mid-Autumn Festival moon viewing, he ordered me to fetch a golden cup to pour wine. Unintentionally, I dropped it into the river, and he wanted to kill me. I fled to this place for safety." The abbess said, "Madam, you dare not return to the boat, your hometown is far away, and you wish to find another match, but finally lack a good matchmaker. Alone and destitute, where can you rely on?" Madam Wang could only weep.

    199

    尼又曰：“老身有一言相劝，未审尊意如何？”王曰：“若吾师有以见处，即死无憾！”尼曰：“此间僻在荒滨，人迹不到，茭葑之与邻，鸥鹭之与友，幸得一二同袍，皆五十以上，侍者数人，又皆淳谨。娘子虽年芳貌美，奈命蹇时乖。盍若舍爱离痴，悟身为幻，被缁削发，就此出家。禅榻佛灯，晨餐暮粥，聊随缘以度岁月，岂不胜于为人宠妾，受今世之苦恼，而结来世之仇仇乎？”王拜谢曰：“是所志也。”遂落发于佛前，立法名慧圆。王读书识字，写染俱通，不期月间，悉究内典，大为院主所礼待。凡事之巨细，非王主张，莫敢辄自行者。而复宽和柔善，人皆爱之。每日于白衣大士前礼百余拜，密诉心曲，虽隆寒盛暑弗替。既罢，即身居奥室，人罕见其面。

    Explanation

    199

    The nun then said, "I have a piece of advice to offer, I wonder what your esteemed opinion is?" The woman replied, "If my teacher has something to advise, I will have no regrets even if it costs my life!" The nun said, "This place is situated in a remote coastal area where human footsteps rarely reach. Living beside reeds and water plants, being friends with seagulls and herons, we are fortunate to have a few fellow practitioners, all over fifty years old, and their attendants are also very simple and honest. Although you are young and beautiful, your fate and timing are unfortunate. Why not let go of attachment and delusion, realize that the body is illusory, wear the monastic robe and shave your head, and enter monastic life? The monk's bed and the Buddha's lamp, breakfast and evening porridge, passing the days following the Dharma, wouldn't it be better than being a favored concubine, suffering in this life, and making enemies in the next life?" The woman bowed and thanked her, saying, "That is what I wish to do." She then shaved her head in front of the Buddha and took the Dharma name Hui Yuan. Wang read books and learned to write, and was skilled in both calligraphy and painting. Within a few months, she thoroughly studied Buddhist scriptures and was greatly respected and treated well by the abbot. All matters, big or small, unless Wang approved, nobody dared to act on their own. She was gentle, kind, and virtuous, and everyone loved her. Every day she would pay over a hundred bows before the Bodhisattva Guanyin, secretly confiding her innermost feelings, even in the coldest winters and hottest summers, she never stopped. Afterward, she would immediately retreat to a secluded room, and few people saw her face.

    岁余，忽有人至院随喜，留斋而去。明日，持画芙蓉一轴来施，老尼张于素屏。王过见之，识为英笔，因询所自。院主曰：“近日檀越布施。”王问：“檀越何姓名？今住甚处？以何为生？”曰：“同县顾阿秀，兄弟以操舟为业。年来如意，人颇道其劫掠江湖间，未知诚然否？”王又问：“亦尝往来此中乎？”曰：“少到耳。”即默识之。乃援笔题于屏上曰：

    Explanation

    200

    After more than a year, someone suddenly came to the temple to visit, left offerings, and then departed. The next day, the person brought a scroll of painted lotus flowers as a gift, and the old nun hung it on a plain screen. As Wang passed by and saw it, he recognized the handwriting as that of a talented person and asked about its origin. The temple master replied, "It was recently donated by a benefactor." Wang asked, "What is the benefactor's name? Where does he live now? What does he do for a living?" The master answered, "He is Gu Axiu from the same county. His brothers make their living by plying boats. Recently, he has been doing well, but people often say he robs and plunders on the rivers and lakes. I don't know if that is true." Wang then asked, "Has he ever come here before?" The master replied, "He comes here rarely." Wang immediately remembered the person. He then took a brush and wrote on the screen, saying:

    岁余，忽有人至院随喜，留斋而去。明日，持画芙蓉一轴来施，老尼张于素屏。王过见之，识为英笔，因询所自。院主曰：“近日檀越布施。”王问：“檀越何姓名？今住甚处？以何为生？”曰：“同县顾阿秀，兄弟以操舟为业。年来如意，人颇道其劫掠江湖间，未知诚然否？”王又问：“亦尝往来此中乎？”曰：“少到耳。”即默识之。乃援笔题于屏上曰：

    201

    少日风流张敞笔，写生不数黄筌。芙蓉画出最鲜妍。岂知娇艳色，翻抱死生冤！粉绘凄凉疑幻质，只今流落谁怜！素屏寂寞伴枯禅。今生缘已断，愿结再生缘。

    其词盖《临江仙》也。尼皆不晓其所谓。

    一日，忽在城有郭庆春者，以他事至院。见画与题，悦其精致，买归为清玩。适御史大夫高公纳麟退居姑苏，多募书画，庆春以屏献之，公置于内馆，而未暇问其详。偶外间忽有人卖草书四幅，公取观之，字格类怀素而清劲不俗。公问；“谁写？”其人对：“是某学书。”公视其貌，非庸碌者。即询其乡里姓名，则蹙頞对曰：“英姓崔，字俊臣，世居真州。以父荫补永嘉尉，挈累赴官，不自慎重，为舟人所图，沉英水中，家财妻妾，不复顾矣。幸幼时习水，潜泅波间。度既远，遂登岸投民家，而举体沾湿，了无一钱在身。

    Explanation

    201

    In his youth, he wielded the brush of Zhang Chang with grace and elegance, his skill in painting living things not inferior to Huang Quan. He painted lotuses with the most vivid and beautiful colors. Who would have thought that such a beautiful color could bring a grievance of life and death! The powdered colors depict a desolate scene that seems like an illusion. Now it is wandering and who will pity it. The plain screen is lonely, accompanying the dry meditation. The bond of this life has been severed, I wish to form a new bond in the next life.

    The poem is likely a Ling Jiang Xian (临江仙). The nuns do not understand what it means.

    One day, suddenly in the city, there was a man named Guo Qingchun, who came to the temple for some other matter. He saw the painting and the inscription, and was delighted by its exquisite beauty, so he bought it to keep as a fine object. Coincidentally, the Grand Censor Gao Nalin, who had retired to Suzhou, was collecting paintings and calligraphy. Guo Qingchun presented the screen to him, and Gao placed it in his inner hall but did not have time to inquire about its details. Suddenly, someone outside was selling four pieces of grass script calligraphy. Gao took them to look at them, and found the style similar to Huaisu but clear and vigorous, not vulgar. He asked, "Who wrote this?" The seller replied, "It is mine, a student of calligraphy." Gao looked at his face and found him not an ordinary person. He immediately asked about his hometown and name, but the man frowned and replied, "My surname is Ying, my given name is Junchen, and I come from Zhenzhou. Because of my father's favor, I was appointed as the magistrate of Yongjia. I took my family with me to take up the post, but I was not careful, and was robbed by boatmen, sinking me into the water. My family's wealth, my wife and concubines, I no longer cared about. Fortunately, I had learned to swim when I was young, and I swam underwater. When I felt I was far away, I climbed ashore and went to a commoner's house, but my body was completely wet, and I had no money on me.

    202

    赖主翁善良，易以裳衣，待以酒食，赠以盘缠，遣之曰：‘既遭寇劫，理合闻官，不敢奉留，恐相连累。’英遂问路出城，陈告于平江路。今听侯一年，杳无音耗，惟卖字以度日，非敢谓善书也。不意恶札，上彻钧览。”公闻其语，深悯之，曰：“子既如斯，付之无柰！且留我西塾，训诸孙写字，不亦可乎？”英幸甚。公延入内馆，与饮。英忽见屏间芙蓉，泫然垂泪。公怪问之。曰：“此舟中失物之一，英手笔也。何得在此？”又诵其词，复曰：“英妻所作。”公曰：“何以辨识？”曰：“识其字画。且其词意有在，真拙妇所作无疑。”公曰：“若然，当为子任捕盗之责。子姑秘之。”乃馆英于门下。

    Explanation

    202

    Thanks to the kind host, he exchanged his clothes, was treated with food and drink, and given money for travel. The host sent him off with these words: "After being robbed by bandits, according to the law, one should report to the authorities; we dare not keep you, for fear of being implicated." Ying then asked for directions and left the city, reporting to the Pingjiang Road authorities. Now waiting for a year, no news has come, and he survives by selling his calligraphy, not daring to claim he is skilled in writing. Unintentionally, he wrote a bad letter, which reached the imperial review. The official heard his words and deeply pitied him, saying, "Since you are like this, there is nothing to be done! And let you stay in my western study to teach my grandchildren calligraphy, is it not acceptable?" Ying was very fortunate. The official invited him into the inner hall and shared a drink with him. Suddenly, Ying saw a lotus on the screen, and tears welled up in his eyes. The official asked him curiously. Ying said, "This is one of the lost items from the boat, written by me. How did it end up here?" He recited the words again and said, "It was written by my wife." The official asked, "How do you recognize it?" Ying replied, "Recognize the handwriting. And the meaning of the words is clear; it is undoubtedly written by a clumsy woman." The official said, "If so, I will take on the responsibility of catching the thieves. You should keep it secret." Then, the official invited Ying to stay under his roof.

    203

    明日，密召庆春问之。庆春云：“买自尼院。”公即使宛转诘尼：“得于何人？谁所题咏？”数日报云：“同县顾阿秀舍，院尼慧圆题。”公遣人说院主曰：“夫人喜诵佛经，无人作伴，闻慧圆了悟，今礼为师，愿勿却也。”院主不许。而慧圆闻之，深愿一出，或者可以借此复仇，尼不能拒。公命舁至，使夫人与之同寝处，暇日，问其家世之详。王饮泣，以实告，且白题芙蓉事，曰：“盗不远矣，惟夫人转以告公，脱得罪人，洗刷前耻，以下报夫君，则公之赐大矣！”而未知其夫之故在也。夫人以语公，且云其读书贞淑，决非小家女。公知为英妻无疑，属夫人善视之，略不与英言。公廉得顾居址出没之迹，然未敢轻动。惟使夫人阴劝王蓄发返初服。

    The next day, the official secretly summoned Qingchun to question him. Qingchun replied, "I bought it from a nunnery." The official then subtly interrogated the nun: "From whom did you get it? The official sent someone to persuade the abbot: "My wife enjoys reciting Buddhist scriptures but has no one to accompany her. The official knew for sure that she was Ying's wife and ordered the wife to treat her well, barely speaking to Ying. The official investigated Gu's residence and movements but dared not act rashly. He only had the wife secretly encourage Wang to grow her hair and return to her initial attire.

    又半年，进士薛理溥化为监察御史，按郡。溥化，高公旧日属吏，知其敏手也，具语溥化，掩捕之，敕牒及家财尚在，惟不见王氏下落。穷讯之，则曰： “诚欲留以配次男，不复防备。不期当年八月中秋逃去，莫知所往矣。”溥化遂置之于极典，而以原赃给英。英将辞公赴任，公曰：“待与足下作媒，娶而后去，非晚也。”英谢曰：“糟糠之妻，同贫贱久矣。今不幸流落他方，存亡未卜。且单身到彼，迟以岁月，万一天地垂怜，若其尚在，或冀伉俪之重谐耳。感公恩德，乃死不忘，别娶之言，非所愿也。

    真之才士陆仲甗，作画芙蓉屏歌，以纪其事，因录以警世云：

    画芙蓉，妾忍题屏风！屏间血泪如花红。败叶枯梢两萧索，断缣遗墨俱零落。去水奔流隔死生，孤身只影成飘泊。成飘泊，残骸向谁托？泉下游魂竟不归，图中艳姿浑似昨。浑似昨，妾心伤，那禁秋雨复秋霜！宁肯江湖逐舟子，甘从宝地礼医王。医王本慈悯，慈悯怜群品，逝魄愿提撕，茕嫠赖将引。芙蓉颜色娇，夫婿手亲描。花萎因折蒂，干死为伤苗，蕊干心尚苦，根朽恨难消。但道章台泣韩翃，岂期甲帐遇文箫。芙蓉良有意，芙蓉不可弃。幸得宝月再团圆，相亲相爱莫相捐。谁能听我芙蓉篇？人间夫妇休反目，看此芙蓉真可怜。

    A Talented Scholar Named Lu Zhongyan Composed a Song About the Painted Lotus Screen, to Record the Events, and It Is Recorded to Warn the World:

    Painting the lotus, I dare not inscribe on the screen! The blood and tears on the screen are as red as the flowers. Withered leaves and dry branches are both desolate, torn silk and scattered ink are all fallen apart. The flowing water separates life and death, alone and in solitude, I become a wanderer. As a wanderer, to whom can my remains be entrusted? The soul in the spring (grave) does not return, the beautiful figure in the painting is still like yesterday. Still like yesterday, my heart is wounded, how can I endure the autumn rain and frost again! Rather than follow a boatman on the rivers and lakes, I willingly follow the Medicine King in the sacred place. The lotus flower is charming, the husband personally painted it. The flower withers because the stem is broken, drying up is caused by injuring the seedling, the heart is still bitter even though the petals are dry, the root rots and the hatred is hard to erase. It is said that Han Hong wept at Zhangtai, who would have expected to meet Wen Xiao in the Jia tent. The lotus flower indeed has meaning, the lotus cannot be abandoned. Fortunately, the moon and the pearl are reunited, love each other and do not abandon each other. Who can listen to my lotus flower poem? Husbands and wives in the world should not quarrel, look at this lotus flower, it is truly pitiable.

    秋千会记
    元大德二年戊戌，孛罗以故相齐国公子拜宣徽院使，奄都剌为佥判，东平王荣甫为经历，三家联住海子桥西。宣徽生自相门，穷极富贵，第宅宏丽，莫与为比。然读书能文，敬礼贤士，故时誉翕然称之。私居后有杏园一所，取“春色满园关不住，一枝红杏出墙来”之意，花卉之奇，亭榭之好，冠于诸贵家。每年春，宣徽诸妹、诸女，邀院判、经历宅眷，于园中设秋千之戏，盛陈饮宴，欢笑竟日。各家亦隔一日设馔。自二月末至清明后方罢，谓之秋千会。适枢密同佥帖木尔不花子拜住过园外，闻笑声。于马上欠身望之，正见秋千竞蹴，欢哄方浓。潜于柳阴中窥之，睹诸女皆绝色，遂久不去。为阍者所觉，走报宣徽。索之，亡矣。

    秋千会记

    In the year 1298 AD, during the reign of Emperor Chengzong of the Yuan Dynasty, Bo Luo, a descendant of the former ruling family of the Jin Dynasty, was appointed as the Minister of the Imperial Household. Alongside him were Yin Du La, who served as a deputy minister, and Dong Ping Wang Rong Fu, who served as an official. The three families lived in a row on the west side of Hai Zi Bridge. Bo Luo, born into a family of high officials, enjoyed extreme wealth and power. His mansion was grand and magnificent, unmatched by any other noble family. Despite his high status, he was well-read and skilled in writing, respected scholars, and was widely praised for his virtues. Behind his private residence, he had a garden dedicated to apricot trees, inspired by the famous line from a poem by Ye Shao-weng: "The spring scenery cannot be confined within the garden; a branch of red apricot flowers extends over the wall." The garden was renowned for its unique flowers and beautiful pavilions, surpassing those of all other noble families. Every spring, Bo Luo's sisters and daughters would invite the wives and daughters of the deputy minister and the official to the garden for a swing festival. A grand banquet was set up, and they laughed and joked all day. Each family would also set up a feast every other day. The festival lasted from late February until after the Qingming Festival, known as the Swing Festival. One day, while passing by the garden, the son of the deputy minister of the Military Council, Tie Mu Er Bu Hua, heard laughter. He leaned forward on his horse to look at the garden and saw the women competing in swinging, with the joy and excitement at their peak. He peeked from under the willow trees and saw that all the women were extremely beautiful. He stayed for a long time, but was noticed by the gatekeeper, who ran to report to Bo Luo. When Bo Luo searched for him, he was gone.

    211

    Bai Zhu heard of the change and, that night, secretly went to mourn it, knocking on the coffin and saying, "Bai Zhu is here." Suddenly, a voice from within the coffin responded, "Open the coffin, and I will live." He looked all around the four corners, noting that the lacquer nails were firmly fastened, making it impossible to open. He then planned with the monk, saying, "Spare no effort; the sin of opening the coffin, I will take full responsibility, and I will not burden you. We will share all the contents." The monk, who had always known about the elaborate burial, also had the intention to gain something and so chopped off the lid. The woman indeed came to life, and both were extremely happy. He then took off half of the gold bracelets and jewelry to thank the monk. Calculating the rest, they still amounted to tens of thousands of strings of cash. He then entrusted the monk to buy lacquer and repair the coffin, so that the matter would not be revealed. Bai Zhu then took Suge Shili to Shangdu, where they stayed for a year, and no one knew about it.     贾云华还魂记
    魏鹏，字寓言，其先钜鹿人。九世祖飞卿，宋高宗朝，仕至御史中丞。以论秦桧误国，贬襄阳令，死葬白马山，子孙遂留居焉。宗族蕃衍，富拟封君，迨元朝尤盛。鹏父巫臣，延祐初，参政江浙行省，生鹏于公廨而父卒。母郢国萧夫人，携鹏暨二兄枿、棨，扶榇归襄阳。魏生五岁通五经，七岁能属文，肌肤莹然，眉目如画，乡里以神童称之。至正间，累举不偶，深置恨焉。

    Explanation

    213

    Bai Zhu had three sons: the eldest, Jiaohua, served up to the position of Left Censor of the Pacification Commission of Liaoyang and its Surroundings but died young. The second son was Manggu Dai, and the youngest was Heisi. Both became members of the imperial guard and carried the emperor's personal weapons. Manggu Dai died first. Heisi reached the position of Chief of the Privy Council. When the imperial army arrived in Yan, Emperor Toghon Temür ruled from the Qingning Hall, gathering the empresses, concubines, and the crown prince to discuss how to avoid the war. Heisi and Chancellor Shilumen cried and advised, saying, "The world is the world of Emperor Shizu. It should be defended to the death." The emperor did not listen. At midnight, they opened Jiande Gate and fled. Heisi followed into the desert, and his fate is unknown.

    The Tale of Jia Yunhua's Return to Life
    Wei Peng, courtesy name Yuyan, was originally from Juzhu. His ninth-generation ancestor, Fei Qing, served as Vice President of the Censorate during the reign of Emperor Gaozong of Song. Because he criticized Qin Hui for mismanaging the country, he was demoted to the position of magistrate of Xiangyang, died, and was buried on White Horse Mountain, after which his descendants remained there. The clan grew prosperous, their wealth comparable to that of a noble, and especially so during the Yuan dynasty. Wei Peng's father, Wuchen, was a provincial governor in Jiangzhe during the early years of the Yuan dynasty's reign of Emperor Renzong, and Wei Peng was born in the government office while his father died. His mother, Lady Xiao of Yingguo, took Wei Peng and his two brothers, Nie and Qi, along with the coffin, back to Xiangyang. Wei Peng, at five years old, had mastered the Five Classics, and at seven, could write essays. His skin was radiant, and his eyes and eyebrows were like paintings. The villagers called him a prodigy. During the reign of Emperor Huizong of Yuan, he failed multiple times in the imperial examinations and deeply resented it.

    214

    He once said, "A true man should easily achieve fame and success, yet and yet cannot even obtain a degree!" Then he sighed deeply. Lady Xiao, upon hearing this, feared that he would become depressed and fall ill, so she commanded him, saying, "Qiantang, your father's hometown is Tongxiang. All the renowned teachers and scholars of this era are mostly former students or officials of your father. Go and seek their teachings, perhaps there will be some success. Especially in the southeastern region, which is a great province with extraordinary landscapes. Which can broaden the mind and inspire poetic expression. Go forth! Do not limit yourself to one place." Then he took out a sealed letter from his chest and gave it to him, saying, "When you are free from studying there, you should visit the former Chancellor Jia Pingzhang's wife, Lady Mo of Xingguo, and present this to her to discuss your marriage. I have my reasons, be careful not to open it rashly." The son left, privately opened the seal, and learned that before he was born, his mother had a prearranged marriage agreement with her. Overjoyed, he hastened to set out. The letter from Lady Mo, attached below:

    215

    懿恭敛衽再拜，奉书邢国太夫人几前：懿恭阔别十五年，远隔数千里，各天一所，杳不相闻。缅想穹祇叶相，茵鼎善调，喜溢门阑，福臻闺阃，健羡何可胜言！如懿恭者，既失所天，苟存贞节，一家长幼，处此粗安，无足为太夫人道。第念先平章与先夫参政，官虽僚友，情则弟兄；妾荷太夫人视同娣妹，始因有妊，各发誓言，夫人尝举汉光武、贾复故事，指妾腹而言曰：“生子耶，我女嫁之；生女耶，我子娶之。”厥后神启其衷，天作之配，庆门诞瓦，寒舍得雄。不幸未期，夫君薨逝，妾提挈诸孤，扶柩归殡，山遥水远，无地相逢。今者，幼儿已冠，贤女谅亦及笄，苟未订盟，愿如夙誓。故敢冒昧贡书，布兹悃款，仍令此子亲赍奉闻。倘到阶庭，希垂顾眄。伫聆金诺，拱俟报音。会晤未期，临缄于悒！不具。

    Explanation

    215

    Yi Gong, with folded sleeves, bows twice in deep respect and presents this letter before the desk of Lady Tai of the State of Xing: Yi Gong has been parted from you for fifteen years, separated by thousands of miles, each under a different heaven, and we have not heard from each other. I recall the harmonious will of Heaven and Earth, the gentle and wise arrangements of fate — joy fills the gate, blessings reach the inner chambers, and how can one adequately express the admiration and envy I feel! As for Yi Gong, having lost the one who was my heaven, I have maintained my virtue, and my family, young and old, have managed to live in a state of rough peace — not worth mentioning to Lady Tai. Yet I think of my late husband’s colleague and my late husband, who were officials, though colleagues in office, they were like brothers in sentiment. I have been treated by Lady Tai as a sister-in-law. At the time I became pregnant, we each made vows. Lady Tai once cited the story of Emperor Guangwu of Han and General Zhu Fu, pointing to my womb and saying: “If a son is born, my daughter will marry him; if a daughter is born, my son will marry her.” Afterwards, the gods opened my heart, and Heaven arranged this union — joy came to our household with the birth of a son, and our humble home gained a strong male heir. Unfortunately, before this could be realized, my husband passed away. I took care of the orphans and carried his coffin back for burial, but the mountains and rivers were far, and we had no chance to meet. Now, my son has reached the age of manhood, and my daughter, I suppose, is also of marriageable age. If they have not yet been betrothed, I hope they will follow the old promise. Therefore, I dare to submit this letter, conveying my sincere feelings, and have had this son personally deliver it to you. If he reaches your doorstep, I hope you will look upon him kindly. I await your golden promise, and bow in anticipation of your reply. Until we meet, as I close this letter, I feel deep sorrow. I remain, respectfully,
    Yi Gong.

    216

    生奉命，翌旦戒行。逾两月，抵杭，僦居于北关门边妪家。妪善延纳，生颇安之。越数日，舍馆既定，乃渐出游，访问故人，无一在者。惟见湖山佳丽，清景满前，车马喧阗，笙歌盈耳。生乃赋《满庭芳》词一阕，以纪其胜，因题于寓舍纸窗之上。词曰：

    天下雄藩，浙江名郡，自来惟说钱塘。水清山秀，人物异寻常。多少朱门甲第，闹丛里，争沸丝簧。少年客，谩携绿绮，到处鼓求凰。 徘徊应自笑，功名未就，红叶谁将？且不须惆怅，柳嫩花芳。闻道蓝桥路近，愿今生一饮琼浆。那时节，云英觑了，欢喜杀裴航。

    Explanation

    216

    The protagonist received his command and prepared to depart the next day. After two months, he arrived in Hangzhou and rented a residence near the northern gate from an old woman. The woman was hospitable, and the protagonist found himself quite at ease. After several days, once his lodging was settled, he gradually began to go out. He visited his old friends, but none of them were there. All he saw were the beautiful lakes and mountains, with clear and beautiful scenery filling his view. The sound of carriages and horses was loud, and the music and singing filled his ears. The protagonist then composed a poem titled "Man Ting Fang" to record the beauty of the place, and he wrote it on the paper window of his rented residence. The poem reads:

    A powerful province in the world, a famous county in Zhejiang, since ancient times only speaks of Qiantang. Clear water and beautiful mountains, people and things are extraordinary. How many noble mansions, in the midst of the crowd, compete to play string and wind instruments. A young guest, casually carrying a green qin, goes everywhere playing the "Seeking the Phoenix" tune. Wandering and laughing at oneself, have not achieved fame and success, who will give a red leaf? Do not need to be sad, the willows are tender and the flowers are fragrant. Hearing that the Blue Bridge is nearby, wish to drink nectar in this life. At that time, Yun Ying looked at it, Pai Hang was overjoyed.

    217

    偶边妪见之，问曰：“斯作郎君所缀乎？”生未答。妪曰：“郎君岂以老妇为不知音也耶？大凡乐府蕴藉为先，此词虽佳，尚欠妩媚，欧、晏、秦、黄，殆不如是。”生闻之，乃大惊，因致谢曰：“浅陋之言，献笑多矣。”因诹妪出处，方知为达睦丞相宠姬。丞相薨，出嫁民家，今老矣，通诗书，晓音律，喜笑谈，善刺绣，多往来达官家，为女子师，皆呼为边孺人。生曰：“然则丞相正与先公大参及贾平章为同辈人矣。”妪骇曰：“郎君岂魏参政子乎？”生曰：“然。”妪曰： “真韩子所谓称其家儿者也。”因出杯款生，生乃得备询参政旧日僚采。妪曰：“俱无矣，惟贾氏一门在此耳。”生曰：“老母有书奉达于彼，敢托为之先容。”妪许诺。

    Explanation

    217

    An elderly woman from the neighborhood saw him and asked, "Does this belong to the young man?" The young man did not answer. The woman said, "Young man, do you think the old woman is not a connoisseur of music? Generally speaking, yuefu poetry should be subtle and profound. This poem is good, but it lacks charm. The works of Ouyang Xiu, Yan Shu, Qin Guan, and Huang Tingjian are perhaps not like this." Hearing this, the young man was greatly surprised and replied with thanks, "I have made many mistakes with my shallow and unrefined words." He then inquired about the woman's background and learned that she had once been the favorite concubine of Chancellor Da Mu. After the chancellor's death, she was married into a common family. She is now old, but she is well-versed in poetry and literature, skilled in music and rhythm, enjoys conversation, and is adept at embroidery. She frequently visits the homes of high-ranking officials and serves as a teacher to women, and everyone calls her Madam Bian. The young man said, "Then Chancellor Da Mu was indeed a contemporary of my father, the Political Advisor, and Grand Councillor Jia." The woman was surprised and asked, "Are you the son of Political Advisor Wei?" The young man replied, "Yes." The woman said, "Indeed, you are the very person Confucius referred to when he said one should praise one's own children." She then offered the young man a drink, and he was able to ask her about the chancellor's former colleagues. The woman said, "They are all gone now, except for the Jia family." The young man said, "My mother has a letter for them. Could you deliver it on my behalf?" The woman agreed.

    218

    生又问：“平章弃禄数年，今有谁在？生事若何？”妪曰：“平章一子名麟，字灵昭。一女名娉娉，字云华，母梦孔雀衔牡丹蕊置怀中而生。语颜色则若桃花之映春水，论态度则若流云之迎晓日。十指削纤纤之玉，双鬓绾袅袅之丝。填词度曲，李易安难继后尘；织锦绣图，苏若兰讵容独步！邢国钟爱之，俾从余讲学，余自以为弗如也。且夫人勤励，治产有方，珠履玳簪，不减昔时之丰盛；钟鸣鼎食，宛如向日之繁华。”生闻之，知其必指腹之人也，急欲一往。会妪病目，弗能前，遂止。夫人讶妪久不来，乃遣婢春鸿往妪家问焉。时妪目愈，欲生偕行，值生偶出，妪乃先随鸿往，诣夫人谢，且道魏生母寄书事。邢国骇愕，曰：“正尔念之，今焉至此，亟为我召来，勿缓也！”春鸿承命，复至请生，生便同行。

    Explanation

    218

    The young man then asked, "After the chancellor abandoned his salary for several years, who is still alive now? How are they doing?" The old woman replied, "The chancellor has one son named Lin, courtesy name Lingzhao. He also has a daughter named Pingping, courtesy name Yunhua. She was born when her mother dreamed of a peacock carrying a peony bud and placing it in her womb. In terms of appearance, she is like a peach blossom reflected in spring water; in terms of demeanor, she is like a cloud greeting the morning sun. Her fingers are as slender as carved jade, and her hair is tied up like graceful silk. In composing lyrics and setting music, she is difficult to follow in the footsteps of Li Qingzhao; in weaving brocade and embroidery, no one can match Su Ruolan! Lady Xing deeply loves her and has her study under me. I consider myself inferior to her. Moreover, Lady Xing is diligent and skilled in managing her property. She wears pearl-adorned shoes and tortoiseshell hairpins, not falling short of her former prosperity; she enjoys a life of luxury and abundance, much like the past. When the young man heard this, he knew she must be the one destined for a prearranged marriage and was eager to go. However, the old woman was suffering from eye disease and could not proceed, so he stopped. Lady Xing was surprised that the old woman had not come for a long time and sent her maid Chunhong to inquire at the old woman's house. At that time, the old woman's eyes had improved and wanted to go with the young man, but he happened to be out. The old woman then followed Chunhong and went to Lady Xing's house to thank her and also to tell her about the matter of the letter sent by Wei Sheng's mother. Lady Xing was startled and said, "I was just thinking about it, and now here you are. Quickly summon him for me, do not delay!" Chunhong received the command and went again to invite the young man, who agreed to go with her.

    219

    既及门，鸿先入。俄而二青衣导生至重堂，即东阶少立。邢国服命服出，坐堂中。生再拜。夫人曰：“魏郎几时来耶？”生曰：“数日耳。”命坐于西鸑前钿椅上。茶罢，夫人曰：“记得别时，尚在襁褓，今长成若是矣！”慰劳甚至，且问萧夫人暨枿、棨安否？生答以幸俱无恙。夫人为生道旧，如在目前，但不及指腹誓姻之说。生疑之，乃顾随来老仆青山解囊，取母书投上。夫人拆封，观毕，纳诸袖中，亦不发言。

    Explanation

    219

    Having reached the gate, Hong entered first. Soon after, two servants in green robes led the student to the main hall, where he stood at the eastern steps. Duchess Xing, dressed in her ceremonial attire, emerged and sat in the hall. The student bowed twice. The lady said, "When did Wei come?" The student replied, "Just a few days ago." She gestured for him to sit on a jeweled chair before her in the west. After tea, the lady said, "I remember when we parted, you were still in swaddling clothes, but now you have grown up so much!" She comforted and encouraged him greatly, and also inquired about the well-being of Lady Xiao and the children. The student replied that they were all well. The lady recounted old stories as if they were happening now, but she did not mention the betrothal made by pointing to the bellies. The student was puzzled by this, so he turned to the old servant Qingshan who had followed him, opened his bag, and handed up his mother's letter. The lady opened the envelope, read it, put it in her sleeve, and said nothing.

    220

    顷间，一童子出，娟娟如琼瑶。夫人命拜生。生答拜。夫人曰： “小儿子也，当教之，乃答礼耶？”复命侍妾秋蟾曰：“召娉娉来。”须臾，边妪领二丫鬟拥一女子从绣幕后冉冉而至，面生前展拜。生逡巡欲起避。夫人曰：“无妨！小女子也。”拜毕，退立于夫人座右。边妪亦侍座于隅。生窃窥娉娉，真倾国色也，虽西施、洛神，未可优劣。生见后，魂神飞越，色动心驰，恐夫人觉之，即起辞出。夫人曰：“先平章视先参政犹骨肉，尊堂亦视老身如娣妹。

    Explanation

    220

    A short while later, a young child emerged, graceful as jade. The lady ordered the child to bow to the man. The man returned the bow. The lady said, "This is a little boy; we should teach him to return the courtesy, but he is too young to understand such formalities." She then instructed her maid, Autumn Moon, to call Pingping. Soon, an elderly woman led two maidservants, escorting a woman who approached slowly and gracefully from behind a screen embroidered with flowers. She bowed before the person in front of her. The man hesitated, wanting to stand up and step back. The lady said, "It's okay! She is just a young lady." After the bow, she stood to the right of the lady's seat. The elderly woman also remained seated at the side. The man secretly glanced at Pingping and was struck by her extraordinary beauty, which even compared to Xi Shi and Luo Shen, it would be hard to say which was more beautiful. His soul and spirit were transported, his heart and eyes were drawn, and fearing that the lady would notice, he immediately stood up and excused himself. The lady said, "The previous Chancellor viewed the previous Censor as family, and your mother also regards me as a sister."

    221

    自二父云亡，两家阔别，鱼沉雁杳，音耗不闻。本谓此生无复再见，岂意余年得睹英妙，老怀喜慰，何可胜言！郎君乃尔寡情耶？”生揖返席，不敢复辞。邢国目娉入，意若使治具然。于时开宴，水陆毕陈。夫人亲酌饮生，生跪受而饮。既而命麟与娉娉更劝迭进。娉酒至，生辞以“乍出远方，久疏曲糵，今不胜杯酌矣。”娉娉捧杯再拜。生欲熟视之，固辞不敢先饮。夫人曰：“郎君年长于汝，自今以后，既是通家，当为兄妹，汝宜跪劝。”娉遂跪。生仓皇遽接，一吸而尽。

    Explanation

    221

    Since the death of my two fathers, the two families have been separated, like fish sinking and geese disappearing, with no news or messages heard. I originally thought we would never see each other again in this life, but who would have thought that in my remaining years I would see such excellence? My old heart is filled with joy and comfort, how can it be fully expressed! Is the young master so unfeeling? The guest bows and returns to his seat, dare not refuse again. Madame Xing looks at Pīng entering, as if she were instructing someone to prepare the feast. At that moment, the feast begins, with all kinds of dishes from both land and sea laid out. The lady-in-waiting personally pours wine for the guest, who kneels to receive and drinks. She then orders Lin and Pīng to take turns pouring wine. When Pīng's wine comes, the guest declines by saying, "I just arrived from afar and have been away from alcohol for a long time, so I cannot handle the wine now." Pīng holds the cup and bows twice. The guest wants to look at her closely but she firmly declines and dares not drink first. Madame Xing says, "You should kneel and pour." Pīng then kneels, and the guest hastily accepts and drinks it all in one go.

    222

    娉娉收杯，至夫人前，沥余酒于案曰：“兄饮未釂，更告一杯可乎？”夫人笑曰：“才为兄妹，便钟友爱之情，郎君岂得戛然乎？”边妪亦从傍更相劝，生乃尽饮。夫人复让边妪曰：“郎君既舍汝家，乃不早以见告，当满进一觥。”妪笑而饮。宴罢，告归。夫人曰：“郎君毋还邸中，只在寒舍安下。”生略辞。夫人曰：“贫家寂寥，愿勿嫌也。”即呼家仆脱欢、小苍头宜童，引生于前堂外东厢房止宿。生入门，但见屏帏床褥，书几盥盆，笔砚琴棋，靡一不备。妪家行李，亦已在焉。

    生既得定居，复遇绝色，且惊且喜，睡不能成，因赋《风入松》一阕，乘醉书于粉壁之上。词云：

    碧城十二瞰湖边，山水更清妍；此邦自古繁华地，风光好，终日歌弦。苏小宅边桃李，坡公堤上人烟。 绮窗罗幕锁婵娟，咫尺远如天。红娘不寄张生信，西厢事，只恐虚传。怎及青铜明镜，铸来便得团圆！

    Explanation

    222

    Píngpíng picked up her cup and went to the lady's presence, pouring the remaining wine onto the table and saying, "My brother has not finished drinking, may I have another cup?" The lady smiled and said, "We have just become siblings, and we already feel affection for each other. How could the young gentleman suddenly stop?" The old woman also encouraged them from the side, and the young man finished his drink. The lady then asked the old woman, "Since the young gentleman has stayed in your home, why did you not inform us earlier? You should have offered him a full cup." The old woman laughed and drank. After the banquet, she said she would return home. The lady said, "The young gentleman should not return to the inn. He can stay at my humble home." The young man slightly declined. The lady said, "My home is poor and quiet, I hope you will not find it distasteful." She immediately called her servants Tuōhuān and Yítóng, who led the young man to a room in the east wing outside the front hall to stay. The young man entered the door and saw screens, curtains, beds, and bedding, writing desks and washbasins, writing brushes, inkstones, zithers, and chess sets—everything was fully prepared. The old woman's belongings were also there.

    The young man had settled down and met a beautiful woman, feeling both surprised and happy, he could not sleep. He composed a poem titled "Wind Enters the Pine" and wrote it on a white wall while drunk. The poem says:

    Twelve green cities overlook the lake's edge, the mountains and waters are even more clear and beautiful. This land has been a place of ancient prosperity, the scenery is good, and there is singing and music all day long. Peach and plum trees by Su Xiaozhi's house, people living by Po Gong's dike. Silk windows and embroidered curtains lock the graceful lady, yet she is as distant as heaven. Hongniang does not send a letter to Zhang Sheng, the story of the western chamber, only fears it is a false tale. How could it compare to the bronze mirror cast, which brings immediate reunion!

    223

    是夕，娉娉返室，亦厚属生，因呼侍女朱樱曰：“魏兄卧否？”樱曰：“弗知也。”娉语之曰：“汝往厢房岩之。”去良久，反命云：“郎君微吟烛下，若有深思，既而取笔，题数行于壁间，妾谛视之，乃《风入松》词也。”娉曰：“汝记忆乎？”樱曰：“已记之矣。”遂口占一过。娉便濡毫，展双鸾霞笺，次其韵，顷刻而就，封缄付樱曰：“明晨汝奉汤与郎君盥面时，以此授之。”樱收于囊。次日黎明，如教而往。生盥沃竟，樱出缄畀生曰：“娉小娘致意郎君，有书奉达。” 生慌忙取视之，乃和生所赋壁间《风入松》，词云：

    玉人家在汉江边，才貌及春妍，天教分付风流态，好才调，会管能弦。文采胸中星斗，词华笔底云烟。 蓝田新锯璧娟娟，日暖绚晴天。广寒宫阙应须到，霓裳曲，一笑亲传。好向嫦娥借问，冰轮怎不教圆？

    Explanation

    223

    That evening, Pinging returned to her room and entrusted the young man with a significant task. She then called her servant girl Zhu Ying and asked, "Is Brother Wei awake?" Zhu Ying replied, "I don't know." Pinging instructed her, "Go to the side room and check." After a long time, Zhu Ying returned and reported, "Young Master Wei is softly reciting under the candlelight, as if deep in thought. He then took up his brush and wrote several lines on the wall. I looked at it carefully and it is a poem titled 'Wind Enters the Pine.'"

    Pinging asked, "Do you remember it?" Zhu Ying replied, "I have remembered it." She then recited the poem once. Pinging then wet her brush, unfolded the double phoenix cloud-patterned paper, followed the rhyme scheme, and composed a poem in a short time. She sealed it and gave it to Zhu Ying, saying, "In the morning, when you serve Young Master Wei his morning tea and he washes his face, give this to him." Zhu Ying put the poem in her bag.

    The next morning at dawn, Zhu Ying followed the instructions. When Young Master Wei had finished washing, Zhu Ying took out the sealed poem and handed it to him, saying, "Miss Pinging has a message for you, there is a letter to deliver." Young Master Wei hastily took and looked at it, and it was a response to his own poem written on the wall titled 'Wind Enters the Pine.' The poem read:

    The jade maiden lives by the Han River, her beauty and talent are as fresh as spring. Heaven has endowed her with a graceful demeanor. She has excellent talent and skill in music. Her literary talent is like stars in her chest, her words flow like clouds and smoke from her pen. The new jade from Lantian shines beautifully, the warm sun brightens the clear sky. She should visit the palace of the moon, she should personally teach the Nirvana dance. It would be good to ask Chang'e, why isn't the ice wheel (moon) made round.

    Translation of the poem:

    As if in a dream, I wander alone,
    The night deep, the moon dim.
    Joy turned to sorrow, heart lost,
    Words unspoken, tears unshed.

    The guqin's melody, soft and clear,
    Yet it could not mend my broken heart.
    The evening passed, the madam woke,
    And I was left to face the cold, empty room.

    In this fleeting moment, I see
    The fragility of love and hope.
    As if in a dream, I drift away,
    Leaving behind the echoes of my heart.

    233

    The Silk of the Dragon Palace

    The silk originally comes from the dragon palace, always in the hands of a beautiful lady. It is reserved for the night of the wedding, when it is used to wipe the fresh blood on the branches of a crabapple tree.

    The good fortune of the handkerchief entering, the man follows closely behind, reaching the pine hall. Peng is leaning against the railing, playing with the new willows in the courtyard, saying, "The green shade is so lush!" She then recites a line from a poem by Xin Qiji: "Do not lean on the dangerous railing, for the setting sun is where the willows and smoke break the heart." The man quickly steps forward, placing his hand on her back and asking, "What is the purpose of breaking one's heart?" Peng is surprised and says, "The madman has come here again?" The man replies, "Is it indeed like this for the madman? Han Shou stole fragrant flowers, Sima Xiangru washed dishes, and the madman acts as such." Peng then orders Fu to bring tea. Fu pretends to drop the handkerchief on the ground, and Peng picks it up and reads the poem on it, becoming angry and saying, "This must be what my brother did, how dare this little girl be so reckless? I will take it to tell my mother." The man apologizes profusely and even kneels down. Peng smiles and puts the handkerchief in her bosom, saying, "Do not say more, let us sit together, enjoy a short moment of happiness, if my mother returns, then it will be too late." The man is greatly delighted and sits down. Peng calls Fu to bring out the delicacies and wine, personally holding a golden lotus cup and pouring wine to encourage the man. The man refuses to drink, but Peng persists in her persuasion. The man thanks her, saying, "Even if I eat a little, I will get drunk, no need for wine." He drinks a few cups, then orders the food and drink to be removed, and Peng complies.

    234

    生乃促席与娉联坐，语娉曰：“我奉命慈亲，为此姻事，艰难水陆，千里远来。今夫人了无一语，道及前盟，必有他谋。事恐中变，命为兄妹，其意可知。子复漠然，路人相视，殊无聊赖。久拟赋归，但以未与子言，故迟迟不决耳。今幸相逢，难期再会，予之心事，子既知之，谐与不谐，明以见告，毋徒使我为周南留滞之客也。”娉闻之，抚髀叹曰：“余岂木石之人哉！兄之此言，岂知我者！妾自遇兄来，忘飧废事，心动神疲，夜寐夙兴，惟君子是念。顾以葑菲，得侍房帷，偕老百年，乃深幸也。第恐天不与人方便，不能善始令终。张珙、申纯，足为明鉴。兄如不弃菅蒯，妾可永执箕帚，毋轻一举，当计万全。”生曰：“若待六礼告成，则予墓草宿矣。子其怜之，毋吝今夕！”娉未及对，而兰苕报夫人回矣。生仓忙趋出。是日，三月丙午也。

    Explanation

    234

    The protagonist drew close to the woman and sat beside her, saying to her, "I have come here on behalf of my kind and loving parents to arrange this marriage. I have traveled a thousand miles, facing great difficulties by land and sea. Now, my lady, you have not spoken a single word about our previous agreement, and I fear you may have other plans. The situation may change, and you may want to be treated as siblings, which is clear in your intentions. You are indifferent and treat me like a stranger, which is quite uninteresting. I have long planned to return home, but I have hesitated because I have not spoken to you. Now, I am fortunate to meet you again, and it is difficult to meet again. My inner thoughts and feelings, you now know, so please clearly inform me whether our relationship will be harmonious or not. Do not just make me a stranded guest in Zhou South." The woman, upon hearing this, patted her thigh and sighed, saying, "Am I made of wood and stone? Your words, brother, do not understand me! Since I met you, I have forgotten my meals and neglected my duties. My heart is moved, and my spirit is tired. I sleep late at night and rise early in the morning, thinking only of the gentleman. Considering myself as a worthless plant, I am fortunate to serve in the inner chamber and live with you for a hundred years. However, I fear that heaven does not grant people convenience, and we may not have a good beginning and a good end. Zhang Gong and Shen Chun are clear examples. If you do not reject me, I can hold the broom forever, and we should not act lightly but plan for a hundred percent success." The protagonist said, "If we wait for the six rites of marriage to be completed, I will be long dead. You should pity me and not be stingy with tonight!" The woman had not yet responded when the servant Lan Tiao reported that the lady had returned. The protagonist hurried out in a fluster. That day was the third month, the day of Bingwu.

    丁未清晨，生入谒，夫人曰：“昨因祭扫，就过湖上诸寺一行，佳景满前，令人应接不暇，所惜者，寓言不在耳。”生唯唯而退。至中堂侧门，与娉相遇，侍妾森然，前遮后拥，彼此注视，莫交一言。生归室闷闷，因诵崔颢《黄鹤楼》诗云：“日暮乡关何处是？烟波江上使人愁！”适娉经窗处，闻之，因穴窗呼生曰： “男儿何怀土之切乎？”生曰：“事属参差，终不能就，处此无益，莫若归去。”娉曰：“少顷，当令福福诣君。”言讫而去。早饭罢，福果来，谓生曰：“娉小娘有简奉君。”生拆而观之，乃诗一首云：

    235

    Early morning of the Ding Wei day, the protagonist entered to pay respects, and the lady said, "Yesterday, due to the tomb-sweeping, I visited several temples by the lake. The scenery was so beautiful that I couldn't take it all in, and what I regretted most was that the person I was waiting for was not here." The protagonist nodded and withdrew. Upon reaching the side door of the central hall, he met Ping, surrounded by her maids, who stood before and behind her, both of them staring at each other without exchanging a word. The protagonist returned to his room feeling dejected and recited a line from Cui Hao's poem "Yellow Crane Tower," saying, "Where is my hometown at dusk? The misty waves on the river make me sad!" Just as Ping passed by the window, she heard him and called out through the window, "Why do men feel so deeply attached to their homeland?" The protagonist replied, "The matter is complicated, and ultimately, I cannot achieve my goal. Staying here is not beneficial; it would be better to return." Ping said, "In a short while, I will send Fu to visit you." After saying this, she left. After breakfast, Fu indeed came and told the protagonist, "Miss Ping has a letter for you." The protagonist opened it and found a poem inside:

    Spring light is fleeting, and there may not be much more of it. Do not let such a fine night pass in vain. Sending words to the gallant scholar, let us make it so that tonight we see Chang'e.

    After finishing, the student was so delighted that he could not restrain himself; he earnestly watched the sun slant westward, eagerly awaiting the arrival of night. Unexpectedly, just before noon, his friend Jin Zai Rong arrived and persuaded him to go to Pingkang. The student refused on the grounds of other matters, but Jin would not allow it, and in the end, he reluctantly went along. Upon arriving, there was a courtesan named Xiu Mei, who understood poetry and verse, and had long admired talented men. Seeing the student’s elegant bearing, she urged him to drink from a large cup, and Jin joined in the loud drinking. The student had no intention of drinking, but being pressed by the two of them, he became heavily drunk and returned home. He spread out a purple silk mat and lay on the ground beside the stone balustrade in front of his room. By the time the evening moon had brightened, his wife was asleep, and Peng took the opportunity to keep their appointment. But she found the student sound asleep, his breath reeking of alcohol. She called to him, but he did not respond. Disheartened, she walked down the steps. She slowly entered the student’s room, took a fine brush, and wrote a quatrain on his silk skirt, then put down the brush and left. The poem read:

    Mist and clouds of dawn and dusk seldom remain in place,
    In vain does the divine maiden descend from Wu’s peak.
    Xiangwang was indeed heartless,
    Drunk and lying in the glow of the moon and flower shadows.

    At the fifth watch, when the sky was bright, the student had also sobered up. He took a step into the shade of the flowers, but saw fallen blossoms on his sleeve and dew wetting his clothes. He recalled the time of his appointment with Peng, and burst into tears. While still brooding in sorrow, a sudden wind blew at his garment hem, and as the hem flipped up, the writing became visible. He raised his eyes and saw it was a seven-character quatrain, written by Peng. Deeply grieved, he lamented the lost opportunity, realizing he had been misled by others and had deeply disappointed Peng. He then cut off the skirt’s hem, mounted it on a scroll, and hung it on the wall. Still following the original rhyme, he composed another poem and sealed it to send to Peng. The poem read:

    In the room, a black lacquered screen bed adorned with mother-of-pearl inlays stood, with a red silk canopy embroidered with gold and various colors. The area in front of the room was quite wide, about one zhang (a traditional Chinese unit of length).     少小惜红芳，文君在绣房。马相如、赋就求凰。此夕偶谐云雨事，桃浪起，湿衣裳。 从此褪蜂黄，芙蓉愁见霜！海誓山盟休忘却，两下里，细思量。自此，往来频数，无夕不欢，虽连理之柯，比翼之鸟，奚以过也。

    Explanation

    241

    In youth, cherishing the red blooms, Zhuo Wenjun dwelled in her boudoir. Sima Xiangru, composing the "Chang'an Fu," sought to win her heart. On that night, their union was consummated, and a metaphorical wave of passion arose, wetting their garments. From then on, her youthful blush faded, and the lotus flower mourned the approach of frost. Do not forget the solemn vows we made, both of us, let's think carefully. From that day forward, our meetings were frequent, and every night was filled with joy, even surpassing the bond of intertwined trees and birds flying together.

    Alas, time passes so quickly, and joy turns to sorrow. As summer wanes and autumn winds begin to blow, suddenly, letters from Lady Xiao and the two brothers arrived, calling the young man back to take the provincial examination. Upon receiving the letter, he was filled with disappointment but did not tell his fiancée. Yet, in his words and actions, he often showed signs of longing. The fiancée noticed, and he could not hide it, so he showed her the letter from his mother, and they both wept. Not many days later, the second brother sent a servant named Hai Xian to deliver a letter to Lady Xingguo, urging the young man to return soon. The lady opened the letter, read it, and called the young man to come, showing him the letter from his mother and saying, "Your wife misses you deeply, and your two brothers are eager for you to return, and you wish to take the autumn examination together, which is truly a beautiful thing in human life. I am reluctant to let you go, but the commands of your mother and brothers cannot be disobeyed. I wish for you to achieve high honors, to be the first to win, and to hear the news of your success, bringing glory to us. The time for returning has not yet come, so please come back when the time is right." She then prepared his luggage and sent him on his way.

    娉时侍夫人座侧，闻知此言，泪落如注，即起入内。其夜，伺夫人睡静，乃潜出别生，相视饮泣。遂谓生曰：“正尔欢娱，乃有远别！天耶人耶！何至此极也！”生曰：“我为母兄所逼，且只暂归，三两月间，再图相见。子第宽心，保摄眠食，勿为无益之悲，徒损倾城之貌。”娉掩涕曰：“兄途中谨慎，早早到家，有便再来，勿为长往。妾丑陋之身，乃兄所有，倘念幺么，不我遐弃，虽死之日，犹生之年。”乃面生再拜曰：“只此别兄，明日不能出矣。”生亦哽咽，目送娉退。次早，娉又遣福福叩门，持手简，送鸦青珝丝成鞋一双，绫袜一緉赠生。简曰：
